玄怪录 - Records of Mysterious Anomalies

    1

    《玄怪录》 唐 牛僧孺
    　　卷一
    　　○杜子春
    　　杜子春者，周、隋间人。少落魄，不事家产，然以心气闲纵，嗜酒邪游。资 产荡尽，投于亲故，皆以不事事之故见弃。方冬，衣破腹空，徒行长安中，日晚 未食，彷徨不知所往，于东市西门，饥寒之色可掬，仰天长吁。有一老人策杖于 前，问曰：“君子何叹？”子春言其心，且愤其亲戚疏薄也。感激之气，发于颜 色。老人曰：“几缗则丰用？”子春曰：“三五万则可以活矣。”老人曰：“未 也，更言之。”“十万。”曰：“未也。”乃言：“百万。”曰：“未也。”曰： “三百万。”乃曰：“可矣。”于是袖出一缗，曰：“给子今夕，明日午时俟子 于西市波斯邸，慎无后期。”及时，子春往，老人果与钱三百万，不告姓名而去。

    Explanation

    1

    The Xuan Guai Lu by Niu Sengru of the Tang Dynasty
    Volume One
    ○ Du Zichun
    Du Zichun was a man from the Zhou and Sui dynasties. In his youth, he was dissolute and neglected his family affairs, yet he had a relaxed and unrestrained temperament, enjoying alcohol and wandering in morally questionable ways. His assets were depleted, and he turned to relatives and friends for help, but they all abandoned him due to his lack of diligence. In the winter, he walked through Chang'an in tattered clothes, empty-handed, and without food, wandering aimlessly and unsure of where to go. At the West Gate of the East Market, his face bore the visible signs of extreme hunger and cold, and he looked up to the sky and sighed deeply. An old man came forward with a walking stick and asked, "Why are you sighing, sir?" Du Zichun explained his situation and expressed his frustration at the indifference of his relatives. His feelings of indignation were evident on his face. The old man asked, "How much would be enough for a comfortable life?" Du Zichun replied, "Thirty to fifty thousand coins would be sufficient." The old man said, "Not enough, tell me more." "One hundred thousand," Du Zichun said. "Not enough," the old man replied. "One million," Du Zichun said. "Not enough," the old man said. "Three million," Du Zichun said. "That will do," the old man replied. He then took out a string of coins from his sleeve and said, "Here is some money for tonight. Meet me at the Persian inn in the West Market tomorrow at noon. Be careful not to be late." When the time came, Du Zichun went to the inn, and the old man indeed gave him three million coins without revealing his name and then left.

    2

    子春既富，荡心复炽。自以为终身不复羁旅也，乘肥衣轻，会酒徒，徵丝竹 歌舞于倡楼，不复以治生为意。一二年间，稍稍而尽。衣服车马，易贵从贱，去 马而驴，去驴而徒，倏忽如初。既而复无计，自叹于市门。发声而老人到，握其 手曰：“君复如此，奇哉！吾将复济子，几缗方可？”子春惭不对，老人因逼之， 子春愧谢而已。老人曰：“明日午时，来前期处。”子春忍愧而往，得钱一千万。 未受之初，愤发以为从此谋生，石季伦、猗顿小竖耳。钱既入手，心又翻然，纵 适之情，又却如故。不三四年间，贫过旧日。

    Explanation

    2

    After becoming wealthy, Zi Chun's desire to indulge in extravagance flared up once more. He believed he would never again be a wanderer, and so he rode in luxurious carriages and wore fine clothes, gathering with drinking companions and hiring musicians and dancers from brothels. He no longer cared about making a living. Within one or two years, his wealth was gradually spent. His clothes and vehicles, once luxurious, became cheap, and he went from riding horses to riding donkeys and then to walking, suddenly returning to his original state. Soon after, he was at a loss again and lamented by the city gate. As soon as he spoke, an old man appeared, grasped his hand and said, "You are back to this, how extraordinary! I will help you again, but how many strings of coins are enough?" Zi Chun was ashamed and could not respond, and the old man pressed him further, to which Zi Chun could only apologize in embarrassment. The old man said, "Come to the same place tomorrow at noon." Reluctantly, Zi Chun went, and received one million coins. At first, he was determined to use the money to make a living, thinking that figures like Shi Chong and Yi Dun were insignificant. However, as soon as the money was in his hands, his heart turned again, and his desire for pleasure returned to its former state. Within three or four years, he was poorer than before.

    3

    复遇老人于故处，子春不胜其愧， 掩面而走，老人牵裾止之，曰：“嗟乎！拙谋也。”因与三千万，曰：“此而不 痊，则子贫在膏肓矣。”子春曰：“吾落魄邪游，生涯罄尽。亲戚豪族，无相顾 者，独此叟三给我，我何以当之？”因谓老人曰“吾得此，人间之事可以立，孤 孀可以衣食，于名教复圆矣。感叟深惠，立事之后，唯叟所使。”老人曰：“吾 心也。子治生毕，来岁中元，见我于老君双桧下。”子春以孤孀多寓淮南，遂转 资扬州，买良田百顷，郭中起甲第，要路置邸百余间，悉召孤孀分居第中，婚嫁 甥侄，迁祔旅榇，恩者煦之，仇者复之。既毕事，及期而往。

    Explanation

    3

    He encountered the old man again at the same place, and Zi Chun could not bear his shame, covering his face and running away. The old man pulled his sleeve to stop him, saying, "Alas! It was a poor plan." Then he gave him three million, saying, "If this does not heal, then you will be poor beyond help." Zi Chun said, "I am a wandering, disreputable person, and my life's resources are exhausted. Neither relatives nor wealthy families care for me. Only this old man has given me three times. How can I repay such kindness?" He then told the old man, "With this, I can establish myself in the world, provide for widows and orphans, and restore my reputation in the teachings. Grateful for the old man's deep kindness, after I have established myself, I will follow your commands." The old man said, "It is my heart. When you have finished managing your affairs, next year during the Zhongyuan Festival, meet me under the two cypress trees of Laojun." Zi Chun, knowing that many widows and orphans lived in Huainan, transferred his resources to Yangzhou, bought a hundred acres of good land, built a grand mansion in the city, and set up over a hundred houses on main roads. He summoned all the widows and orphans and divided them among the houses, married off his nephews and nieces, arranged the burial of the deceased, and treated those who were kind to him with warmth and those who were hostile with forgiveness. After completing all these tasks, he went to meet the old man as agreed.

    4

    老人者方啸于二桧之阴，遂与登华山云台峰。入四十里余，见一居处，室屋 严洁，非常人居。彩云遥覆，鸾鹤飞翔，其上有正堂，中有药炉，高九尺余，紫 焰光发，灼焕窗户。玉女九人环炉而立，青龙白虎，分据前后。其时日将暮，老 人者不复俗衣，乃黄冠绛帔士也。持白石三丸，酒一卮遗子春，令速食之讫。取 一虎皮铺于内西壁，东向而坐，戒曰：“慎勿语，虽尊神、恶鬼、夜叉、猛兽、 地狱，及君之亲属为所囚缚，万苦皆非真实，但当不动不语耳，安心莫惧，终无 所苦。当一心念吾所言。”言讫而去。子春视庭，唯一巨瓮，满中贮水而已。

    Explanation

    4

    The old man was chanting in the shade of two cypress trees, and then he ascended with him to the Yuntai Peak of Mount Hua. After traveling more than forty miles, they came upon a dwelling, the rooms and houses of which were clean and tidy, not inhabited by ordinary people. Colorful clouds covered from afar, and lunatic phoenixes and cranes were flying. Above was a main hall, and in the middle was a furnace, nine feet high, emitting purple flames that shone brightly, illuminating the windows. Nine jade maidens stood around the furnace, and the green dragon and white tiger stood respectively in front and behind. By then, it was evening, and the old man no longer wore secular clothing; instead, he was a scholar with a yellow crown and a red cape. He held three white stones and a cup of wine and gave them to Zichun, instructing him to eat them quickly. He then took a tiger skin and laid it on the west wall inside, facing east, and warned, "Be cautious not to speak. Even revered deities, evil spirits, yakshas, fierce beasts, and hells, and even if your relatives are bound by them, all kinds of suffering are not real. Just remain still and silent. Be at ease and do not fear; ultimately there will be no suffering. Concentrate on what I have said." After speaking, he left. Zichun looked at the courtyard and saw only a large jar, full of water.

    5

    道士适去，而旌旗戈甲，千乘万骑，遍满崖谷来，呵叱之声动天，有一人称 大将军，身长丈余，人马皆着金甲，光芒射人。亲卫数百人，拔剑张弓，直入堂 前，呵曰：“汝是何人，敢不避大将军！”左右竦剑而前，逼问姓名，又问作何 物，皆不对。问者大怒，催斩，争射之，声如雷，竟不应。将军者拗怒而去。俄 而猛虎、毒龙、狻猊、狮子、腹蛇万计，哮吼拿攫而争前，欲搏噬，或跳过其上。 子春神色不动。有顷而散。既而大雨滂澍，雷电晦暝，火轮走其左右，电光掣其 前后，目不得开。须臾，庭际水深丈余，流电吼雷，势若山川开破，不可制止， 瞬息之间，波及坐下。子春端坐不顾。未顷而散。

    Explanation

    5

    The Taoist had just departed when flags, spears, and armor, a thousand chariots and ten thousand horses, filled the ravines and valleys, advancing with shouts and commands that shook the heavens. A man called himself the Great General, over ten feet tall, with both men and horses clad in golden armor, shining brightly. Hundreds of personal guards drew their swords and stringed their bows, entering the hall directly and shouting, "Who are you, and dare you not avoid the Great General!" The attendants drew their swords and advanced, forcing the question of names and what the individual was doing, but all answered not. The questioner grew furious, urging execution and shooting arrows, the sound like thunder, yet still no response. The general left in anger. Soon, thousands of tigers, venomous dragons, lion-like beasts, lions, and vipers roared, snarling, and clawing, rushing forward, wishing to seize and devour, or leaping over them. Zi Chun remained unperturbed. After a while, they dispersed. Then, heavy rain poured down, thunder and lightning darkened the sky, fire wheels moved around them, and lightning flashed before and behind them, blinding their eyes. In an instant, the water in the courtyard was over ten feet deep, flowing lightning and roaring thunder, the force like mountains and rivers being torn apart, unstoppable. In an instant, the waves reached under their feet. Zi Chun sat calmly without looking up. After a short while, it dispersed.

    6

    将军者复来，引牛头狱卒，奇 貌鬼神，将大镬汤而置子春前，长枪刃叉，四面周匝，传命曰：“肯言姓名即放， 不肯言，即当心叉取置之镬中。”又不应。因执其妻来，捽于阶下，指曰：“言 姓名免之。”又不应。乃鞭捶流血，或射或斫，或煮或烧，苦不可忍。其妻号哭 曰：“诚为陋拙，有辱君子。然幸得执巾栉，奉事十余年矣，今为尊鬼所执，不 胜其苦。不敢望君匍匐拜乞，望君一言，即全性命矣。人谁无情，君乃忍惜一言。” 雨泪庭中，且咒且骂，子春终不顾。将军曰：“吾不能毒汝妻耶？”令取锉碓， 从脚寸寸坐刂之。妻叫哭愈急，竟不顾之。将军曰：“此贼妖术已成，不可使久 在世间。”敕左右斩之。

    Explanation

    6

    The general returned, leading a bull-headed jailer with an appearance so bizarre and supernatural that it seemed like a ghost. He placed a large cauldron of boiling water in front of Zi Chun, surrounded by long spears and forks. He commanded, "If you reveal your name, you will be set free. If you refuse, we will impale you and cast you into the cauldron." Zi Chun remained silent. The general then dragged Zi Chun's wife down the steps and pointed at her, saying, "Speak your name to save yourself." Still, she did not respond. The general ordered whips and beatings, causing blood to flow, or shooting and chopping, or boiling and burning, all forms of torture that were unbearable. The wife wept and cried, saying, "Truly, I am unworthy and clumsy, a disgrace to a gentleman. Fortunately, I have served you for many years. Now I am held by a powerful spirit, unable to bear the suffering. I dare not hope that you will crawl and beg, but I hope for a word from you to save my life. Who among people has no feelings? You are willing to spare just one word." She wept tears in the courtyard, cursing and scolding, but Zi Chun remained unmoved. The general said, "I cannot harm your wife?" and ordered to fetch a millstone, cutting her from the feet upwards. She cried more desperately. The general said, "This demon's magic is complete. Cannot allow him to stay in the world for long," and ordered the attendants to behead him.

    7

    斩讫，魂魄被领见阎罗王，王曰：“此乃云台峰妖民乎？”促付狱中，于是 熔铜、铁杖、碓捣、硙磨、火坑、镬汤、刀山、剑林之苦，无不备尝。然心念道 士之言，亦似可忍，竟不呻吟。狱卒告受罪毕，王曰：“此人阴贼，不合得作男 身，宜令作女人。”配生宋州单父县丞王勤家，生而多病，针灸医药之苦，略无 停日。亦尝坠火堕床，痛苦不济，终不失声。俄而长大，容色绝代，而口无声， 其家目为哑女，亲戚相狎，侮之万端，终不能对。

    Explanation

    7

    After the execution, the soul was led to the King of Hell, who asked, "Is this the evil person from Yuntai Peak?" The soul was then sent to prison, where it endured all manner of tortures: molten copper, iron rods, pestles and mortars, fire pits, boiling cauldrons, knife mountains, and sword forests. Despite these torments, the soul remembered the words of the Taoist and found them somewhat bearable, never groaning even once. When the jailer reported that the soul had finished its punishment, the King of Hell said, "This person is evil and treacherous; it is not fitting for them to be reborn as a man. Let them be reborn as a woman." The soul was reborn into the family of Wang Qin, the county magistrate of Shanfu, Song Prefecture. She was born with many illnesses, enduring the pain of acupuncture and medicine without respite. She also fell into fires and fell off beds, suffering greatly but never crying out. As she grew up, she was beautiful beyond compare, yet she remained mute. Her family called her a deaf-mute girl, and relatives and friends mocked and teased her in countless ways, but she could not respond.

    8

    同乡有进士卢珪者，闻者容而 慕之，因媒氏求焉。其家以哑辞之，卢曰：“苟为妻而贤，何用言矣，亦足以戒 长舌之妇。”乃许之。卢生备礼亲迎为妻，数年，恩情甚笃，生一男，仅二岁， 聪慧无敌。卢抱儿与之言，不应。多方引之，终无辞。卢大怒曰：“昔贾大夫之 妻鄙其夫才不笑尔。然观其射雉，尚释其憾。今吾陋不及贾，而文艺非徒射雉也， 而竟不言。大丈夫为妻所鄙，安用其子！”乃持两足，以头扑于石上，应手而卒， 血溅数步。子春爱生于心，忽忘其约，不觉失声云：“噫！”

    Explanation

    8

    A Fellow Village Scholar Named Lu Gui

    There was a scholar named Lu Gui from the same village who, upon hearing of her beauty and virtue, admired her greatly and sought her hand through a matchmaker. Her family declined because she was mute. Lu said, "If she is a good wife, why does it matter if she cannot speak? It is also sufficient to warn against the gossipy women." Thus, he accepted her. Lu prepared the necessary rituals and married her. After several years, they were deeply affectionate, and she gave birth to a son who was only two years old but incredibly intelligent. When Lu held the child and spoke to him, the child did not respond. Despite many attempts to engage him, the child remained silent. Enraged, Lu said, "In the past, the wife of Duke Jia despised her husband because he lacked wit. However, when she saw him shoot pheasants, she still let go of her resentment. Now, I am inferior to Duke Jia, and my literary and artistic talents are not just for shooting pheasants, yet he remains silent. A man who is despised by his wife, what use is his son?" He then grabbed the child's feet and struck his head against a rock, killing him instantly. Blood splattered several steps. Zi Chun, filled with love for the child, forgot his vow and unconsciously exclaimed, "Ah!"

    9

    “噫”声未息，身坐故处，道士者亦在其前，初五更矣。其紫焰穿屋上天， 火起四舍，屋室俱焚。道士叹曰：“措大误余乃如是！”因提其髻投水瓮中。未 顷火息。道士前曰：“出。吾子之心，喜怒哀惧恶欲，皆能忘也。所未臻者，爱 而已。向使子无‘噫’声，吾之药成，子亦上仙矣。嗟乎，仙才之难得也！吾药 可重炼，而子之身犹为世界所容矣。勉之哉！”遥指路使归。子春强登基观焉， 其炉已坏，中有铁柱大如臂，长数尺。道士脱衣，以刀子削之。
    　　子春既归，愧其忘誓，复自效以谢其过，行至云台峰，绝无人迹，叹恨而归。

    Explanation

    9

    Ah! The sound had not yet died down when the person sat in the same place, and the Taoist priest was also in front of him. It was the fifth watch of the night. The purple flame shot through the house and into the sky, and a fire broke out in all four quarters, burning down all the houses and rooms. The Taoist priest sighed and said, "You scholar have caused me so much trouble!" He then pulled the person's hair and threw him into a water jar. Soon the fire was extinguished. The Taoist priest stepped forward and said, "Come out. Your heart, free from joy, anger, sorrow, fear, and desire, can all be forgotten. The only thing that has not been achieved is love. If you had not made that 'Ah!' sound, my medicine would have been successful, and you would have become an immortal. Alas, it is difficult to find someone with the talent to become an immortal! My medicine can be refined again, and your body is still part of the world. Be diligent!" He pointed to the road to send the person back. Zi Chun forced his way up to look, and the furnace was already ruined, with an iron pillar as thick as an arm and several feet long inside. The Taoist priest took off his clothes and used a knife to shave it.

    Zi Chun returned home, feeling ashamed for breaking his vow, and tried to make amends for his mistake. He walked to Yun Tai Peak, where there were no human tracks, and returned home in regret.

    10

    ○裴谌
    　　裴谌、王敬伯、梁芳约为方外之友。隋大业中，相与入白鹿山学道，谓黄白 可成，不死之药可致，云飞羽化，无非积学。辛勤采炼，手足胼胝，十数年间。 无何，梁芳死，敬伯谓谌曰：“吾所以去国忘家，耳绝丝竹，口厌肥豢，目弃奇 色，去华屋而乐茅斋，贱欢娱而贵寂寞者，岂非觊乘云驾鹤，游戏蓬壶？纵其不 成，亦望长生，寿毕天地耳。今仙海无涯，长生未致，辛勤于云山之外，不免就 死。敬伯所乐，将下山乘肥衣轻，听歌玩色，游于京洛，意足然后求达，垂功立 事，以荣耀人寰，纵不能憩三山，饮瑶池，骖龙衣霞，歌鸾飞凤，与仙翁为侣， 且腰金拖紫，图影凌烟，厕卿大夫之间，何如哉？子盍归乎？无空死深山。”谌 曰；“吾乃梦醒者，不复低迷。”敬伯遂归，谌留之不得。时唐贞观初，以旧籍 调授左武卫骑曹参军，大将军赵朏妻之以女。数年间，迁大理廷评，衣绯，奉使 淮南，舟行过高邮。

    Explanation

    10

    Pei Chen, Wang Jingbo, and Liang Fang were friends who sought to transcend conventional social and moral norms. During the era of Emperor Yang of Sui, they entered the White Deer Mountain together to practice Daoism, believing that gold and silver could be transmuted, the elixir of immortality could be attained, and that spiritual transformation and ascension to heaven were possible through diligent study. They worked tirelessly, their hands and feet covered in calluses, for more than a decade. Soon, Liang Fang died, and Wang Jingbo said to Pei Chen, "I have forsaken my country and family, cut myself off from music, grown tired of rich food, abandoned beautiful colors, left grand houses for a humble hut, and valued solitude over pleasure. Is it not to hope to ride clouds and ride on cranes, to play in the mythical Isles of the Immortals? Even if I do not achieve immortality, I still hope for long life, to live as long as the heavens and earth. Now, the sea of immortality is boundless, and I have not yet attained eternal life. My hard work in the mountains has not saved me from death. What I enjoy is to descend from the mountains, ride in fine vehicles and wear light clothing, listen to songs and admire beautiful women, travel to Luoyang, and only then seek to achieve something, to establish accomplishments and leave a legacy, to honor the human world. Even if I cannot rest in the Three Mountains, drink from the Jade Pool, ride dragons and wear clouds, sing with phoenixes and fly with cranes, and be companions with immortals, I can still wear gold and purple, have my image inscribed on the Hall of Heroic Deeds, and mingle with the ranks of high officials. What do you think? Why don't you return? Don't die in vain in the mountains." Pei Chen replied, "I am now awake from my dream; I will not be disheartened again." Wang Jingbo then returned, but Pei Chen could not persuade him to stay. At the beginning of the Zhenguan era of the Tang dynasty, Wang Jingbo was appointed as a Left Guard Cavalry Officer based on his previous credentials, and the general Zhao Fei married him to his daughter. Over the next few years, Wang Jingbo was promoted to a judge in the Supreme Court, wore red robes, and was sent as an envoy to Huainan, where he sailed past Gaoyou.

    11

    制使之行，呵叱风生，行船不敢动。时天微雨，忽有一渔舟突过，中有老人， 衣蓑戴笠，鼓棹而去，其疾如风。敬伯以为吾乃制使，威振远近，此渔父敢突过 我。试视之，乃谌也。遽令追之，因请维舟，延之坐内，握手慰之曰：“兄久居 深山，抛掷名宦而无成，到此极也。夫风不可系，影不可捕，古人倦夜长，尚秉 烛游，况少年白昼而掷之乎？敬伯自出山数年，今廷尉评事矣。昨者推狱平允， 乃天锡命服。

    Explanation

    11

    The envoy's journey was marked by his commanding presence, with shouts and commands like a gust of wind, causing boats to dare not move. It was slightly raining at the time. Suddenly, a fishing boat passed through, with an elderly man inside, dressed in a straw cloak and hat, rowing his boat away swiftly, like the wind. Jingbo thought he was the envoy, with his authority resonating far and wide, and wondered how this fisherman dared to pass him by. He looked at him, and it was Chen. He immediately ordered to follow him, and then asked him to tie his boat, inviting him to sit inside. He grasped his hand and comforted him, saying, "Brother, you have been living deep in the mountains for a long time, abandoning officialdom without achieving anything, reaching this extreme. The wind cannot be tied, the shadow cannot be caught. Ancient people, tired of long nights, still held candles to play. How much more so for young people to throw away their daytime?" Jingbo has been out of the mountains for several years, and now he is an official in the Imperial Censorate. Yesterday, when he adjudicated a case fairly, it was a gift from heaven to be appointed.

    12

    淮南疑狱，今氵献于有司，上择详明吏覆讯之，敬伯预其选，故有 是行。虽未可言官达，比之山叟，自谓差胜。兄甘劳苦，竟如曩日，奇哉！奇哉！ 今何所须，当以奉给。”谌曰：“吾侪野人，心近云鹤，未可以腐鼠吓也。吾沉 子浮，鱼鸟各适，何必矜炫也。夫人世之所须者，吾当给尔，子何以赠我？吾与 山中之友，或市药于广陵，亦有息肩之地。青园桥东，有数里樱桃园，园北车门， 即吾宅也。子公事少隙，当寻我于此。”遂倏然而去。

    Explanation

    12

    A Case of Doubt in Huainan

    A case of doubt in Huainan was presented to the authorities, and the emperor selected thorough and clear officials to re-examine it. Jinglei was chosen for this task, hence his journey. Although he did not reach high office, compared to a mountain hermit, he considered himself slightly better. His brother willingly endured hard work, still as before, how remarkable! How remarkable! What do you need now, I will provide it. Chen replied, "We rustic people, our hearts are close to the clouds and cranes, cannot be frightened by something as insignificant as a rotten mouse. I sink, you float, fish and birds each find their own place, why must you boast or show off? What the world needs, I will provide for you, what can you give me? I with my friends in the mountains, sometimes buy medicine in Guangling, also have a place to rest one's burden. East of Qingyuan Bridge, there is a cherry orchard several miles long, the carriage gate north of the garden, is my house. If you have a little free time from your official duties, you should find me here." Then he suddenly left.

    13

    敬伯到广陵十余日，事少闲，思谌言，因出寻之。果有车门，试问之，乃裴 宅也。人引以入，初尚荒凉，移步愈佳。行数百步，方及大门，楼阁重复，花木 鲜秀，似非人境。烟翠葱茏，景色妍媚，不可形状。香风飒来，神清气爽，飘飘 然有凌云之意，不复以使车为重，视其身若腐鼠，视其徒若蝼蚁。既而稍闻剑佩 之声，二青衣出曰：“阿郎来。”俄有一人，衣冠伟然，仪貌奇丽，敬伯前拜， 视之乃谌也。裴慰之曰：“尘界仕官，久食腥膻，愁欲之火焰于心中，负之而行， 固甚劳困。”遂揖以入，坐于中堂，窗户栋梁，饰以录宝，屏帐皆画云鹤。有顷， 四青衣捧碧玉台盘而至，器物珍异，皆非人世所有，香醪嘉馔，目所未窥。既而 日将暮，命其促席，燃九光之灯，光华满座。女乐二十人，皆绝代之色，列坐其 前。

    Explanation

    13

    Jingbo arrived in Guangling for more than ten days, with few affairs and leisure. Thinking of Chen's words, he went out to look for him. Indeed, there was a carriage door. He tried to ask about it, and it turned out to be Pei's residence. People led him in. At first, it was still desolate, but as he moved further, it became better. After walking several hundred steps, he finally reached the main gate. Towers and pavilions were repeated, and flowers and trees were fresh and beautiful, seeming not of this world. Smoke and greenery were lush, and the scenery was beautiful and charming, beyond description. A fragrant wind came swiftly, refreshing his spirit and clearing his mind. He felt light and airy as if he could touch the clouds, no longer considering his carriage important, seeing himself as a rotten mouse and his followers as ants. Soon, he heard the sound of swords and belts. Two young men came out and said, "Master is coming." Soon, there was a person, wearing splendid attire, with extraordinary beauty and grace. Jingbo bowed before him, and he saw that it was Chen. Pei comforted him, saying, "Officials of the mundane world, long accustomed to the stench of meat, the flames of desire and sorrow burned in their hearts, carrying it with them, indeed very tiring and exhausting." He then invited him in and sat in the main hall. Windows, doors, and beams were decorated with precious materials, and screens and curtains were all painted with clouds and cranes. After a while, four young men carried a jade table and plate, with precious and rare utensils, all not found in the mundane world. Fragrant wine and delicious food, things never seen before. Soon, the day was ending, and he ordered the seating to be moved closer, lighting lamps with nine lights, the light filling the room. Twenty female musicians, all of extraordinary beauty, sat in front of him.

    14

    裴顾小黄头曰：“王评事昔吾山中之友，道情不固，弃吾下山，别近十年， 才为廷尉属。今俗心已就，须俗妓以乐之。顾伶家女无足召者，当召士大夫之女 已适人者。如近无姝丽，五千里内皆可择之。”小黄头唯唯而去。诸妓调碧玉筝， 调未谐而黄头已复命，引一妓自西阶登，拜裴席前。裴指曰：“参评事。”敬伯 答拜，细视之，乃敬伯妻赵氏也。敬伯惊讶不敢言，妻亦甚骇，目之不已。遂令 坐玉阶下，一青衣捧玳瑁筝授之，赵素所善也，因令与妓合曲以送酒。

    Explanation

    14

    Pei Gu called to the small yellow-haired servant and said, "Mr. Wang, who was once my friend in the mountains, had not held firm to the Dao, abandoned me and went down the mountain. We have not seen each other for nearly ten years, and only recently became an associate of the Chief Justice. Now his worldly desires have settled, and he needs secular courtesans to entertain him. But among the courtesans, there is no one worth summoning; we should summon the daughters of scholars and officials who have already been married. If there is no beauty nearby, one may choose from anywhere within five thousand li." The small yellow-haired servant replied with a polite nod and left.

    The courtesans began tuning the jade-green zither, but before the tuning was complete, the yellow-haired servant returned with a message, leading a courtesan up from the western steps and bowing before Pei’s seat. Pei pointed and said, "Respectful Sir." Jingbo returned the bow, then looked closely at her and realized she was his wife, Zhao. Jingbo was stunned and could not speak, and his wife was also greatly shocked, unable to stop looking at her. Pei then ordered her to sit on the jade steps, and a servant in green clothing presented her with a tortoiseshell zither, which Zhao had always been skilled at playing. He then ordered her to play a duet with the courtesan to accompany the wine.

    15

    敬伯坐间 取一殷色朱李投之，赵顾敬伯，潜系于衣带。妓奏之曲，赵皆不能逐。裴乃令随 赵所奏，时时停之，以呈其曲。其歌舞虽非云韶九奏之乐，而清沉宛转，酬献极 欢。天将晓，裴召前黄头曰：“送赵氏夫人。”且谓曰：“此堂乃九天画堂，常 人不到。吾昔与王为方外之交，怜其为俗所迷，自投汤火，以智自烧，以明自贼， 将沉浮于生死海中，求岸不得，故命于此，一以醒之。今日之会，诚难再得，亦 夫人之宿命，乃得暂游，云山万重，往复劳苦，无辞也。”赵拜而去。

    Explanation

    15

    During the gathering, Jinger took a dark red plum and threw it to Zhao, who glanced at Jinger and secretly tied it to his belt. The courtesans played music, but Zhao could not keep up with the melody. Pei then instructed the musicians to pause at the moments Zhao played, highlighting his performance. Although the music and dance were not the divine music of the Ninefold Chimes, they were still clear, deep, and graceful, bringing great joy to the audience. As dawn approached, Pei summoned a servant and said, "Escort Lady Zhao." He also addressed her, saying, "This hall is the Nine Heavens' Painted Hall, a place rarely visited by ordinary people. In the past, I had a spiritual friendship with Wang, who was lost in worldly concerns, throwing himself into danger, burning himself with wisdom, and destroying himself with clarity, caught in the cycle of birth and death, unable to find a shore. I arranged for him to come here to wake him up. Today's gathering is truly a rare opportunity, also part of your predestined fate, allowing you to briefly visit, facing countless mountains and hardships, with no regrets." Zhao bowed and departed.

    16

    裴谓敬伯曰：“评公使车留此一宿，得无惊群将乎？宜且就馆，未赴阙闲时， 访我可也。尘路遐远，万愁攻人，努力自爱。”敬伯拜谢而去。后五日，将还， 潜诣取别，其门不复有宅，乃荒凉之地，烟草极目，惆怅而返。
    　　及京奏事毕，得归私第，诸赵竞怒曰：“女子诚陋拙，不足以奉事君子。然 已辱厚礼，亦宜敬之。夫上以承祖先，下以继后事，岂苟而已哉。奈何以妖术致 之万里而娱人之视听乎？朱李尚在，其筵足徵，何讳乎？”敬伯尽言之，且曰： “当此之时，敬伯亦自不测。此盖裴之道成矣，以此相炫也。”其妻亦记得裴言， 遂不复责。

    16

    Pei told Jingbo, "If the envoy's carriage stays here for one night, would it not disturb the troops? It is best to temporarily stay in the guesthouse, and you may visit me before the time of reporting to the imperial court. The dusty road is far away, and a thousand worries assail one; take care of yourself." Jingbo bowed and thanked him before departing. Five days later, as he was about to return, he secretly went to bid farewell. The door no longer had a house; it had become a desolate place, with grass and tobacco plants stretching to the horizon. He returned with a sense of sadness and longing.

    After finishing the report in the capital and returning to his private residence, the various Zhao angrily said, "The woman is indeed ugly and clumsy, not fit to serve a gentleman. Yet, having already received great respect, it is also proper to respect her. To honor the ancestors above and continue the affairs of the future below, how could it be just a casual matter? How could one use magic to bring her from afar to entertain people? The red and black (colors) are still there; the banquet is sufficient proof. Why hide it?" Jingbo spoke everything, and added, "At that time, Jingbo was also uncertain. This is because Pei's method has succeeded; he is showing off with this." His wife also remembered Pei's words and did not rebuke him further.

    17

    吁！神仙之变化，诚如此乎？将幻者鬻术以致惑乎？固非常智之所及。且夫 雀为蛤，雉为蜃，人为虎，腐草为萤，蜣螂为蝉，鲲为鹏，万物之变化，书传之 记者，不可以智达，况耳目之外乎！
    　　○韦氏
    　　京兆韦氏女者，既笄二年，母告之曰：“有秀才裴爽者，欲聘汝。”女笑曰： “非吾夫也。”母记之，虽媒媪日来，盛陈裴之才，其家甚慕之，然终不谐。又 一年，母曰：“有王悟者，前参京兆军事，其府之司录张审约者，汝之老舅也， 为王媒之，将聘汝矣。”女亦曰：“非也。”母又曰：“张亦熟我，又为王之媒 介也，其辞不虚矣。”亦终不谐。

    Explanation

    17

    Oh! The transformations of immortals, are they truly like this? Or is it that the deceiver sells his tricks to cause confusion? It is certainly beyond the reach of ordinary wisdom. Let alone the transformations of sparrows into clams, pheasants into sea dragons, people into tigers, decaying grass into fireflies, beetles into cicadas, and the giant fish into the giant bird. The transformations of all things, as recorded in books and traditions, cannot be understood by intelligence, how much more so beyond what we can see and hear!

    The daughter of the Wei family of Jingzhao, two years after she reached the age of marriage, her mother told her: "There is a scholar named Pei Shuang who wishes to marry you." The girl laughed and said: "He is not my husband." Her mother remembered this, even though matchmakers came every day, greatly praising Pei's talents, his family greatly admired her, but it still did not work out. Another year later, her mother said: "There is a man named Wang Wu, who previously served in the military of Jingzhao. His recorder, Zhang Shenyue, is your uncle, and he is the matchmaker for Wang. He will marry you." The girl also said: "No." Her mother then said: "Zhang also knows me well, and he is the matchmaker for Wang. His words are not false." But it still did not work out.

    18

    又二年，进士张楚金求之。母以告之，女笑曰：“吾之夫乃此人也。”母许 之，遂择吉焉。既成礼讫，因其母徐问之，对曰：“吾此乃梦徵矣。然此生之事 皆见矣，岂独适楚金之先知乎！某既笄，梦年二十适清河楚金，以尚书节制广陵， 在镇七年，而楚金伏法。阖门皆死，惟某与新妇一人，生入掖庭，蔬食而役者十 八年，蒙诏放出。自午承命，日暮方出宫关，与新妇渡水，迨暗及滩，四顾将昏 然，不知所往，因与新妇相于滩于掩泣，相勉曰：‘此不可久立，宜速渡。’遂 南行。及岸数百步，有坏坊焉。

    18

    After another two years, the Jinshi Zhang Chujin sought her. His mother told him about it, and the woman smiled and said, "My husband is this person." His mother agreed, and he then chose an auspicious date. After the ceremony was completed, he gently asked his mother, and she replied, "This is a sign from my dream. However, all the events of this life were seen, how could it be only the knowledge of being married to Zhang Chujin first? I had already reached the age of笄 (a coming-of-age ceremony for girls), and in my dream, I was twenty years old and married to Zhang Chujin of Qinghe. As a Shangshu (Minister of State) controlling Guangling, he governed for seven years, and then Zhang Chujin was executed. The entire family died, only I and the new bride survived, and we survived and entered the imperial harem, where we served for eighteen years, eating vegetarian food. We received an imperial decree to be released. From noon when I received the order, it was evening when I left the palace gates, and together with the new bride, we crossed the water. When it became dark and we reached the shoal, looking around, it was already dusk, and we did not know where to go. So we wept together on the shoal, encouraging each other, 'We cannot stay here for long, we should cross quickly.' We then went south. After walking several hundred steps to the shore, there was a ruined building there.

    19

    自入西门，随垣而北，其东大门屋，因造焉，又 无人而大开，遂入。及坏戟门，亦开，又入。逾屏回廊四合，有堂既扃。阶前有 四大樱桃树林，花发正茂。及月色满庭，似无人居，不知所告。因与新妇对卧阶 下。未几，有老人来诟逐，告以前情，遂去。又闻西廊步必履之声，有一少年郎 来诟，且呼老人令遂之。苦告之，少年郎低首而走。徐乃白衫素履，哭拜阶下曰： ‘某尚书之侄也。’乃恸哭曰：‘无处问耗，不知阿母与阿嫂至，乃自天降也。 此即旧宅，堂中所锁，无非旧物。’恸哭开户，宛如故居之地，居之九年前从化 （本句疑有脱误）。”其母大奇之。且人之荣悴，无非前定，素闻之矣，岂梦中 之信，又如此乎？乃心记之。

    19

    Entering from the western gate, he followed the wall to the north. The eastern main gate, which was constructed there, was wide open and unoccupied, so he entered. When he reached the broken gate of the halberd, it was also open, and he entered again. Crossing the screen and the four-sided corridor, he found a hall that was already locked. In front of the steps, there were four large cherry tree groves, and the flowers were in full bloom. When the moonlight filled the courtyard, it seemed as if no one lived there, and he did not know what to report. So he lay down with his new wife at the base of the steps. Not long after, an old man came to scold and chase them away, and he told him of the previous situation before leaving. Then he heard the sound of footsteps and shoes in the western corridor, and a young man came to scold, calling out to the old man to follow. He pleaded with him, and the young man lowered his head and walked away.     　　○元无有
    　　宝应中，有元无有，尝以仲春末独行维扬郊野。值日晚，风雨大至。时兵荒 后，人户逃窜，入路旁空庄。须臾霁止。斜月自出。无有憩北轩，忽闻西廊有人 行声，未几至堂中。有四人，衣冠皆异，相与谈谐，吟咏甚畅，乃云：“今夕如 秋，风月如此，吾党岂不为文，以纪平生之事？”其文即曰口号联句也。吟咏既 朗，无有听之甚悉。其一衣冠长人曰：

    Shortly afterward, Chu Jin was granted command in Guangling. During the Shénlóng era, Xu Jingye was implicated in a plot to restore the throne and was executed by collective punishment, with only his wife and female relatives spared from death, though they were sentenced to serve in the Yechting for eighteen years.     ○ Yuan Wu You

    During the Bǎoyìng era, there was a man named Yuan Wu You, who once, at the end of the second lunar month, walked alone in the outskirts of Weiyang. It was late in the day when a sudden downpour began. At that time, it had been after a period of war and famine, and people had fled their homes. He entered an empty farmhouse by the roadside. Soon the rain ceased, and a slanted moon appeared. Yuan Wu You rested in the northern pavilion when he suddenly heard footsteps in the western corridor. Shortly afterward, four figures entered the hall. They all wore unusual clothing and engaged in lively conversation and recitation. One of them said, “Tonight is like autumn, with such a fine wind and moon—should our group not compose a poem to record our life’s experiences?” Their composition was a haokou lianju (a form of collective verse). As they recited, Yuan Wu You listened intently. One of the tall men, dressed in unusual attire, said:

    21

    “齐纨鲁缟如霜雪，寥亮高声为子发。”
    　　其二黑衣冠短陋人曰：
    　　“嘉宾良会清夜时，辉煌灯烛我能持。”

    　　“清冷之泉俟朝汲，桑绠相牵常出入。”
    　　其四黑衣冠，身亦短陋，诗曰：
    　　“爨薪贮水常煎熬，充他口腹我为劳。”

    　　○郭代公
    　　代国公郭元振，开元中下第，自晋之汾，夜行阴晦失道。久而绝远有灯火之 光，以为人居也，迳往投之。八九里有宅，门宇甚峻。既入门，廊下及堂下灯烛 辉煌，牢馔罗列，若嫁女之家，而悄无人。公系马西廊前，历阶而升，徘徊堂上， 不知其何处也。俄闻堂中东阁有女子哭声，呜咽不已。

    The fine silk from Qi and Lu is as pure as frost and snow, and a clear and resonant voice is raised for you.

    "At a gathering of distinguished guests during a clear night, I can manage brilliant lamps and candles."

    The third person, dressed in an old yellow robe and also short and unremarkable, recited:
    "A cool and clear spring waits to be drawn in the morning, with a mulberry rope frequently being used to draw water."

    "I burn firewood to store water and frequently boil it, laboring to fill others' stomachs."

They praised each other, envying their self-pride, even though Ruan Ji's "Elegies" could not surpass it. The four people returned to their old place late in the morning, and the host searched for them, finding only an old pestle, candle holder, water bucket, and broken pot in the hall. Thus, it was known that the four people were these objects.

    ○ Duke Guo
    Duke Guo Yuanzhen, during the reign of Emperor Xuanzong of Tang, failed the imperial examination and traveled from Jin to Fen. He was walking at night in the dark and lost his way. After a long time, he saw a distant light of lamps, thinking it was a human dwelling, and went straight to it. After eight or nine miles, he reached a mansion with a very imposing gate. After entering, the corridors and hall were brightly lit with lamps and candles, and the food was arranged as if it were a wedding feast, yet there was no one around. The duke tied his horse in front of the western corridor, climbed the steps, and wandered around in the hall, not knowing where he was. Soon, he heard the sound of a woman crying in the east pavilion, sobbing endlessly.

    22

    公问曰：“堂中泣者，人 耶，鬼耶？何陈设如此，无人而独泣？”曰：“妾此乡之祠有乌将军者，能祸福 人，每岁求偶于乡人，乡人必择处女之美者而嫁焉。妾虽陋拙，父利乡人之五百 缗，潜以应选。今夕，乡人之女并为游宴者，到是，醉妾此室，共锁而去，以适 于将军者也。今父母弃之就死，而令惴惴哀惧。君诚人耶，能相救免，毕身为扫 除之妇，以奉指使。”公愤曰：“其来当何时？”曰：“二更。”公曰：“吾忝 为大丈夫也，必力救之。如不得，当杀身以徇汝，终不使汝枉死于淫鬼之手也。” 女泣少止，于是坐于西阶上，移其马于堂北，令一仆侍立于前，若为宾而待之。

    Explanation

    22

    The gentleman asked, "Who is weeping in the hall? Is it a human or a ghost? Why is it set up like this, with no one here but she is weeping alone?" She replied, "In this village's shrine, there is a deity known as the Black General, who can bring misfortune or blessings to people. Every year, he seeks a spouse from the villagers, and the villagers must choose the most beautiful unmarried girls and marry them. Although I am ugly and clumsy, my father profited from the villagers' offer of five hundred strings of cash and secretly agreed to my being chosen. Tonight, the villagers' daughters, who were all participating in a feast, came to this room, got me drunk, locked me up, and left to take me to the Black General. Now, my parents have abandoned me to die, and I am filled with fear and grief. If you are truly a human, can you save me? I will serve as a cleaning woman for the rest of my life and obey your commands." The gentleman angrily said, "When will he come?" She replied, "At the second watch." He said, "I am unworthy to be a man of virtue, but I will do my utmost to save you. If I fail, I will kill myself to save you, and I will never let you die in vain at the hands of a lustful ghost." The woman's weeping stopped a little. Then, he sat on the western steps, moved his horse to the north of the hall, and had a servant stand in front of him, treating him as a guest.

    23

    未几，火光照耀，车马骈阗，二紫衣吏入而复出，曰：“相公在此。”逡巡， 二黄衣吏入而出，亦曰：“相公在此。”公私心独喜：“吾当为宰相，必胜此鬼 矣。”既而将军渐下，导吏复告之。将军曰：“入。”有戈剑弓矢翼引以入，即 东阶下，公使仆前曰：“郭秀才见。”遂行揖。将军曰：“秀才安得到此？”曰： “闻将军今夕嘉礼，愿为小相耳。”将军者喜而延坐，与对食，言笑极欢。公于 囊中有利刀，思取刺之，乃问曰：“将军曾食鹿腊乎？”曰：“此地难遇。

    Explanation

    23

    Shortly thereafter, the light of the fire shone brightly, and carriages and horses were crowded together. Two officials in purple robes entered and then exited, saying, "The prime minister is here." Hesitantly, two officials in yellow robes entered and then exited, also saying, "The prime minister is here." The scholar secretly delighted, thinking, "I shall become the prime minister and will surely overcome this ghost." Soon after, the general gradually descended, and the guide officials reported to him again. The general said, "Enter." With spears, swords, bows, and arrows as accompaniment, the scholar then bowed and said, "Deacon Guo is here." He proceeded to pay his respects. The general asked, "How did you come to be here?" The scholar replied, "I heard that you are having a joyous occasion tonight and merely wish to be a minor official." The general was pleased and invited him to sit, and they ate together, speaking and laughing very joyfully. The scholar had a sharp knife in his bag and thought to kill him, so he asked, "Have you ever eaten deer jerky?" The general replied, "It is hard to find here."

    24

    ”公 曰：“某有少须珍者，得自御厨，愿削以献。”将军者大悦。公乃起，取鹿腊并 小刀，因削之，置一小器，令自取。将军喜，引手取之，不疑其他。公伺其无机， 乃投其脯，捉其腕而断之。将军失声而走，导从之吏，一时惊散。公执其手，脱 衣缠之，令仆夫出望之，寂无所见，乃启门谓泣者曰：“将军之腕已在于此矣。 寻其血踪，死亦不久。汝既获免，可出就食。”泣者乃出，年可十七八，而甚佳 丽，拜于公前，曰：“誓为仆妾。”公勉谕焉。天方曙，开视其手，则猪蹄也。

    Explanation

    24

    The official said, "I have something rare and precious, obtained from the imperial kitchen, and I wish to carve and present it." The general was very pleased. The official then rose, took the deer jerky and a small knife, carved it, placed it in a small container, and allowed the general to take it himself. The general was pleased and reached out to take it, with no suspicion of any other intention. The official waited for the right moment, then threw the jerky, grabbed the general's wrist, and broke it. The general cried out and ran away, and the officials accompanying him were suddenly scattered in alarm. The official held his hand, removed his clothes, and wrapped them around it. He ordered the driver to look outside, but saw nothing. He then opened the door and said to the weeping person, "The general's wrist is now here. Following the blood trail, death will not be far off. Since you have been spared, you may go out to eat." The weeping person then came out, about seventeen or eighteen years old, and very beautiful. She knelt before the official and said, "I swear to be your servant and concubine." The official encouraged and advised her. It was just dawn, and when he opened his hand, it was a pig's paw.

    25

    俄闻哭泣之声渐近，乃女之父母兄弟及乡中耆老，相与舁榇而来，将收其尸 以备殡殓。见公及女，乃生人也。咸惊以问之，公具告焉。乡老共怒残其神，曰： “乌将军，此乡镇神，乡人奉之久矣，岁配以女，才无他虞。此礼少迟，即风雨 雷雹为虐。奈何失路之客，而伤我明神，致暴于人，此乡何负？当杀公以祭乌将 军，不尔，亦缚送本县。”挥少年将令执公，公谕之曰：“尔徒老于年，未老于 事。

    Explanation

    25

    Soon, the sound of weeping grew closer, and it turned out to be the girl's parents, brothers, and the elders of the village, all carrying the coffin together, intending to collect the body for burial. Seeing the gentleman and the girl, they realized they were still alive. Everyone was surprised and asked about it, and the gentleman explained in detail. The village elders, enraged by the desecration of their god, said, "General of the Crows, this is our village deity. The villagers have worshipped him for a long time. We provide him with a girl each year, and only then do we avoid other calamities. If this ritual is slightly delayed, wind, rain, thunder, and hail will wreak havoc. How can a lost traveler harm our clear god and bring violence upon our people? What has this village done wrong? We should kill you to sacrifice to General of the Crows. If not, we will bind you and send you to our county." They gestured to the young men to seize the gentleman, but he explained to them, "You may be old in age, but you are not experienced in handling such matters."

    26

    我天下之达理者，尔众听吾言。夫神，承天而为镇也，不若诸侯受命于天子 而疆理天下乎？”曰：“然。”公曰：“使诸侯渔色于中国，天子不怒乎？残虐 于人，天子不伐乎？诚使尔呼将军者，真神明也，神固无猪蹄，天岂使淫妖之兽 乎？且淫妖之兽，天地之罪畜也，吾执正以诛之，岂不可乎！尔曹无正人，使尔 少女年年横死于妖畜，积罪动天。安知天不使吾雪焉？从吾言，当为尔除之，永 无聘礼之患，如何？”乡人悟而喜曰：“愿从公命。”

    Explanation

    26

    I, who understand the principles of the world, address you all. The deity, who upholds the heavens and stabilizes the earth, is not as worthy as the feudal lords who receive their mandate from the Son of Heaven and govern the realm, is he not? The people responded affirmatively. I said, "If the feudal lords indulge in lust within the central lands, would the Son of Heaven not be angry? If they oppress and harm people, would the Son of Heaven not punish? If indeed the one you call 'General' is truly a deity, a deity would not have pig's feet. Would Heaven send a lustful and monstrous beast? Moreover, a lustful and monstrous beast is the guilty creature of heaven and earth. I will uphold righteousness and punish it, is this not possible! You people have no righteous ones. If your young girls die year after year at the hands of this monstrous beast, accumulated sins move Heaven. How do you know that Heaven does not intend for me to avenge this? If you follow my words, I will eliminate it for you, and you will never again suffer from the burden of bride prices. What do you say?" The villagers understood and were pleased, saying, "We wish to follow your command."

    27

    乃令数百人，执弓矢刀枪锹之属，环而自随，寻血而行。才二十里，血入 大冢穴中。因围而属刂之，应手渐大如瓮口，公令束薪燃火投入照之。其中若大 室，见一大猪，无前左蹄，血卧其地，突烟走出，毙于围中。
    　　乡人翻共相庆，会钱以酬公。公不受，曰：“吾为人除害，非鬻猎者。”得 免之女辞其父母亲族曰：“多幸为人，托质血属，闺闱未出，固无可杀之罪。今 者贪钱五十万，以嫁妖兽，忍锁而去，岂人所宜！若非郭公之仁勇，宁有今日？ 是妾死于父母而生于郭公也。请从郭公，不复以旧乡为念矣。”泣拜而从公，公 多歧援谕，止之不获，遂纳为侧室，生子数人。

    Explanation

    27

    The official ordered hundreds of people, armed with bows, arrows, swords, spears, shovels, and other tools, to form a circle around themselves and follow the trail of blood. After traveling only twenty li, the blood led them to a large tomb's cave. They surrounded the area and began digging, and as they dug, the opening gradually widened like the mouth of a jar. The official then ordered bundled firewood to be lit and thrown into the opening to illuminate it. Inside, they found a large room containing a pig with no left front hoof, lying on the ground in blood. The pig burst out of the smoke and died within the enclosure.

    The villagers rejoiced together and gathered money to reward the official. The official declined, saying, "I am here to eliminate harm for people, not to sell hunting." The woman who had been spared, addressing her parents and relatives, said, "I am fortunate to be human, entrusted with blood relations, and have not yet left the inner chambers, so there is no fault in killing. Greedy for fifty thousand coins, I chose to marry an evil beast, enduring the lock and leaving, is this suitable for a person? If not for the benevolence and courage of Official Guo, how could I have this day? I have died to my parents and been reborn through Official Guo. I will follow Official Guo, no longer thinking of my old hometown." She wept and bowed, following the official. Despite many attempts to persuade and stop her, the official eventually took her as a concubine, and they had several children.

    28

    公之贵也，皆任大官之位。事已前定，虽生远地，而至于鬼神终不能害，明 矣。
    　　○来君绰
    　　隋炀帝征辽，十二军尽没，总管来护坐法受戮，炀帝尽欲诛其诸子。君绰忧 惧连诛，因与秀才罗巡、罗逖、李万进结为奔走之友，共亡命至海州。
    　　夜黑迷路，路旁有灯火，因与共投之。扣门数下，有一苍头迎拜君绰，君绰 因问：“此是谁家？”答曰：“科斗郎君，姓威，即当府秀才也。”遂启门，又 自闭，敲中门，曰：“蜗儿，外有四五个客。”蜗儿即又一苍头也。遂开门，秉 烛引客就馆客位，床榻茵褥甚备。俄有二小童持烛自中门出，曰：“六郎子出来。” 君绰等降阶见主人。主人辞彩朗然，文辩纷错，自通姓名曰“威污蠖”。叙寒温 讫，揖客由阼阶，坐曰：“污蠖忝以本州乡赋，得与足下同声，清宵良会，殊是 所愿。”即命酒合坐。渐至酣畅，谈谑交至，众所不能对。

    Explanation

    28

    The person's rise to prominence was marked by holding high-ranking official positions. The matter was predetermined, and even if born far away, the gods and spirits could not harm him, clearly showing the inevitability of his success.

    ○ Junchuo

    During the reign of Emperor Yang of Sui, when he launched a campaign against Goguryeo, all twelve armies were defeated. General Lai Hu was executed for legal reasons, and Emperor Yang wanted to execute all of his sons. Junchuo, fearing that he would be implicated in the execution, formed a close friendship with the scholars Luo Xun, Luo Ti, and Li Wanjin, and they fled together to Haizhou.

    At night, they were lost and disoriented. They saw lights along the road and decided to seek refuge there. They knocked on the door several times, and an old servant greeted Junchuo with a bow. Junchuo asked, "Who lives here?" The servant replied, "This is a young scholar named Wei, surnamed Wei, a local scholar from the prefecture." They then opened the door and closed it again, knocking on the inner door and saying, "Wotou, there are four or five guests outside." Wotou was another young servant. They opened the door and lit candles to guide the guests to the guest room, where the beds and cushions were well-prepared. Soon, two young boys carrying candles came out from the inner door and said, "Sixth Master, come out." Junchuo and the others descended the steps to meet the host. The host spoke eloquently and persuasively, introducing himself as "Wei Wuhuo." After exchanging pleasantries, he invited the guests to sit on the main seat and said, "Wuhuo is honored to share the same state with you, and a pleasant meeting on a clear night is a great wish." He then ordered wine and sat down with them. Gradually, they became merry, and jokes and teasing alternated, leaving everyone unable to respond.

    29

    君绰颇不能平，欲以 理挫之，无计，因举觞曰：“君绰请起一令，以坐中姓名双声者，犯罚如律。” 君绰曰：“威污蠖。”实讥其姓。众皆抚手大笑，以为得言。及至污蠖，改令曰： “以坐中人姓为歌声，自二字至五字。”令曰：“罗李，罗来李，罗李罗来，罗 李罗李来。”众皆惭其辩捷。罗巡又问：“君风雅之士，足得自比云龙，何玉名 之自贬子耶？”污蠖曰：“仆久从宾贡，多为主司见屈。以仆后于群士，何异尺 蠖于污池乎？”巡又问：“公华宗，氏族何为不载？”污蠖曰：“我本田氏，出 于齐威王，亦犹桓丁之类，何足下之不学耶？”既而蜗儿举方丈盘至，珍羞水陆， 充溢其间。君绰及仆者无不饱饫。夜阑彻烛，连榻而寝。迟明叙别，恨恨俱不自 胜。

    Explanation

    29

    Jun Chuo was quite unable to be at peace, wanting to use reason to defeat him/her, but having no plan, he then raised his cup and said, "Jun Chuo proposes to start a rule: those whose names in the company have homophones will be punished according to the law." Jun Chuo said, "Wei Wuhuo," which was actually a pun on the person's name. Everyone clapped and laughed loudly, thinking they had hit the mark. When it came to Wuhuo, he changed the rule and said, "To make the surnames of the people in the company into songs, from two characters to five characters." The rule was, "Luo Li, Luo Lai Li, Luo Li Luo Lai, Luo Li Luo Li Lai." Everyone was ashamed of their quick wit. Luo Xun then asked, "You are a gentleman of refined tastes, worthy to compare oneself to a dragon. Why do you belittle yourself with such a name?" Wuhuo said, "I have been a guest scholar for a long time, often being humiliated by the examiners. What difference is there between a small caterpillar in a dirty pool?" Luo Xun asked again, "You are of noble lineage, why is your clan not recorded?" Wuhuo said, "I am originally from the Tian family, descended from Duke Wei of Qi, also like the Huan and Ding families. How is it that you are not well-read?" Soon after, a large tray was brought, filled with delicacies from both land and sea. Jun Chuo and the servants all ate their fill. As night deepened and the candles were extinguished, they slept on the same couch. At dawn, they parted ways, both deeply saddened and could not bear it.

    30

    君绰等行数里，犹念污蠖，复来，见昨所会之处，了无人居，唯污池，池边 有大螾，长数尺。又有蜗螺丁子，皆大常者数倍，方知污蠖及二竖皆此物也。 遂共恶昨宵所食，各吐出青泥及污水数升。
    　　
    　　卷二
    　　○崔环
    　　安平崔环者，司戎郎宣之子。元和五年夏五月，遇疾于荥阳别业。忽见黄衫 吏二人，执帖来追，遂行数百步，入城。城中有街两畔，官林相对，绝无人家， 直北数里到门，题曰“判官院”。见二吏迤逦向北，亦有林木，袴靴秣头，佩刀 头，执弓矢者，散立者，各数百人。同到之人数千，或杻，或系，或缚，或囊 盛耳头，或连其项，或衣服俨然，或簪裙济济，各有惧色，或泣或叹。其黄衫人 一留伴环，一入告。

    Explanation

    30

    Jun Chuo and his companions walked several miles, still thinking about the "污蠖" (a type of creature), and then returned. They saw the place where they had met the previous day, but there was no sign of human habitation, only a dirty pond. By the pond's edge, there was a large earthworm, several feet long. There were also snails and something called "丁子," all of which were several times larger than usual. They then realized that the "污蠖" and the two little devils were all the same kind of creature. As a result, they all became disgusted with what they had eaten the previous night and each vomited out several liters of green mud and dirty water.

    Volume Two
    ○ Cui Huan
    Cui Huan of Anping was the son of Cui Xuan, a military officer. In the fifth year of the Yuanhe era, during the summer of May, he fell ill at his estate in Zhengyang. Suddenly, he saw two officials in yellow robes, holding a summons, who came to escort him. They walked several hundred steps and entered the city. The city had streets on both sides, with government forests facing each other, and there were no houses at all. They walked straight north for several miles to a gate, which was inscribed with the words "Judicial Office." They saw two officials walking north, and there were also trees, men wearing trousers and boots, and those wearing headgear, carrying swords, and holding bows and arrows, scattered among them, numbering several hundred people. There were thousands of people who had come with them, some bound, some tied, some bound, some in bags with their heads, some with their necks connected, some dressed neatly, some with hairpins and skirts, all showing signs of fear, some crying and some sighing. One of the officials in yellow robes stayed to accompany Cui Huan, while the other entered to report.

    31

    俄闻决人四下声，既而告者出曰：“判官传语：何故不抚幼 小，不务成家，广破庄园，但恣酒色！又虑尔小累无掌，且为宽恕，轻杖放归， 宜即洗心，勿复贰过。若踵前非，固无容舍。”乃敕伴者令送归。环曰：“判官 谓谁？”曰：“司戎郎也。”环泣曰：“弃背多年，号天莫及。幸蒙追到，慈颜 不遥，乞一拜见，死且无恨。”二吏曰：“明晦各殊，去留有隔，不合见也。” 环曰：“向者传语云已见责。此身不入，何以受刑？”吏曰：“入则不得归矣。 凡人有三魂，一魂在家，二魂受杖耳。不信，看郎胫合有杖痕。”遂褰衣自视， 其两胫各有杖痕四，痛苦不济，匍匐而行，举足甚艰。同到之人，叹羡之声，喧 于歧路。

    Explanation

    31

    Soon he heard the sound of people being separated, and then a messenger came out and said: “The Judge has conveyed this message: Why do you neglect the young, fail to establish a family, recklessly destroy estates, and indulge only in wine and sensual pleasures? Considering that you are a minor with no authority, I have shown leniency and will release you with a light beating. You should now cleanse your heart and not repeat your offenses. If you persist in your past wrongs, there will be no place for you to be accepted.” He then ordered his attendants to send him back.

    Huan asked, “Who is this Judge?” The attendant replied, “It is the Officer of Military Affairs.” Huan wept and said, “I have been estranged from you for many years, and my cries to heaven have gone unanswered. Fortunately, you have pursued me, and your kind face is not far away. I beg only for a single sight of you, and I shall die with no regrets.” The two officials said, “The bright and the obscure are different; there is a boundary between staying and going. We cannot meet.”

    Huan said, “Earlier, the message said that I had already been reprimanded. If this body cannot enter, how can I receive punishment?” The official replied, “If you enter, you will not be allowed to return. All people have three souls: one remains at home, and two receive the beating. Do not believe me—look at the young man’s legs and see if there are marks from the beating.” He then lifted his robe to look, and on each of his legs there were four marks from the beating. In great pain, he crawled along, finding it extremely difficult to raise his feet. Those who had accompanied him heard the sounds of admiration and sorrow echoing at the crossroads.

    32

    南行百余步，街东有大林。二吏前曰：“某等日夜事判官，为日虽久，幽冥 小吏，例不免贫。各有许惠资财，竟无暇取，不因送郎阴路，无因得往求之。请 即暂止林下，某等偕去，俄顷即来。诸处皆是恶鬼曹司，不合往，乞郎不移足相 待。”言讫各去，久而不来。环闷，试诣街西行，一署门题曰“人矿院”，门亦 甚净。环素有胆，且恃其父为判官，身又蒙放，遂入其中。过屏障，见一大石， 周回数里。有一军将坐于石北厅上，据案而坐，铺人各绕石及石上，有数十大鬼， 形貌不同，以大铁椎椎人为矿石。东有杻械枷锁者数千人，悲啼恐惧，不可名 状。点名拽来，投来石上，遂椎之，既碎，唱其名。军将判之，一吏于案后读之 云：“傅某狱讫。”鬼亦捧云。其中有傅硙狱者，付火狱者，傅汤狱者。

    Explanation

    32

    Walking southeast for over a hundred steps, they reached a large forest on the eastern side of the street. Two officials approached and said, "We serve the judge in the underworld day and night, and though we have done so for a long time, as minor officials in the underworld, we are inevitably poor. Each of us has been offered gifts and wealth, but we have no time to take them. Without sending you on your way through the underworld, we cannot go to seek them. Please stop temporarily under the tree, and we will go together, returning shortly. All places are offices of evil spirits, and it is not appropriate to go there. Please do not move from your spot." After saying this, they departed, and did not return for a long time. Feeling restless, the person tried to walk west along the street and came to a gate with a sign that read "Human Ore Institute." The gate was also very clean. The person, who had always been brave and relied on their father being a judge in the underworld, having also been granted release, entered the place. Passing through the barriers, they saw a large stone, several miles around. A military officer was seated at the northern hall of the stone, sitting at a desk, with people gathered around the stone and on it. There were dozens of large spirits with different appearances, using large iron hammers to turn people into ore. To the east, there were thousands of people bound with shackles and chains, crying and fearing, beyond description. They were called out by name, dragged to the stone, and then hammered, once broken, their names were called. The military officer judged them, and one clerk read from behind the desk, "Fou (a name) has completed his sentence." The spirits also confirmed it. Among them were those who were to be sent to the furnace, those to be sent to the fire, and those to be sent to the soup.

    环直逼 石前看之，军将指之云：“曹司法严，不合妄入，彼是何人，敢来闲看！”人吏 竞来传问，环恃不对。军将怒曰：“看既无端，问又不对，傍观岂如身试之审乎？” 敕一吏拽来锻之。环一魂尚立，见其石上别有一身，被拽扑卧石上，大锤锤之， 痛苦之极，实不可忍。须臾，骨肉皆碎，仅欲成泥。二吏者走来，槌胸曰：“郎 君，再三乞不闲行，何故来此？”遂告军将曰：“此是判官郎君，阳禄未终，追 来却放，暂来入者。无间地狱，入不须臾。遂道如斯。何计得令复旧？”军将者 亦惧曰：“初问不言，忿而处置，如何？”因问诸鬼曰：“何计得令复旧？”皆 曰：“唯濮阳霞一人耳。”曰；“远近？”曰：“去此万里。昨者北海王与化形 出游，为海人所愪。其王请出，今亦未回。”乃令一鬼召之。

    Liu Guishun

    Liu Guishun from Wu Province, during the twentieth year of the Kaihuang era of the Sui Dynasty, traveled from the southern part of China to Baling. A strong wind blew him to the foot of Junshan Mountain. He moored his boat and went ashore, looking for a small path. Unconsciously, he walked several miles, in a state of high spirits, leaping over streams and ravines, not following the usual path. Suddenly, he saw a large stone by the side of the road, transparent inside and out, round and smooth, surrounding six or seven acres. Outside it was all covered with green bamboo, round and large like a pot, over a hundred feet tall, with leaves trailing white clouds, densely arranged and reaching up to the sky, and a gentle breeze blowing, sounding like the music of silk and bamboo. A tree grew from the center of the stone, over a hundred feet tall, with branches and trunk bending in the shade, appearing in five colors. The green leaves were like plates, the flowers over a foot in diameter, deep blue in color, leaves deep red, with a strange fragrance turning into smoke, floating gently on objects.

    There were thousands of parrots, with red beaks and green feathers, tails two or three feet long, soaring among them, calling each other by name, with clear and resonant sounds. One of them sang a song and said, "This song is what the Lady Gouyi of Emperor Wu of Han often sang." The lyrics were: "Wearing the cicada, clearly conveying the words of the emperor."

    After finishing his meal, two Taoist priests suddenly appeared, descending from the sky. They turned to see Gu Shun and exclaimed, "It is very rare! To be in the presence of a parrot.     During the reigns of Emperor Xuanzong in the Kaiyuan and Tianbao eras, there was a scholar named Cui who lived near the Luogu Pass in Eastern Zhou. He enjoyed planting flowers and bamboo, and outside his home, he cultivated exotic flowers. In the late spring, the fragrance of the blossoms was so strong that it could be smelled from a hundred steps away. Every morning, Cui would wash and brush his teeth before admiring the flowers alone. One day, he suddenly saw a beautiful woman riding a fine horse from west to east, with a few elderly attendants following behind. The woman was exceptionally beautiful, and her horse was swift. Cui did not have time to take a closer look before the woman had already passed by. The next day, she passed by again, and Cui, in anticipation, prepared wine and tea on a mat and chair under the flowers. He approached the horse and said, "I enjoy flowers and plants, and everything in this garden is planted by hand. The fragrance and beauty seem worthy of your attention. I have seen you pass by frequently, and I assume your servants must be tired. I have prepared some wine and food, hoping you will rest here." The woman did not look back and continued on her way. Later, one of the attendants said, "Just prepare the wine and food, and there is no need to worry." The woman turned and scolded, "Why do you speak so lightly to strangers?" After saying this, she rode off.

    The next day, Cui prepared a special wine at the foot of the mountain and awaited the arrival of the young lady. The servant then took control of the young lady's horse and led it to the hall. The elderly servant turned to Cui and said, "Since you are not yet married, may I act as your matchmaker?" Cui was greatly pleased, bowed twice, and knelt, asking the servant not to forget him. The sister was also extremely beautiful in appearance and demeanor. Thus, the young lady was married to Cui.

    崔生母在旧居，殊不知崔生纳室。崔生以不告而娶，但启聘媵。母见女郎， 女郎悉归之礼甚具。经月余日，忽有一人送食于女郎，甘香特异。后崔生觉母慈 颜衰瘁，因伏问几下，母曰：“吾有汝一子，冀得永寿。今汝所纳新妇，妖美无 双。吾于士塑图书之中，未尝识此，必恐是狐媚之辈，伤害于汝，遂致吾忧。” 崔生入室见女郎，女郎涕泪交下，曰：“本待箕帚，便望终天，不知尊夫人待以 狐媚辈，明晨即便请行，相爱今宵耳。”崔生掩泪不能言。

    Explanation

    42

    Cui Sheng's mother was living in their old residence and was completely unaware that her son had taken a wife. Cui Sheng, having not informed his mother, only notified her about the engagement and the secondary wife. When the mother saw the young lady, the young lady had all the wedding rites fully conducted. After more than a month, a person suddenly brought food to the young lady, which was exceptionally sweet and fragrant. Later, Cui Sheng noticed that his mother's face had become pale and worried. He asked her while kneeling, and she said, "I had hoped that you would live long. Now, the new wife you have taken is beautiful and cunning beyond compare. I have never seen such a person in the books of scholars and literati. I fear she may be a deceitful woman who could harm you, causing me great worry." Cui Sheng went into the room to see the young lady, who was weeping and said, "I intended to be a loyal wife, hoping to be with you forever. But I did not know that your mother considers me a deceitful woman. By tomorrow morning, I will request to leave, and our love will last only tonight." Cui Sheng could not speak while holding back tears.

    43

    明日，女郎车骑至，女郎乘马，崔生从送之，入逻谷三十余里，山间有川， 川中异香珍果，不可胜纪。馆于屋室，侈于王者。青衣百许，迎拜女郎曰：“小 娘子，无行崔生，何必将来！”于是捧入，留崔生于门外。未几，一青衣传女郎 姊言曰：“崔生遗行，使太夫人疑阻，事宜便绝，不合相见。然小妹曾奉周旋， 亦当奉屈。”俄而召崔生入，责诮再三，辞辩清婉，崔生但拜伏受谴而已。遂坐 于中寝对食，食讫，命酒，召女乐洽饮，铿锵万变。乐阙，其姊谓女郎曰：“须 令崔郎却回，汝有何物赠送？”女郎遂出白玉合子遗崔生，崔生亦自留别。于是 各呜咽而出。行至逻谷，回望千岩万壑，无径路，自恸哭归家。常见玉合子，郁 郁不乐。

    Explanation

    43

    The next day, the young lady arrived with a grand procession. She rode a horse, and Feng Sheng accompanied and sent her off. They entered the Luo Valley for more than thirty miles, where there was a river in the mountains. The river contained exotic fragrances and precious fruits, too numerous to count. The lodging was in a house, more luxurious than a king's. About a hundred maids in green dresses welcomed and bowed to the young lady, saying, "Young lady, Feng Sheng has no virtue, why bring him here?" They then carried the young lady inside and left Feng Sheng outside the door. Not long after, a maid conveyed the words of the young woman's sister: "Feng Sheng, your lack of virtue has made our grandmother suspicious and hesitant. It would be best to end this matter and not meet again. However, since my younger sister has treated you kindly, she should also receive a gift." Soon after, the sister called Feng Sheng inside, scolding him repeatedly. His words were clear and gentle, and Feng Sheng only bowed and accepted his blame. They then sat in the inner chamber to eat, and after finishing, they ordered wine and summoned female musicians to entertain them. The music was varied and beautiful. After the music ended, the sister said to the young lady, "You must make Feng Sheng return. What do you have to give him as a gift?" The young lady then took out a white jade box to give to Feng Sheng, and Feng Sheng also kept something as a keepsake. They both wept and left. Walking to the Luo Valley, they looked back at the thousands of mountains and valleys, with no paths in sight. Feng Sheng cried bitterly and returned home. He often saw the jade box, feeling melancholy and unhappy.

    忽有胡僧扣门求食，崔生出见，胡僧曰：“君有至宝，乞相示也。”崔生曰： “某贫士，何有见请？”僧曰：“君岂不有异人奉赠，贫道望气知之。”崔生因 出合子示胡僧，僧起拜请曰：“请以百万市之。”遂将去。崔生问僧曰：“女郎 是谁？”曰：“君所纳妻，王母第三个女，玉卮娘子也。姊亦负美名在仙都，况 复人间。所惜君娶之不得久远。倘住一年，君举家必仙矣。”崔生叹怨迨卒。

    Suddenly, a foreign monk knocked on the door asking for food. Cui Sheng went out to see him, and the monk said, "You have a precious treasure, I beg you to show it to me." Cui Sheng replied, "I am a poor scholar, what do I have that you would ask to see?" The monk said, "Do you not have a gift from a strange person? I, a poor monk, can sense it through my qi." Cui Sheng then took out the box and showed it to the foreign monk. The monk stood up and bowed, saying, "I will buy it for a million." He then took the box and left. Cui Sheng asked the monk, "Who is the lady?" The monk replied, "Your wife you have taken is the third daughter of the Queen Mother, the Lady of the Jade Cup. Her sister also has a beautiful reputation in the celestial realm, let alone in the mortal world. It is a pity that you cannot keep her for a long time. If you stay for a year, your whole family will surely become immortals." Cui Sheng sighed and lamented until he died.

    ○曹惠
    　　武德初，有曹惠者，制授江州参军。官舍有佛堂，堂中有二木偶人，长尺余， 雕饰甚巧，丹青剥落。惠因持归与稚儿。后稚儿方食饼，木偶即引手请之。儿惊 报惠，惠笑曰：“取木偶来。”即言曰：“轻红、轻素自有名，何呼木偶！”于 是转盼驰走，悉无异人。
    　　惠问曰：“汝何时来物，颇能作怪？”轻素曰：“某与轻红是宣城太守谢家 俑偶，当时天下工巧，总不及沈隐侯家老苍头孝忠也。轻素、轻红即孝忠所造也。 隐侯哀宣城无辜，葬日故有此赠。时轻素在圹中，方持汤与乐家娘子濯足，闻外 有持兵称敕声，娘子畏惧，跣足化为白蝼，少顷，二贼执炬至，尽掠财物，谢郎 时颔瑟瑟环，亦为贼敲颐脱之。贼人照见轻红等，曰：‘二明器不恶，可与小儿 为戏具。’遂持出，时天正二年也。自尔流落数家，陈末麦铁杖犹子咬头将至此， 以到今日。*?

    45

    A Tale of Cao Hui

    In the early years of the Wu德 era, there was a man named Cao Hui who was appointed as a military secretary in Jiangzhou by imperial decree. In his official residence, there was a Buddhist hall, and in the hall were two wooden figures, each about a foot long, intricately carved and decorated, though their paint had faded. Cao Hui took them home and gave them to his young son. Later, when the child was eating a cake, the wooden figures reached out and asked for it. The child was startled and reported this to Cao Hui, who laughed and said, "Bring the wooden figures here." The figures then spoke, saying, "We are known as Light Red and Light White; why do you call us wooden figures?" They then turned and walked around as if they were real people.

    Cao Hui asked, "When did you come into existence, and are you capable of causing strange events?" Light White replied, "I and Light Red were made by a servant named Xie in the household of the governor of Xuanzhou. At that time, no one in the world could match the craftsmanship of the old servant Xie from the household of Shen Yinhou. Light Red and I were made by Xie. Shen Yinhou, moved by the innocence of the people of Xuanzhou, gave these figures to us on the day of the burial. At that time, I was in the tomb, holding water to wash the feet of Lady Yue. I heard the sound of someone outside with weapons claiming an imperial edict. Lady Yue was afraid, and her bare feet transformed into white ants. Soon after, two bandits with torches arrived and took all the valuables. Lord Xie was wearing a jade ring around his neck, and the bandit knocked it off. The bandits saw Light Red and others, saying, 'These two ritual objects are not bad; they can be toys for children.' So they took them out, and it was the second year of the Tianzheng era. Since then, they have passed through several households. At the end of the Chen dynasty, Wei Tiezhang's nephew named Jiao brought them here, and they have remained until today."

    被萦治试唬骸霸悰判恍鞮撬魍蹙丛蚺巠籧麑五嵩评旨夷餇子？”轻 素曰：“王氏乃生前之妻，乐家乃冥婚耳。王氏本屠酤种，性粗率多力，至冥中 犹与宣城琴瑟不睦，何宣城颜严，则磔石抵关以为威胁。宣城自密启于天帝，帝 许逐之。二女一男，悉随母归矣。遂再娶乐彦辅第八娘子，美资质，善书，好弹 琴，尤与殷东阳仲文、谢荆州晦夫人相得，日恣追寻。宣城尝云：‘我才方古词 人，唯不及东阿耳。其余文士，皆吾机中之肉，可以宰割矣。’见为南曹典铨郎， 与潘典门同列，乘肥衣轻，贵于生前百倍。然十日一朝晋、宋、梁，可以为劳， 近闻亦已停矣。”

    A Woman with Two Heads and Four Arms

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms.

    47

    惠又问曰：“汝二人灵异若此，吾欲舍汝，何如？”即皆喜曰：“以轻素等 变化，虽无不可，君意如不放，终不能逃。庐山山神欲索轻素作舞姬久矣，今此 奉辞，便当受彼荣富。然君能终恩，请命画工，便赐粉黛。”即令工人为图之， 使被锦绣。轻素喜笑曰：“此度非论舞姬，亦当彼夫人。无以奉酬，请以微言留 别。百代之中，但有他人会者，无不为忠臣居大位矣。言曰：‘鸡角入骨，紫鹤 吃黄角甲（疑此处有脱误，“黄角甲”，《广记》作“黄鼠申”，“申”字或属 下读），不害五通泉室，为六代吉昌。’”言讫而灭。
    　　后有人祷庐山神，女巫云：“神君新纳一夫人，要翠花钗簪，汝宜求之，当 降大福。”祷者求而焚之，遂如愿焉。惠亦不能知其微言，访之时贤皆不识，或 云：中书令岑文本识其三句，亦不为人说云。

    47

    The official asked, "You two are so extraordinary, I wish to release you, what do you think?" They both happily replied, "By transforming into light and color, there is nothing we cannot do. If Your Excellency does not release us, we ultimately cannot escape. The god of Mount Lu has long desired to take light and color as his dancers. Now that we are leaving, we will receive his honor and wealth. However, if Your Excellency can fulfill this favor, please command the painter to create a portrait and bestow upon us cosmetics." The official then ordered the workers to make the portrait, and they were dressed in brocade. One of them, Light and Color, smiled and said, "This time, it's not just about being a dancer, but also his wife. There is nothing to repay, so please leave this subtle message as a farewell. In a hundred generations, if anyone else understands this, they will surely become loyal ministers and hold high positions. The message says: 'The rooster's horn penetrates the bone, the purple crane eats the yellow rat's skin (there may be an error here, 'yellow rat's skin,' the Guangji records 'yellow rat's tail,' the 'tail' character might belong to the next line), it will not harm the five-communication spring chamber, bringing good fortune for six generations.'" After speaking, they vanished.

    Later, someone prayed to the god of Mount Lu, and the female shaman said, "The divine lord has recently taken a new wife, who requires a jade flower hairpin. You should seek it and burn it, and you will receive great blessings." The one who prayed sought the hairpin and burned it, and as a result, his wish was fulfilled. The official could not understand the subtle message, and when he consulted learned scholars, none of them could decipher it. Some said that the chancellor Cen Wenben recognized three of the sentences, but he did not share them with others.

    ○滕庭俊
    　　文明元年，毗陵掾滕庭俊患热病积年，每发身如火烧，热数日方定。召医， 医不能治。后之洛调选，行至荥阳西十四五里，天向暮，未达前所。遂投一道旁 庄家，主人暂出未至，庭俊心无聊赖，自叹吟曰：“为客多苦辛，日暮无主人。” 即有老父，须发甚秃，衣服亦弊，自堂西出而曰：“老父虽无所解，然性好文章， 适不知郎君来，正与和且耶联句次，闻郎君吟‘为客多苦辛，日暮无主人’，虽 曹丕‘客子常畏人’不能过也。老父与和且耶同作浑家门客，门客虽贫，亦有斗 酒接郎君清话耳。”庭俊甚异之，问：“老父居止何所？”老父曰：“仆忝浑家 扫门之客，姓麻，名束禾，第大，君何不呼为麻大。”庭俊即谢不敏，与之偕行， 绕堂西隅，遂见一门，门启，华堂复阁甚绮秀，馆中有樽酒盘杓。麻大揖庭俊同 坐。

    48

    In the first year of the Wenming era, the official of Piling, Teng Tingjun, suffered from a chronic fever illness that had plagued him for many years. Whenever it flared up, his body felt as if it were on fire, and the fever lasted for several days before subsiding. He called for a doctor, but the doctor could not cure him. Later, he went to Luoyang for promotion, and on his way, he reached a place about fifteen or sixteen miles west of荥yang as dusk approached. He had not yet reached his destination, so he sought shelter at a nearby farm. The owner was temporarily absent, and Teng Tingjun felt bored and sang to himself, saying, "Being a guest brings much hardship and bitterness, at dusk, there is no host." Just then, an old man with sparse hair and shabby clothes came out from the west side of the hall and said, "Although I have no special skills, I enjoy literature. I didn't know you were coming, and I was just composing poetry with Hé Qiěyē. I heard you sing, 'Being a guest brings much hardship and bitterness, at dusk, there is no host.' Although Cao Pi's line 'guests often fear people' cannot surpass it, I am a humble servant in the household. My name is Ma Shùhé, and you can call me Ma Dà. Although I am poor, I still have a jug of wine to entertain you with a pleasant conversation."

    Teng Tingjun was surprised and asked, "Where does the old man live?" The old man replied, "I am a humble servant in the household, and my name is Ma, and I am the first elder. Why don't you call me Ma Dà?" Teng Tingjun politely declined, saying he was not quick-witted enough, but he accompanied the old man. They walked around the west corner of the hall and saw a door. When they opened the door, they found a splendid hall with multiple floors, beautifully decorated. There was a feast prepared in the hall with a jug of wine and plates and cups. The old man bowed to Teng Tingjun and invited him to sit down.

    　　○顾总

    Lord Tiwen is known for his hospitality, but how many people does he support?

    If Feng Huan were still alive, he would be among the lowest-ranking guests today. Cai and Ma laughed and said, "How can you mock me? If you had been with your wife, one day would have been enough." They then had a lavish feast with multiple rounds of food and drink. When the host arrived, he couldn't find Ting Jun. He sent someone to call him, and Ting Jun replied, "Yes." But the guest rooms and Ma and He were nowhere to be seen. Ting Jun was in the latrine, with only a large fly and a broom nearby. Ting Jun had previously suffered from a fever, but after this, he was completely cured and the fever never returned.

    In the first year of the Tianjian era of the Liang dynasty, Gu Zong was a county official. He was often beaten and often felt depressed and resentful. He escaped to a place between tombs, wandering and feeling melancholic, not knowing where to go. Suddenly, two yellow-clad men saw Gu Zong and said, "Lord Liu, do you remember our past interactions?" Gu Zong was surprised and said, "My family is the Gu family, and I have never met you before, so why are you asking about our past interactions?" The two men replied, "We are Wang Can and Xu Gan. You were Lord Liu Zhen in life, a Grand Councilor of Kunning, but you were demoted to a minor official for accepting bribes, and you probably don't remember this now. However, your words are still clear, and you still have the style of a secretary." They then took out five volumes of books from their sleeves and showed them to Gu Zong, saying, "These are your collected works. You should read them carefully." Gu Zong tried to read them, and suddenly he understood everything clearly and felt a surge of creative inspiration.

    其集人多有本，惟卒后数篇记得。诗一章，题目曰《从驾游幽丽宫却忆平生 西园文会因寄修文府正郎蔡伯喈》，诗曰：

    51

    Most of his collections are available, but only a few poems are remembered after his death. One poem, titled "Following the Emperor on a Tour of the Beautiful Palace, Recalling Past Literary Gatherings at the Western Garden and Sending This Poem to Cai Bojia, the Right Minister of the Ministry of Culture," reads as follows:

    In the Han dynasty, the laws and norms were in chaos, and the rivers and lakes were turbulent.
    The illustrious Wei Emperor, Cao Cao, rescued those in peril and calmed the waves.
    The heavenly mandate has been established, and the people are also secure and complete.
    He greatly opened the Chancellor's office and gathered all the fragrant orchids.
    At first, I followed the many gentlemen, daily serving the wise ruler with joy.
    The cultural emperor was in the spring palace, his filial piety exceeding the usual inquiries about health.
    The supervisor had extra leisure time, the gardens were freely visited.
    The lowly minister wore a hairpin and pen, supporting the holy one with harmonious music.
    Walking out of the palace at night, it was cool; precious trees were bathed in clear dew.
    The celestial phenomena are indeed splendid, resounding like jade and stone.
    Being commanded to compose a harmonious piece, looking back, it was difficult to complete.
    My weak nature could not sustain itself, it was fragile, decaying, and withered.
    Who would have thought for over a decade, the tombs were cold, with paulownia and Chinese parasol trees.
    Today, in the country of K'un-ming, again, wearing the official cap.
    Serving the emperor in the distant palace, climbing high into the clouds.
    But recalling the time at the Western Garden, for a moment, sorrow and bitterness filled the heart.

    君昔汉公卿，未央冠群贤。

    ○周静帝居延部落主
    　　周静帝初，居延部落主勃都骨低凌暴，奢逸好乐，居处甚盛。忽有人数十至 门，一人先投剌曰：“省名部落主成多受。”因趋入。骨低问曰：“何故省名部 落？”多受曰：“某等数人各殊，名字皆不别造。有姓马者，姓皮者，姓鹿者， 姓熊者，姓獐者，姓卫者，姓班者，然皆名受。唯某帅名多受耳。”骨低曰： “君等悉似伶官，有何所解？”多受曰：“晓弄碗珠。性不爱俗，言皆经义。” 骨低大喜曰：“目所未睹。”有一优即前曰：“某等肚饥，臈臈怡怡，皮漫 绕身三匝。主人食若不充，开口终当不舍。”骨低悦，更命加食。一人曰：“某 请弄大小相成，终始相生。”于是长人吞短人，肥人吞瘦人，相吞残两人。长者 又曰：“请作终始相生耳。”于是吐下一人，吐者又吐一人。递相吐出，人数复 足。骨低甚惊，因重赐赍遣之。

    Explanation

    54

    During the reign of Emperor Jing of Northern Zhou, the tribal leader of Juyan, Bo Du Gu Di, was known for his oppressive behavior, extravagant lifestyle, and love for pleasure. He lived in great splendor. Suddenly, several people arrived at his door, and one of them first presented a card, saying, “I am the leader of the tribe, Cheng Duo Shou.” He then hurriedly entered. Bo Du Gu Di asked, “Why did you name the tribe?” Cheng Duo Shou replied, “We several people are all unique, and our names are not specially created. There are those surnamed Ma, Pi, Lu, Xiong, Zhang, Wei, and Ban, but all of us are named Shou. Only my leader’s name is Duo Shou.” Bo Du Gu Di said, “You all seem like court jesters, what do you understand?” Cheng Duo Shou replied, “We are skilled in playing with bowls and pearls. We do not love the common, and our words are all based on classical principles.” Bo Du Gu Di was greatly delighted and said, “I have never seen anything like this before.” One of the jesters stepped forward and said, “We are all hungry, happy and content, with our skin wrapped around our bodies three times. If the host’s food is not sufficient, we will not stop opening our mouths.” Bo Du Gu Di was pleased and ordered more food to be brought. One of them said, “I will perform a trick of the big and small, the beginning and the end.” He then had tall people swallow short people, and fat people swallow thin people, until two people were left. The taller one then said, “Please perform the beginning and the end.” He then spat out one person, and the one who spat out another person. One after another, they spat out, and the number of people was restored. Bo Du Gu Di was greatly surprised and heavily rewarded and sent them away.

    骨低深怒，欲伺隙杀之。因令密访之。见至一古宅基而灭。骨低闻而令掘之， 深数尺，于瓦砾下得一大木槛。中有皮袋数千。槛旁有谷麦，触即为灰。槛中得 竹简书，文字磨灭，不可识。唯隐隐似有三数字，若是“陵”字。骨低知是诸袋 为怪，欲举出焚之。诸袋因号呼槛中曰：“某等无命，寻合化灭。缘李都尉留水 银在此，故得且存。某等即都尉李少卿般粮袋，屋崩平压，绵历岁月，今已有命， 见为居延山神收作伶人，伏乞存情于神，不相残毁。自此不敢复扰高居矣。”骨 低利其水银，尽焚诸袋。无不为冤楚声，血流漂洒。焚讫，骨低房廊户牖悉为冤 痛之音，如焚袋时，月余日不止。其年骨低举家病死，死者相继，周岁无复孑遗。 水银后亦失所在。

    56

    Bone Low was deeply enraged and sought an opportunity to kill him. He then ordered a secret investigation. They discovered that the person had disappeared at the site of an ancient house foundation. Upon hearing this, Bone Low ordered the site to be excavated. After digging several feet deep, they found a large wooden cage beneath the broken tiles and debris. Inside the cage were thousands of leather bags. Beside the cage was some grain and wheat, which turned to ash upon contact. In the cage, they found bamboo slips with faded and unreadable text, except for three faint characters that resembled the word "陵" (mound). Bone Low realized that the bags were supernatural and intended to burn them. The bags cried out from within the cage, saying, "We are doomed and will soon be destroyed. We have been preserved here because Commander Li left mercury with us. We are the grain bags of Commander Li Shaoqing. The house collapsed and crushed us, and over many years, we have now been granted a new life, taken by the god of Juanyuan Mountain to become entertainers. We beg the god to have mercy and not to destroy us. From now on, we will not disturb the high and noble." Bone Low coveted the mercury and burned all the bags. The bags emitted sounds of suffering and lamentation, and blood flowed and splattered. After the burning, the halls, corridors, doors, and windows of Bone Low's house were filled with sounds of sorrow and pain, just as they had been when the bags were burned, for more than a month without stopping. That year, Bone Low's entire family fell ill and died, one after another, with no survivors remaining after a year. The mercury also disappeared.

    In the year of Wenming, Liu Feng, an official of Jingling, spent the night at an empty inn in Yiling. Under the bright moonlight, he took a rest.     　　○董慎
    　　隋大业元年，兖州佐史董慎，性公直，明法理。自都督以下，用法有不直， 必起犯颜而谏之。虽加削责，亦不惧，必俟刑正而后退。尝因事暇偶归家，出州 门，逢一黄衣使者曰：“太山府君呼君为录事，知之乎？”因出怀中牒示慎。牒 曰：“董慎名称茂实，案牒精练，将分疑狱，必俟良能，权差知右曹录事者。” 印处分明，及后署曰倨。慎谓使者曰：“府君呼我，岂有不行，然不识府君名谓 何？”使者曰：“录事勿言，到府即知矣。”因持大布囊，内慎于中，负之趋出 兖州郭，致囊于路左，汲水为泥，封慎两目。
