    ○ Dong Shen

    In the first year of the Daoyi era of the Sui Dynasty, Dong Shen, an assistant official in Yanzhou, was upright and knowledgeable in legal matters. If any subordinate official used the law unfairly, he would boldly advise them. Even if punished, he would not be afraid and would wait for justice to be served before retreating. One day, when he was free and returning home, he met a messenger dressed in yellow who said, "The Lord of Tai Mountain has called you to serve as a recorder, do you know this?" The messenger then showed a document from his chest. The document read, "Dong Shen is renowned for his reputation and solid achievements, and his case files are well-prepared. He is to be appointed as a recorder in the right department." The seal was clear, and the document was signed "A." Dong Shen asked the messenger, "The lord calls me, how could I not go? But I do not know the lord's name." The messenger replied, "Recorder, do not worry; you will know at the lord's place." The messenger then took a large sack, placed Dong Shen inside, carried him out of the city, and sealed his eyes with mud.

    61

    慎目既无所睹，都不知经过远近，忽闻大唱曰：“范慎追董慎到。”使者曰： “诺。”趋入。府君曰：“所追录事，今复何在？”使者曰：“冥司幽秘，恐或 漏泄，向请左曹匿影布囊盛之。”府君大笑曰：“使一范慎追一董慎，取左曹布 囊盛一右曹录事，可谓能防慎矣。”便令写出，抉去目泥，便赐青缣衣、鱼须笏、 豹皮靴，文甚斑驳。邀登副阶，命左右取榻令坐，曰：“藉君公正，故有是请。 今有闽州司马令狐寔等六人，置无间狱，承天曹符，以寔是太元夫人三等亲，准 令式递减三等。昨罪人程翥一百二十人引例，喧讼纷纭，不可止遏。已具名申天 曹。天曹以为罚疑唯轻，亦令量减二等。余恐后人引例多矣，君谓宜如何？”慎 曰：“夫水照妍蚩而人不怒者，以其至清无情，况于天地刑法，岂宜恩贷奸慝。 然慎一胥吏尔，素无文字，虽知不可，终语无条贯。常州府秀才张审通，辞彩隽 拔，足得备君管记。”府君令帖召。

    Once Fan Shen's eyes were opened, he saw nothing, completely unaware of how far he had traveled. Suddenly, he heard a loud call: "Fan Shen, pursue Dong Shen to his destination." The messenger replied, "Yes," and hurriedly entered. The magistrate asked, "Where is the recorder we were pursuing?" The messenger replied, "The underworld is secretive, and there is fear of leakage or exposure. Previously, I requested the Left Department to hide the shadow in a cloth bag and contain him." The magistrate laughed and said, "To send one Fan Shen to pursue one Dong Shen, and to take a cloth bag from the Left Department to contain a recorder from the Right Department—this can be said to be able to prevent caution." He immediately ordered the recorder to be written out, the mud from his eyes removed, and then granted him a blue silk robe, a fish whisker tablet, and leopard skin boots, which were quite mottled. He invited Fan Shen to ascend to the secondary platform, ordered the attendants to fetch a couch for him to sit on, and said, "Because of your fairness, I have this request. Now, there are six people, including the governor of Minzhou, Lingfu Shi, who are placed in a no-judgment prison. According to a decree from the celestial department, since Shi is a third-degree relative of Lady Taiyuan, the punishment is reduced by three degrees according to the regulations. Yesterday, one hundred and twenty criminals, including Cheng Zhu, cited examples, causing noisy and chaotic litigation that could not be stopped. The names have already been listed and submitted to the celestial department. The celestial department considered that punishment should be lenient in doubt and also ordered a reduction of two degrees. I fear that later people will cite many examples. What do you think should be done?" Fan Shen said, "Water reflects beauty and ugliness, and people do not get angry because it is extremely clear and impartial. How much more so for heavenly laws? How can they be lenient with wickedness? But I am just a minor official, have never written anything, and even though I know it is wrong, my words lack coherence. The scholar Zhang Shentong from Changzhou is eloquent and outstanding and is qualified to serve as your secretary." The magistrate ordered a summons to be issued.

    62

    俄顷审通至，曰：“此易耳，君当判以状申。”府君曰：“尹善为我辞。” 即补充左曹录事，仍赐衣服如董慎，各给一玄狐，每出即乘之。审通判曰：“天 本无私，法宜画一，苟从恩贷，是恣奸行。令狐寔前命减刑，已同私请；程翥后 申簿诉，且异罪疑。倘开递减之科，实失公家之论。请依前付无间狱，仍录状申 天曹者。”即有黄衫人持状而往。少顷，复持天符曰：“所申文状，多起异端。 奉主之宜，但合遵守。周礼八议，一曰议亲，又元化匮中释冲符，亦曰无不亲。 是则典章昭然，有何不可。岂可使太元功德，不能庇三等之亲。仍敢愆违，须有 惩谪。府君可罚不紫衣六十甲子，余依前处分者。”府君大怒审通曰：“君为情 辞，使我受谴。”即命左右取方寸肉塞却一耳，遂无闻。审通诉曰：“乞更为判 申，不允，则甘罪再罚。

    Explanation

    62

    Soon, Shentong arrived and said, "This is easy. You should judge and submit a report." The magistrate said, "Yi should speak well for me." Immediately, he was appointed as Left Censor and was also given clothes like those of Dong Shen, each was given one black fox, and each time they went out, they rode it. Shentong judged and said, "Heaven is originally impartial. The law should be uniform. If one grants mercy, it would be to indulge in wicked deeds. Linghu Shi was previously ordered to reduce the sentence, which is the same as a private request; Cheng Zhu later submitted a petition, and there is a difference in doubt. If one opens the door to successive reductions, it would be to lose the public's opinion. Please follow the previous order to send to the hell of no return, and record the report to be submitted to the heavenly court." There was a man in yellow clothes who took the report and went. Soon, he returned with a heavenly decree saying, "The submitted report contains many heretical things. In accordance with the master's will, it should only be followed. The Rites of Zhou have the Eight Deliberations, the first is deliberation for relatives. The Yuanhua Kui in Shi Chongfu also says there is no one who is not a relative. The rules are clearly established, what is there to not accept? How can the great virtue of Taiyuan not protect three grades of relatives? Still dare to violate, there must be punishment. The magistrate should be punished by not wearing purple robes for sixty years. The rest should follow the previous disposition." The magistrate was very angry at Shentong and said, "You speak out of sentiment, making me suffer punishment." He immediately ordered his attendants to take a piece of flesh and plug one of his ears, so he could no longer hear. Shentong pleaded, "I beg you to judge and submit again. If you do not agree, I will willingly accept the punishment again."

    63

    ”府君曰：“君为我去罪，即更与君一耳。”审通又判 曰：“天大地大，本以无亲；若使奉主，何由得一？苟欲因情变法，实将生伪丧 真。太古以前，人犹至朴，中古之降，方闻各亲。岂可使太古育物之心，生仲尼 观蜡之叹。无不亲，是非公也，何必引之。请宽逆耳之辜，敢荐沃心之药。庶其 阅实，用得平均。令狐寔等并请依正法。仍录状申天曹者。”黄衣人又持往，须 臾又有天符来曰：“再省所申，甚为允当。府君可加六天副正使，令狐寔、程翥 等并正法处置者。”府君悦，即谓审通曰：“非君不可以正此狱。”因命左右割 下耳中肉，令一小儿擘之为一耳，安于审通额上，曰：“塞君一耳，与君三耳， 何如？”又谓慎曰：“甚赖君荐贤以成我美，然不可久留君，当寿一周年相报耳。 君兼本寿，得二十一年矣。”即促送归家。

    Explanation

    63

    The magistrate said, "If you remove my sins, then give me one more chance." Shentong then ruled, "Heaven and earth are vast, but they are fundamentally impartial; if it is to serve the ruler, how could one achieve unity? If one wishes to change the law based on emotions, it will inevitably lead to falsehood and the loss of truth. Before the ancient times, people were still very simple; in the middle ages, one began to hear about various forms of kinship. How can one allow the ancient heart of nurturing all things to give rise to Confucius's sigh at the sacrificial ceremony? If there is no distinction in kinship, it is not fair or just; why should one follow it? Please forgive the offense of hearing unpleasant truths, and I dare to recommend a remedy for the heart. Perhaps by examining the facts, fairness can be achieved. I ask that Linghu Shi and others be dealt with according to the proper law. And record the case for submission to the heavenly court." A yellow-robed messenger took it away, and shortly thereafter another heavenly edict arrived, saying, "Upon reviewing what has been submitted, it is indeed appropriate. The magistrate can be appointed as a deputy to the Six Heavenly Officials. Linghu Shi, Cheng Zhu, and others will be dealt with according to the proper law." The magistrate was pleased and said to Shentong, "Without you, this case could not have been resolved." He then ordered his attendants to cut a piece of flesh from his own ear and had a small child divide it into one ear, which he placed on Shentong's forehead, saying, "I block one of your ears and give you three ears; how is that?" He also said to Shentong, "I greatly rely on your recommendation of worthy individuals to complete my good deeds, but I cannot keep you here for long; I will reward you with an additional year of life. You will live for twenty-one years in total." He then immediately sent him back home.

    64

    使者复以泥封二人，布囊各送至宅，欻如写出，而顾问妻子，妻子云：“君 亡精魂已十余日矣。”慎自此果二十一年而卒。审通数日额角痒，遂踊出一耳， 通前三耳，而踊出者尤聪。时人笑曰：“天有九头鸟，地有三耳秀才。”亦呼为 鸡冠秀才者。慎初见府君称邻，后方知倨乃邻家也。
    　　
    　　卷三
    　　
    　　○开元明皇幸广陵
    　　
    　　开元十八年正月望夕，帝谓叶仙师曰：“四方之盛，陈于此夕，师知何处极 丽？”对曰：“灯烛华丽，百戏陈设，士女争妍，粉黛相染，天下无逾于广陵矣。” 帝曰：“何术可使吾一观之？”师曰：“待御皆可，何独陛下乎。”俄而虹桥起 于殿前，板阁架虚，栏楯若画。师奏：“桥成，请行，但无回顾而已。”于是帝 步而上之，太真及侍臣高力士、黄幡绰、乐官数十人从行，步步渐高，若造云中。

    Explanation

    64

    The envoy sealed two people with clay and sent each in a cloth bag to their homes, as if suddenly written out. He then asked his wife, and she replied, "Your spirit has left for over ten days." Shen indeed died twenty-one years later. Shen Tong felt itching on his forehead for several days, and suddenly a new ear grew out, making him have three ears in total, with the new one being especially intelligent. People at the time laughed and said, "Heaven has a nine-headed bird, and earth has a three-eared scholar." They also called him the Scholar with a Chicken's Comb. Shen initially called the magistrate "neighbor," but later realized that Jù was his neighbor.

    Volume Three
    Chapter on Emperor Xuanzong's Visit to Guangling
    In the eighteenth year of the Kaiyuan era, on the night of the full moon in the first month, the emperor said to Leaf Master, "The grandeur of the four directions is displayed on this night. Teacher, do you know where it is most splendid?" The master replied, "The lights and candles are splendid, and various performances are set up. Men and women vie for beauty, their faces adorned with rouge and powder. There is none more splendid than Guangling in the world." The emperor asked, "What method can allow me to see it once?" The master said, "Anyone can wait for it, why only Your Majesty?" Suddenly, a rainbow bridge rose in front of the palace, its wooden pavilion built on empty space, its railings like paintings. The master said, "The bridge is ready, please go, but do not look back." Thus, the emperor stepped onto it, followed by Tai Zhen and the attendants, including Gao Lishi, Huang Fanchuo, and dozens of musicians. Step by step, they rose higher, as if ascending into the clouds.

    65

    俄顷之间，已到广陵矣。月色如昼，街陌绳直，寺观陈设之盛，灯火之光， 照灼台殿。士女华丽，若行化焉，而皆仰望曰：“仙人现于五色云中。”乃蹈舞 而拜，阗溢里巷。帝大悦焉，乃曰：“此真广陵也？”师曰：“请敕乐官奏《霓 裳羽衣》一曲，后可验矣。”于是作乐云中，瞻听之人，纷坛相蹈。曲终，帝意 将回，有顷之间，已到阙矣。帝极喜。
    　　
    　　人或谓仙师幻术造微，暂炫耳目。久之未决。后数旬，广陵奏云：“正月十 五日三更，有仙人乘彩云自西来，临孝感寺道场上，高数十丈。久之，又奏《霓 裳羽衣》一曲，曲终西去。官僚士女，无不具瞻。斯盖陛下孝诚感通，玄德昭著， 名应仙录，道冠帝图。不然，何以初元朝礼之晨而庆云现，小臣贱修之地而仙乐 陈。则垂衣裳者徒闻帝德，歌《南风》者才洽人心，岂与盛朝同日而语哉！”上 览表，大悦，方信师之不妄也。

    Explanation

    65

    In a moment, they had already arrived at Guangling. The moonlight was as bright as daylight, the streets as straight as a string, and the splendid arrangement of temples and observatories, with the lights shining brightly on the palaces and halls. The men and women were splendidly dressed, as if they were walking in a transformation, and all looked up and said, "The immortal appeared in a cloud of five colors." They then danced and bowed, and the streets were filled with people. The emperor was greatly pleased, and he said, "This is truly Guangling?" The teacher replied, "Please order the music officials to play the Nirvana Robe melody, which can be verified later." Then the music was made in the clouds, and the people who watched and listened were all over the place. When the music ended, the emperor's thoughts were about to return, and in a short while, they had already arrived at the palace gates. The emperor was extremely happy.

    Some people said the immortal teacher's magic was extremely subtle, temporarily dazzling the eyes and ears. For a long time, there was no decision. After several weeks, Guangling reported, "On the 15th day of the first month at midnight, there was an immortal riding a colorful cloud coming from the west, arriving at the Daoist platform of Xianggan Temple, towering tens of feet high. After a while, they played the Nirvana Robe melody again, and when the music ended, the immortal went west. Officials, gentlemen, and ladies all looked up. This is because Your Majesty's filial piety and sincerity have moved the heavens, and Your Majesty's virtuous nature is clearly evident. Your Majesty's name is recorded in the immortal books, and Your Majesty's virtue surpasses that of emperors. Otherwise, why would auspicious clouds appear in the morning of the first year's court ceremony, and why would immortal music be played in the humble abode of a lowly official? Those who wear robes only hear of Your Majesty's virtue, and those who sing the South Wind only touch people's hearts. How could they be compared to a prosperous dynasty?" The emperor read the report and was greatly pleased, and then believed the teacher was not lying.

    66

    ○袁洪儿夸郎
    　　
    　　陈朱崖太守袁洪儿，小名夸郎，年二十，生来性好书，乐静，别处一院，颇 能玄言。尝野见翠翠鸟，命罗得之。袁甚好玩，清夜月明，彻烛长吟：“露湿寒 塘草，月映清淮流。”忽失翠鸟所在，见一双鬟婢子立在其左，曰：“袁郎此篇 甚为佳妙，然未知我二十七郎封郎能押剧韵，人为三言四言句诗，一句开口，一 句合咏。春诗曰：‘花落也，蛱蝶舞，人何多疾，吁足忧苦。’如剧韵押法之者， 有一二百首，不能尽记得。

    Explanation

    66

    Governor Yuan Hong'er of Zhu Ya, nicknamed Kuanglang, was twenty years old. From birth, he had a fondness for books and enjoyed a quiet life. He lived in a separate courtyard and was quite capable of speaking in a profound manner. Once, while out in the wild, he saw a green bird and ordered it to be captured. Yuan greatly enjoyed this bird. On a clear night under the bright moon, he lit candles and recited poetry: "Dew wets the grass in the cold pond, the moon reflects on the clear river." Suddenly, he lost track of where the green bird was. He saw a pair of maidens with braided hair standing to his left and said, "This piece by Master Yuan is very excellent, but I wonder if my 27th son, Feng Lang, can handle the complex rhyming. People write three-character and four-character poetic lines, one line starting and one line ending. The spring poem says: 'Flowers fall, butterflies dance, why do people suffer so much, it's enough to cause worry and distress.' There are over a hundred such poems, but I cannot remember them all."

    67

    ”夸郎甚异之，曰：“汝是谁家青衣，乃得至此？且 汝封郎，吾可屈致之乎？”婢子曰：“某王家二十七娘子从嫁，本名翡翠，偶因 化身游行，使为袁郎子罗得。封郎去此不远，但具主人之礼，少顷封郎即至。” 夸郎乃命酒具茶器，未移时，翡翠至，曰：“封郎在门外。”出见一少年，可二 十余，言辞温雅，风流爽迈。揖让登席，讨论子史，自哺竟夕，宾主相得。夸郎 曰：“足下高居，当垂见喻。”封郎曰：“平仲来日当有蔬馔奉邀，然非仆本居， 赘于琅琊耳。”再三殷勤而别。

    Explanation

    67

    Kuāláng was greatly surprised by it and said, "Who is this young lady in service, and how did she come to be here? And you, Fēngláng, can I invite you here?" The servant girl replied, "I am the twenty-seventh daughter of a certain king, originally named Fěicuì. I was once transformed to travel and made to serve as the son of Yuánlángzǐ, Luódé." Kuāláng then said, "Fēngláng is not far from here. Just prepare the host's courtesy, and in a short while, Fēngláng will arrive immediately." Soon, Fěicuì arrived and said, "Fēngláng is at the door." Upon seeing a young man, about twenty years old, with gentle and refined speech and graceful and spirited demeanor, they bowed and yielded, sat down, discussed Confucian and historical texts, spent the entire day and night together, and got along well. Kuāláng said, "Since you reside in a high position, you should explain this to me." Fēngláng replied, "Píngzhòng will have vegetable dishes to invite you the next day, but I am not from my original residence; I am currently staying in Lángyá." They repeatedly bid farewell sincerely.

    68

    及明日辰后，有小童前拜曰：“封郎使归儿送书，令从二郎引路。”启书读 曰：“佳辰气茂，思得良会，驻足层台，企俟光仪，唯足下但东驰耳。”夸郎即 策马从之，可行十里，忽见泉石萦彻，异花骈植，宾馆宏敞，穷极瑰宝。门悬青 绡幕，下宛一尺余，皆爇兽炭。夸郎与封郎相见，方顾异之，平仲回叱一小童曰： “捧笔奴，早令汝煎火浣幕，何故客至犹未毕！”但令去火，而幕色尤鲜。坐未 几，又有四人出宅，皆风雅士也。封生曰：“主人王二兄、三兄、四兄、六郎子， 其名曰准、曰推、曰惟、曰淮。?

    Explanation

    68

    By the next day after noon, a little boy came forward to bow and say, "Lord Feng has sent me to deliver a letter, ordering Second Brother to lead the way." Opening the letter to read it, it said, "On a fine day with abundant vitality, I desire a good meeting. Standing on a high platform, I wait eagerly for your presence. Just ride eastward, my lord." Lord Kua immediately mounted his horse and followed. After traveling ten miles, he suddenly saw springs and stones winding through, strange flowers growing in pairs, and a guesthouse that was spacious and grand, filled with the most exquisite treasures. The door hung with green silk curtains, below which was about a foot thick, all heated with animal charcoal. Lord Kua met with Lord Feng and was just about to look at it in wonder. Pingzhong called back a little boy and said, "The servant who holds the brush, why didn't you have the fire-washed curtain ready? Why is it not finished when the guest arrives?" Just remove the fire, and the curtain color is even fresher. Not long after sitting, four more people came out of the house, all scholars of refined taste. Lord Feng said, "The host's Second Brother, Third Brother, Fourth Brother, and Sixth Son, their names are Quan, Tui, Wei, and Huai."

    69

    笨淅上嗉嚬淴掞鷩从辛斝嘁拢杂袪殊色，悉 衣珠翠，捧方丈盘至，珍羞万品，中有珍录，无不殚尽。王淮曰：“有少家乐， 请此奉娱。”即有女娃十余人并出，别有胡优，咬指翘足，一时拜员外，资次即 为给舍。淮指二妓曰：“石崇妾仙娥娘也，名称亚于绿珠。”于是丝竹并作，铿 锵清亮。日晚，王氏昆弟醉寝，封生谓夸郎曰：“此亦足为富贵，然丈人为太守， 当不以此盛。”夸郎曰：“不以鄙贱，百倍行采，不审何以致之？”封生曰： “君诚能结同心，仆便请为行人。拙室有姨，美淑善音，请袁君思之。”夸郎曰： “但恐龙门下难为鱼耳。”封生因入白王氏尊长，即出曰：“允矣！明日吉，便 为迎日。”夸郎大悦，许之。

    Explanation

    69

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, a woman from Luoyang was born with two heads and four arms. She was all dressed in pearls and jade, carrying a large tray filled with a myriad of delicacies, none of which were lacking. Wang Huai said, "There is some family entertainment; please enjoy this." Then, a group of young women and foreign entertainers performed a ritual or dance, bowing to the officials in a graceful manner. Wang Huai pointed to two courtesans and said, "They are the concubines of Shi Chong, known as Xian'e Nang, whose fame is second only to that of Lu Zhu." Then the string and wind instruments played together, sounding clear and resonant. By evening, the Wang brothers had drunk themselves to sleep. Feng Sheng said to Kua Lang, "This is also enough for wealth and honor, but since your father is the governor, it is not yet grand enough." Kua Lang said, "Not because of my lowly status, but how can I achieve it?" Feng Sheng said, "If you can truly unite in heart, I will ask to be your messenger. My humble home has an aunt who is beautiful, virtuous, and skilled in music. Please consider her, Mr. Yuan." Kua Lang said, "I am only afraid that it will be difficult to become a fish under the Dragon Gate." Feng Sheng then went inside to inform the respected elders of the Wang family, and upon returning, said, "It is agreed! Tomorrow is auspicious; it will be the day of the wedding." Kua Lang was greatly pleased and agreed.

    明日，王氏昆弟方陈设于堂下，茵榻帷帐，赫然炫目。及夸郎入，帘下有女 郎曰：“袁郎行动趋跄，犹似把书入学时。”又老青衣过，夸郎拜谢讫，目之。 即又笑曰：“禽霏□无乳久矣，袁郎何用目之！”将暮，傧来皆至，有青衣持笺 催妆诗，夸郎下笔赋诗曰：

    Explanation

    70

    The Next Day, the brothers of the Wang family had just set up the arrangements in the hall, with cushions, beds, and curtains, brightly dazzling the eyes. When the young man entered, a young woman under the curtain said, "Yuan Lang's movements are still as graceful as when he was carrying books to school." Another elderly servant passed by, and the young man bowed in thanks and looked at him. The servant then laughed and said, "It has been a long time since Qinfen has had milk, why does Yuan Lang look at it!" As dusk approached, all the attendants arrived, and a servant held a note with a poem to hurry the bridegroom. The young man then wrote a poem in response:

    Beautiful flowers naturally have the warmth of spring, not coinciding with the red makeup of the fair lady, disrupting her graceful form. If one uses the face powder of He Lang, one can borrow as much of his radiance as needed.

    The other auspicious rituals were all fully prepared. There were many poems, but not all of them can be remembered. Only the poem about the fan can be recalled:

    The round fan with a new square design, golden flowers illuminating the brocade mat. How can one see it under the lamp, even more so, encountering the person in the moonlight.

    The young man's wife is extraordinarily beautiful, surpassing the realm, with graceful and elegant manners. Her pet name is Congcong, and her formal name is Xie. The second wife or concubine is also similarly graceful and beautiful, quick-witted and good at joking, and gave a poem to Yuan Lang saying:

    71

    人家女美大须愁，往往丑郎门外求。
    　　
    　　昨日金刚脚下见，今朝何得此间游？
    　　
    　　及后，班坐桐阴，封平仲鼓琴，顾谓夸郎曰：“姨夫岂无一言相赠？”夸郎 即赋诗曰：
    　　
    　　宾匣开玉琴，高梧追烦暑。
    　　
    　　商弦一以发，白云飘然举。
    　　
    　　何必苍梧东，激琴怀怨浦。
    　　
    　　夸郎日恣余嗛，遂无归思。忽觉妻皆惨，又饰行装。夸郎问封生，封生曰： “丈人晋侍中王济也，久为阴道交州牧，近改并州刺史。若足下以贤尊在此，不 能俱往，则当从此有终天之别。”其妻呜咽流涕曰：“君本自殊途，不期与会， 致今日之别，亦封郎二兄之过。”遂闻外人呼声，走出，回顾已苍然不复见一物。 太守求不得已近一年，及至，数月犹恍，往往奔至前所，别无所见，复涕泣而退， 终岁乃如故。

    Explanation

    71

    A beautiful woman must often be worried, for she is frequently sought after by unattractive men outside her door.

    Yesterday, I encountered her at the feet of the Buddha statue; how could I have come to this place today?

    Later, we sat under the shade of a paulownia tree, and Feng Pingzhong played the qin. He turned to the arrogant man and said, "Uncle, do you have any words of advice for me?" The arrogant man immediately composed a poem:

    The guest opened the jade qin, and the tall paulownia tree chased away the heat.
    The qin strings played a piece of music, and the white clouds floated up.
    Why go to the east of Cangwu? Play the qin with a heart full of resentment.

    The arrogant man daily indulged in his conceit, thus he had no thoughts of returning. Suddenly, he felt his wife was sad, so he prepared his traveling clothes. The arrogant man asked Feng Pingzhong, who replied, "My father-in-law is Jin Shizhong Wang Ji, who has been the governor of Jiaozhou for a long time. Recently, he was appointed as the governor of Bingzhou. If you are here with your respected father-in-law, we cannot go together. Then we will have a final farewell here." His wife wept and said, "We were originally on different paths, and it was unexpected that we met. This separation today is also the fault of Feng Lang's second brother." Then he heard the calls of people outside. He went out, looked back, and found everything had turned gray and nothing was seen. The magistrate sought for him for nearly a year. When he arrived, for several months he was still dazed. Often, he rushed to the place where he met her, but saw nothing else. He cried and withdrew, finally returning to normal after a year.

    ○张左
    　　
    　　前进士张左，尝为叔父言：
    　　
    　　少年南次鄠杜，郊行，见有老父乘青驴，四足白，腰背鹿革囊，颜甚悦怿， 旨趣非凡。叟自斜径合路，左甚异之，试问所从来，叟但笑而不答。至于再三， 叟忽怒叱曰：“年少子，乃敢相逼！吾岂盗贼椎埋者耶？何必问所从来。”左逊 谢曰：“向慕先生高躅，愿从事左右耳，何赐深责？”叟曰：“吾无术教子，但 寿永者。子当嗤我潦倒，欲噱吾释志耳。”遂鞭乘促走，左亦扑马趋，俱至逆旅。 叟枕鹿囊，寝未熟，左方疲倦，取酒将饮，就请曰：“箪醪期先生共之。”叟跳 起曰：“此正吾所好，何子解吾意？”饮讫，左觇其色悦，徐请曰：“小生寡味， 愿先生赐言以广闻见，然非所敢望。”叟曰：“吾所见梁陈隋唐耳，贤愚治乱， 国史已具。然请以身所录者语子。”

    Explanation

    72

    A Former Candidate Zhang Zuo

    Zhang Zuo, a former candidate for the imperial examinations, once told his uncle:

    When I was young and traveling south to the Hu Du region, I was walking in the outskirts when I saw an old man riding a green donkey. The donkey's four legs were white, and he had a bag made of deer skin on his back. His face was very joyful, and his demeanor was extraordinary. The old man came from a side path that met the main road. I was very surprised by him and asked where he had come from. The old man just smiled and did not answer. After asking him repeatedly, the old man suddenly became angry and shouted, "Young man, how dare you press me! Am I a thief or a murderer? Why do you need to ask where I came from?" I apologized humbly, saying, "I admire the lofty conduct of a sage and wish to learn from you. Why do you blame me so severely?" The old man replied, "I have no skills to teach you, only the gift of longevity. You will probably mock my poverty and want to laugh at my aspirations." He then whipped his donkey and hurried away, and I also spurred my horse to follow, and we both arrived at an inn. The old man lay down with his deer skin bag as a pillow and had not yet fallen asleep. I was very tired and took out wine to drink, and I invited him, saying, "Let us share this small amount of wine together." The old man jumped up and said, "This is exactly what I like, how did you understand my meaning?" After drinking, I noticed that his face was very pleased. I then politely asked, "I have little taste, I wish for the teacher to impart words to broaden my knowledge and vision, but I dare not hope for much." The old man said, "What I have seen is the Liang, Chen, Sui, and Tang dynasties. The wise and foolish, the well-governed and chaotic, are all recorded in the national history. However, let me tell you what I have personally recorded."

    73

    吾宇文周时居岐，扶风人也，姓申名宗，慕齐神武，因改为欢。十八，从燕 公于谨征梁元帝于荆州，陷大将军。旋梦青衣二人谓余曰：“吕走天年，人向主 寿。”既觉，吾乃诣占梦者于江陵市，占梦者谓余曰：“吕走，回字也。人向主， 住字也。岂子住乃寿也。”时留兵于江陵，吾遂陈情于校尉托跋烈，许之。

    Explanation

    73

    When I lived in Qi during the Yuwen Zhou period, I was a native of Fufeng, with the surname Shen and given name Zong. I admired the martial prowess of Qi Shen Wu and therefore changed my name to Huan. At eighteen, I followed General Yan Gong Yu Jin in his campaign against Emperor Yuan of Liang in Jingzhou, where I was captured by a great general. Soon after, I dreamed of two men in blue robes who said to me, “Lü goes the natural lifespan; people face the master of longevity.” After waking, I went to a dream interpreter in the market of Jiangling. The dream interpreter said to me, “‘Lü goes’ is the character for ‘return,’ and ‘people face the master’ is the character for ‘stay.’ Does this mean that you will live long if you stay?” At that time, troops were stationed in Jiangling, and I then submitted my petition to the military officer Tuoba Lie, who agreed.

    因却诣占梦者曰：“住即合矣，寿有术乎？”占者曰：“汝生前梓潼薛君曹 也，好服木蕊散，多寻异书，日诵黄老一百纸，徙居鹤鸣山下，草堂三间，户外 骈植花竹，泉石萦绕。”八月十五日，长啸独饮，因酒酣畅，大言曰：“薛君曹 疏澹若此，何无异人降止？”忽觉两耳中有车马声，因颓然思寝，才至席，遂有 小车，朱轮青盖，驾赤犊出耳中，各高二三寸，亦不知出耳之难。车有二童，绿 帻青帔，亦长二三寸，凭轼呼御者，踏轮扶下，而谓君曹曰：“吾自兜玄国来， 向闻长啸月下，韵甚清激，私心奉慕，愿接清论。?本翙艽蠛霑唬骸熬薁出吾 耳，何谓兜玄国来？”二童子曰：“兜玄国在吾耳中，君耳安能处我？”君曹曰： “君长二三寸，岂复耳有国土！倘若有之，国人当尽焦螟耳。”二童曰：“胡为 其然！吾国与汝国无异，不信，盍从吾游。或能使留，则君无生死苦矣。

    Then he went to consult a dream interpreter and said, "If you stay, everything will be fine, but is there a method to prolong life?" The dream interpreter replied, "You were previously the man named Xue Juncao from Zitong. You enjoyed taking the wood essence powder, often sought out unusual books, and daily recited a hundred sheets of Huang-Lao. You moved to live at the foot of Crane Chirping Mountain, where you had a thatched cottage with three rooms. In front of the house, flowers and bamboo were planted in rows, and the area was surrounded by springs and stones."

    On the 15th day of the 8th lunar month, Xue Juncao sang loudly and drank alone. As he became drunk and cheerful, he said aloud, "Xue Juncao is so reclusive and indifferent. Why hasn't any extraordinary person come to visit?" Suddenly, he heard the sound of carriages and horses in his ears. He then leaned back and thought of sleeping. As soon as he reached his mat, a small carriage appeared. The carriage had a red wheel and a green canopy, driven by red calves, each about two or three inches tall. He did not know how difficult it was for them to come out of his ear.

    There were two children in the carriage, wearing green headbands and blue cloaks, also about two or three inches tall. They leaned on the carriage's front rail, called the driver, stepped on the wheel, and helped Xue Juncao down. They said to him, "We have come from the Land of Douchuan. We heard you singing loudly under the moon, and the tone was very clear and piercing. We privately admire and respect you and wish to engage in a clear and profound discussion."

    Xue Juncao said, "How can there be a country inside my ear, and how can the people of that country all be tiny insects?" The children replied, "Why is that so? Our country is no different from yours. If you don't believe us, why not come with us on a journey? Perhaps we can make you stay, and then you would no longer suffer from the pain of birth and death."

    The soothsayer further said, "In my previous life, I was a child emerging from your ear.     ○Xiao Zhizhong

    During the reign of the Tang Dynasty, Xiao Zhizhong, the Grand Secretary, was the Governor of Jizhou in the first year of Jingyun. He planned to hunt on the day of the winter solstice and set up traps for a grand occasion.

    78

    先一日，有薪者樵于霍山，暴疟不能归，因止岩穴之中，呻吟不寐。夜将艾， 似闻悉窣有人声。初以为盗贼将至，则匍匐于林木中。时山月甚明，有一人身长 丈余，鼻有三角，体被豹鞟，目闪闪如电，向谷长啸。俄有虎、兕、鹿、豕、 狐、兔、雉、雁骈匝百许步。长人即宣言曰：“余玄冥使者，奉北帝之命，明日 腊日，萧使君当顺时畋腊。尔等若干合箭死，若干合枪死，若干合网死，若干合 棒死，若干合狗死，若干合鹰死。”言讫，群兽皆俯伏战惧，若请命者。老虎洎 老麋，皆屈膝向长人言曰：“以某等之命，即实以分。然萧公仁者，非意欲害物， 以行时令耳。若有少故则止。使者岂无术救某等乎？”使者曰：“非余欲杀汝辈， 但今自以帝命宣示汝等刑名，即余使乎之事毕矣，自此任尔自为计。然余闻东谷 严四兄善谋，尔等可就彼祈求。”群兽皆轮转欢叫。使者即东行，群兽毕从。

    78

    The day before, a woodcutter was chopping wood in Huoshan when he contracted malaria and could not return home. He therefore took refuge in a cave, moaning and unable to sleep. As night was ending, he seemed to hear a rustling sound of human voices. At first, he thought bandits were approaching, so he crawled into the woods. The mountain moon was very bright, and there was a man over ten feet tall with three horns on his nose, clothed in a leopard skin, whose eyes flashed like lightning. He roared towards the valley. Soon, there were tigers, rhinos, deer, pigs, foxes, rabbits, pheasants, and geese gathered around for about a hundred steps. The tall man then declared, "I am the messenger of Xuanming, carrying out the order of the Northern Emperor. Tomorrow is the day of the winter solstice, and Xiao the magistrate will follow the season to hunt and sacrifice. You will die by arrows, spears, nets, clubs, dogs, and eagles." After speaking, the animals all cowered in fear, as if pleading for mercy. The tiger and the old elk both bowed their knees and spoke to the tall man, saying, "Our lives are at your disposal. However, Xiao the magistrate is kind-hearted and does not intend to harm creatures; he is simply following the seasonal command. If there is a slight reason, then it will stop. Does the messenger have no way to save us?" The messenger replied, "It is not my intention to kill you; I am merely fulfilling the divine command by announcing your fates. From now on, you must fend for yourselves. However, I have heard that Elder Yan in Eastern Valley is good at strategy; you may seek his help." The animals all rejoiced and called out. The messenger then headed east, and the animals followed him.

He wrote on the north wall: "Below the dark, eight hundred billion cycles of the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches, Master Dan Fei, Yan Hanzi, exiled to the middle heaven, covered in speckled fur, sixty cycles of the Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches, eating blood and drinking from streams, among apes, descending to the impure world, in the first year of Jingyun, ascending to Taiyi."

    时薪者素晓书诵，因密记得之。少顷，老狐负美女至，才及笄岁，红袂拭目， 残妆妖媚。又有一狐负美酒二瓶，香气酷烈。严四兄即以美女洎美酒瓶，各纳一 囊中，以朱书二符，取水噀之，二符即飞去。
    　　
    　　薪者惧且为所见，即寻路却回。未明，风雪暴至，竟日乃罢，而萧使君不复 猎矣。
    　　
    　　○李汭言
    　　
    　　汉中从事李汭言：
    　　
    　　天宝中有士人崔姓者，尉于巴蜀，才至成都而卒。时连帅章仇兼琼哀其妻少 而无投止，因与青城山下置一别墅。又以其色美，欲聘纳之，计无所出，谓其夫 人曰：“贵为诸侯妻，何不盛为盘筵，邀召女客，五百里内，尽可迎致。”夫人 甚悦。兼琼因命衙官遍报五百里内女郎，即日会成都，意欲因会便留亡尉妻，不 谓已为族舅卢生纳之矣。卢舅密知兼琼意，令尉妻辞疾不行，兼琼大怒，促左右 百骑往收捕。

    Explanation

    81

    A Person Who Earns by the Hour

    A person who earns by the hour, having always been skilled in reciting books, secretly memorized something. Shortly afterward, an old fox carried a beautiful woman, who was just coming of age, her red sleeves wiping her eyes, her makeup unfinished and charmingly seductive. Another fox carried two bottles of fine wine, their aroma strong and pungent. The person named Yan Si, then placed the woman and the wine bottles into separate bags, wrote two red talismans, sprinkled water on them, and the talismans flew away.

    Fearing that he would be seen, the person quickly found a way to return. Before dawn, a violent storm arrived, lasting all day, and as a result, the magistrate no longer went hunting.

    ○ Li Ruiyan

    Li Ruiyan, an official from Hanzhong, said:

    During the Tianbao era, there was a scholar surnamed Cui who served as a military officer in Bashu. He died shortly after arriving in Chengdu. At the time, the governor, Zhang Qiu Jinqiong, felt pity for his young widow, who had no place to go, and so provided her with a summer house in Qingcheng Mountain. Additionally, because of her beauty, he considered marrying her but had no plan, so he told his wife, "As a wife of a feudal lord, why not host a grand banquet and invite female guests from within a 500-li radius? All of them can be invited." The wife was very pleased. The governor then ordered his officials to invite all the women within 500 li to gather in Chengdu the same day, intending to keep the widow during the gathering, but he did not know that she had already been married to his cousin-in-law, Lu Sheng. Lu Sheng, knowing the governor's intentions, had the widow feign illness and not attend, which greatly angered the governor, who then ordered his attendants to capture her.

    82

    卢舅时方食，兵骑绕宅亦合，卢谈笑自若，殊不介怀，食讫，谓尉 妻曰：“兼琼之意可知矣，夫人不可不行。少顷即当送素色衣服来，便可服之而 往。”言讫，乘驴出门，兵骑前揽不得，徐徐而去，追不及矣。俄使一小童捧箱， 内有故青裙、白衫子，绿帔子、绯罗縠绡素，皆非世人之所有。尉妻服之至成都， 诸女郎皆先期而至，兼琼觇于帷下。及尉妻入，光彩绕身，美色旁射，不可正视， 坐皆慑气，不觉起拜。食归，三日而卒，红坏立尽。

    Explanation

    82

    Lu's uncle was just finishing his meal when soldiers and cavalry surrounded the house. Lu remained calm and composed, laughing and talking as usual, and was not at all concerned. After finishing his meal, he told the wife of the magistrate, "The intentions of Jianqiong are known. The lady cannot avoid going. In a short while, they will send white-colored clothes. You may wear them and go." After finishing his words, he rode a donkey out. The soldiers and cavalry tried to grab him but could not. He left slowly, and they could not catch up. Soon, he sent a young boy to carry a box, inside which were old blue skirts, white shirts, green cloaks, and red silk gauze. All of these were not things that ordinary people possessed. The wife of the magistrate wore them and went to Chengdu. All the young ladies arrived ahead of time, and Jianqiong peeped from behind the curtain. When the wife of the magistrate entered, radiant light surrounded her, her beauty shone out, and it was too dazzling to look directly at. Everyone present was awestruck and involuntarily stood up to bow. She returned home to eat and died three days later, with the red color fading away immediately.

    83

    兼琼大骇，具状录奏闻。帝问张果，果云：“知之，不敢言。请问青城王老。” 帝即召兼琼求访王老进之。兼琼搜索青城山前后，并无此人。惟草市药肆云： “常有二人日来买山药，称王老所使。”二人至，兼琼即令衙官随访。入山数里， 至一草堂，王老皤然鬓发，隐几危坐。衙官随入，遂宣诏，兼致兼琼意。王老曰： “此必多言小子张果也。”因与兼琼克期至京师，令先发表，不肯乘传，兼琼从 之。使才至银台，王老亦到。帝召问，张果犹在席侧，见王老，惶恐再拜。王老 叱果曰：“小子何不言之！又遣远取吾来。”果言：“小仙不敢，专俟仙伯言耳。” 因奏曰：“卢二舅即太元夫人库子，因假下游，以亡尉妻微有仙骨，故纳为媵。 无何，盗太元夫人衣服与着，已受谪至重，为郁单天子矣。亡尉妻以衣太元夫人 衣服，堕无间狱矣。”奏讫，苦不愿留，帝放还，出后不知所在。

    Explanation

    83

    Jianshao was greatly alarmed and prepared a report, which he submitted to the emperor. The emperor asked Zhang Guo, who replied, "I know about it, but I dare not speak. Please ask the old man of Qingcheng." The emperor immediately summoned Jianshao and requested him to find the old man of Qingcheng and bring him to the capital. Jianshao searched the areas around Qingcheng Mountain but found no trace of him. Only a pharmacist at a grass market said, "There are usually two men who come every day to buy yam, claiming they are sent by the old man." When these two men arrived, Jianshao ordered an official to follow them. They entered the mountain for several miles and came to a thatched cottage where the old man of Qingcheng sat upright with white hair, resting his head on a table. The official followed in and then announced the imperial edict, conveying Jianshao's intentions. The old man of Qingcheng said, "This must be the talkative little Zhang Guo." He then agreed to a specific time to arrive in the capital and ordered the report to be published first, refusing to travel by official carriage, and Jianshao followed his wishes. The envoy arrived at the Silver Pavilion, and the old man of Qingcheng also arrived. The emperor summoned them, and Zhang Guo was still standing by the side of the seat. Seeing the old man, he was shocked and bowed twice. The old man of Qingcheng scolded Zhang Guo, saying, "Why didn't you speak up! You sent someone far away to fetch me." Zhang Guo replied, "The little immortal dares not, waiting only for the words of the immortal elder." He then reported, "Lu Er's second uncle is the servant of the Lady Taiyuan, who went down to play and took his deceased magistrate's wife, who had a bit of immortal bone, as a concubine. Soon after, she stole the clothes of Lady Taiyuan and wore them, and has already been severely punished, becoming the ruler of the Pure Abodes Heaven. The deceased magistrate's wife, by wearing the clothes of Lady Taiyuan, has fallen into the realm of eternal punishment." After the report, the old man of Qingcheng strongly refused to stay, and the emperor allowed him to return. After leaving, no one knew where he was.

    ○南缵
    　　
    　　广汉守南缵尝为人言：
    　　
    　　至德中有调选得同州督邮者，姓崔，忘名字，轻骑赴任。出春明门，见一青 袍人乘马出，亦不知其姓字，因相揖偕行。徐问何官，青袍人云：“新授同州督 邮。”崔云：“某新授此官，君岂不错误乎？”青袍人笑而不答。又相与行，悉 云赴任。去同州数十里，于斜路中，有官吏拜迎。青袍入谓崔君曰：“君为阳道 录事，某为阴道录事。路从此别，岂不相送耶？”崔生录之，即与连辔入斜路， 遂至一城郭，街衢局署，亦甚壮丽。

    Explanation

    84

    Governor Nan Zuan of Guanghan once told someone:

    During the era of great virtue, there was someone selected to be the supervisor of Tongzhou. His surname was Cui, but his name is forgotten. He rode a light horse to take up his post. As he went out through the Chunming Gate, he saw a man in a green robe riding a horse out. He did not know the man's name, so they bowed to each other and walked together. Slowly, he asked what the man's position was. The man in the green robe said, "I have just been appointed as the supervisor of Tongzhou." Cui said, "I have just been appointed to this position, are you not mistaken?" The man in the green robe smiled and did not answer. They continued walking together, and both said they were going to take up their posts. After traveling dozens of miles from Tongzhou, on a side path, officials came to greet them. The man in the green robe entered and said to Cui, "You are the officer of the yang aspect, and I am the officer of the yin aspect. Our paths diverge from here, should we not bid farewell?" Cui recorded this and immediately rode alongside the man in the green robe into the side path, and they eventually arrived at a city. The streets and government offices were also very grand and magnificent.

    85

    青袍人至厅，与崔生同坐受谒，通胥徒、僧道等讫，次通辞讼狱囚，崔之妻 与焉。崔生大惊，谓青袍人曰：“不知拙室何得至此？”青袍人即避大案后，令 崔生自与妻言。妻云：“被迫至此，已是数日，君宜哀请录事耳。”崔生即祈求 青袍人，青袍人因令胥吏促放崔生妻令回。崔生试问妻犯何罪至此，青袍人曰： “君寄家同州，应同州亡人，皆在此厅勘过。盖君管阳道，某管阴道。”崔生淹 留半日，即请却回。青袍人令胥吏拜送，曰：“虽阴阳有殊，然具是同州也，可 不拜送督邮哉！”青袍人亦偕饯送，再三勤款，挥袂，又令斜路口而去。
    　　
    　　崔生至同州，问妻子，妻子云：“病七八日，冥然无知，神不识生，愈才得 一日。”崔生计之，恰放回日也。妻不记阴道见崔生时，崔生言之，妻始悟如梦， 亦不审记也。

    Explanation

    85

    The green-robed official arrived at the hall and sat down with Cui Sheng to receive an audience. After announcing the presence of clerks, monks, and Taoists, he proceeded to handle litigants and prisoners, including Cui Sheng's wife. Cui Sheng was greatly surprised and asked the official, "How did my humble wife come to be here?" The official stepped back behind the large desk and instructed Cui Sheng to speak with his wife himself. The wife replied, "I was forced to come here and have been here for several days. You should plead with the recorder on my behalf." Cui Sheng immediately begged the official, who then ordered the clerk to hasten the release of Cui Sheng's wife. Cui Sheng asked his wife what crime she had committed to be brought here, and the official explained, "You left your family in Tongzhou. All the deceased from Tongzhou have been examined here. I am in charge of the Yangdao, and I am in charge of the Yindao." Cui Sheng stayed for half a day and then requested to return. The official ordered the clerk to see him off, saying, "Although there is a difference between Yang and Yin, we are both from Tongzhou. How can we not bid farewell to the local official?" The official also accompanied them to see them off, offering repeated hospitality, and waved his sleeves, instructing them to go down a side road.

    When Cui Sheng arrived in Tongzhou and asked his wife about her condition, she said, "I have been ill for seven or eight days, unconscious and unaware, with my spirit not recognizing the living. I only recovered a day ago." Cui Sheng calculated that it was the same day she was released. His wife did not remember seeing Cui Sheng in the Yindao, but when Cui Sheng mentioned it, she began to realize it was like a dream and did not clearly remember it either.

    86

    ○侯遹
    　　
    　　隋开皇初，广都孝廉侯遹入城，至剑门外，忽见四黄石，皆大如斗。遹爱之， 收藏于笼，负之以驴，因歇鞍取看，皆化为金。遹至城货之，得钱百万，市美妾 十余人，大开第宅，近甸良田别墅，货买甚多。
    　　
    　　后乘春景出游，尽载妓妾随从，下车陈设酒肴。忽有一老翁，负大笈至，厕 下坐。遹怒诟之，命苍头扶出，叟不动亦不嗔恚，但引满杯啖炙而笑云：“吾此 来求君偿债耳。君昔将我金去，不忆记乎？”尽取遹妓妾十余人，投之于笈，亦 不觉笈中之窄，负之而趋，走若飞鸟。遹令苍头驰马逐之，斯须已失所在。自后 遹家日贫，却复昔日生计。十余年，却归蜀，到剑门，又见前者老翁，携所将妓 妾游行，傧从极多，见遹皆大笑。问之不言，逼之又失所在。访剑门前后，并无 此人，竟不能测也。
    　　
    　　○巴邛人

    Explanation

    86

    In the early years of the Kaihuang era of the Sui Dynasty, Hou Yu, a filial and honest official from Guangdu, entered the city and reached the outskirts of the Jiemeng Pass. Suddenly, he saw four yellow stones, all as large as a dou. Hou Yu loved them and collected them in a cage, carrying them on a donkey. He stopped to rest and looked at them, and they all turned into gold. Hou Yu sold the gold in the city and made a million coins, buying more than ten beautiful concubines, building a large mansion, and purchasing nearby good farmland and villas.

    Later, he went out for a spring outing, loading all his concubines and maidservants to follow. He got off the carriage and set up wine and food. Suddenly, an old man appeared, carrying a large bag and sitting down. Hou Yu became angry and scolded him, ordering the servants to escort him out. The old man did not move and was not angry, but instead took a full cup, ate roasted meat, and laughed, saying, "I came here to demand repayment of a debt from you. Do you not remember when you took my gold?" The old man then took more than ten of Hou Yu's concubines and threw them into his bag, which did not seem narrow at all. He carried them away, running like a bird. Hou Yu ordered the servants to chase him on horseback, but soon the old man disappeared.

    After that, Hou Yu's family gradually became poor, returning to their former circumstances. Ten years later, he returned to Sichuan and reached the Jiemeng Pass. He saw the old man from before, who was traveling with the concubines he had taken, accompanied by many attendants. When they saw Hou Yu, they all laughed. Hou Yu asked them, but they did not respond. When he pressured them, they disappeared again. He visited the area around the Jiemeng Pass, but there was no one like him, and he could not understand or measure what had happened.

    ○巴邛人

    In Baqing, there was a man who, after drinking a cup of wine, suddenly transformed into a bird and flew away. The people of Baqing were amazed and followed him, but they could not catch him. He flew to a distant mountain and disappeared. The people of Baqing never saw him again.

    87

    有巴邛人，不知姓名，家有桔园。因霜后，诸桔尽收，余有两大桔，如三斗 盎。巴人录之，即令攀摘，轻重亦如常桔。剖开，每桔有二老叟，鬓眉皤然，肌 体红润，皆相对象戏，身长尺余，谈笑自若，剖开后亦不惊怖，但相与决赌。决 赌讫，一叟曰：“君输我海上龙王第七女须发十两，智琼额黄十二枝，紫绢帔一 副，绛台山霞宝散二庾，瀛洲玉尘九斛，阿母疗髓凝酒四钟，阿母女态盈娘子跻 虚龙缟袜八纟两，后日于王先生青城草堂还我耳。”又有一叟曰：“王先生许来， 竟待不得，桔中之乐，不减商山，但不得深根固蒂，为愚人摘下耳。”又一叟曰： “仆饥矣，须龙根脯食之。”即于袖中抽出一草根，方圆径寸，形状宛转如龙， 毫厘罔不周悉，因削食之，随削随满。食讫，以水噀之，化为一龙，四叟共乘 之，足下泄泄云起。须叟，风雨晦冥，不知所在。巴人相传云：百五十年来如此， 似在陈隋之间，但不知的年号耳。

    Explanation

    87

    A Man from Ba and Qiong

    There was a man from Ba and Qiong, whose name is unknown, who had an orange grove. After the frost, all the oranges were harvested, leaving two large oranges, each as big as a three-dou bowl. The people of Ba recorded this, and they were instructed to climb and pick the oranges, which were as heavy as ordinary oranges. When cut open, each orange contained two old men, with white hair and eyebrows, rosy and smooth skin, who all playfully interacted with each other, each about a foot long, chatting and laughing naturally. They were not frightened after being cut open, but they only gambled with each other. After the gambling, one old man said, "You owe me ten taels of the seventh daughter of the Dragon King of the Sea's hair, twelve strands of Zhijiong's forehead yellow, a purple silk shawl, two庾of the precious powder from the Red Platform Mountain, nine斛of the jade dust from Yingzhou, four zhou of the bone-marrow curing wine from Mother, and eight两of the dragon silk stockings from Mother's daughter Tai Ying. You will return them to me at Mr. Wang's Qingcheng Hermitage in the future." Another old man said, "Mr. Wang promised to come, but he never arrived. The joy in the orange is no less than in Shangshan, but they cannot have deep roots and a strong stem, as they are picked by foolish people." Another old man said, "I am hungry, and I need to eat the dragon root meat." He immediately pulled out a grass root from his sleeve, one inch in diameter, shaped like a dragon, with every detail perfect. He cut and ate it, and it refilled as he cut. After eating, he spat water on it, and it turned into a dragon. The four old men rode it together, and clouds rose under their feet. Soon, there was wind, rain, and darkness, and they disappeared. The people of Ba say that it has been like this for over a hundred and fifty years, and it seems to have occurred during the Chen and Sui dynasties, but the exact year is unknown.

    88

    ○刘法师
    　　
    　　贞元中，华州云台观有刘法师者，炼气绝粒，迨二十年。每三元设斋，则见 一人，衣缝掖而面黧瘦，来居末座，斋毕而去，如此者十余年，而衣服颜色不改。 法师异而问之，对曰：“余姓张名公弼，住莲花峰东隅。”法师意此处无人之境， 请同往。公弼怡然许之，曰：“此中甚乐，师能便往，亦当无闷。”
    　　
    　　法师遂随公弼行，三二十里，援萝攀葛，才有鸟道，经过崖谷险绝，虽猿狖 不能过也，而公弼履之若夷途，法师从行亦无难。遂至一石壁，削成，高直千余 仞，下临无底之谷。一迳阔数寸，法师与公弼侧足而立。公弼乃以指扣石壁，中 有人问曰：“为谁？”曰：“某。”遂划然开一门，门中有天地日月。公弼将入， 法师随公弼亦入，其人乃怒谓公弼：“何引外人来？”其人因阖门，则又成石壁 矣。

    Explanation

    88

    During the reign of Emperor Dezong in the Tang Dynasty, there was a Daoist priest named Liu at the Yuntai Temple in Huazhou. He had been cultivating qi and abstaining from food for nearly twenty years. Every time the three major festivals arrived and rituals were performed, Liu would see a man dressed in simple robes with a dark, emaciated appearance. This man would sit in the last seat during the rituals and leave after they concluded. This happened for over ten years, and the man's clothes and complexion never changed. The priest found this strange and asked him, "What is your name?" The man replied, "My name is Zhang Gongbi, and I live on the eastern slope of Lotus Peak." Liu thought that this place was a remote and uninhabited area and asked Zhang if he could accompany him. Zhang agreed happily and said, "This place is very pleasant. If you can come here, you will also find no boredom."

    Liu then followed Zhang as they traveled for about thirty to forty miles, climbing through dense vegetation where only birds could pass. They passed through extremely dangerous cliffs and valleys, places even apes and monkeys could not cross, but Zhang walked through them as if they were flat roads, and Liu followed without difficulty. They eventually reached a sheer cliff, standing over a thousand feet high, overlooking a bottomless valley below. A narrow path, only a few inches wide, led to a spot where Liu and Zhang stood sideways. Zhang then tapped the stone wall with his finger, and someone inside asked, "Who is it?" Zhang replied, "It's me." Suddenly, the wall opened, revealing a door with its own sky, earth, sun, and moon. As Zhang was about to enter, Liu followed him, and the person inside angrily said to Zhang, "Why have you brought outsiders here?" The person then closed the door, and it reverted to a solid stone wall.

    89

    公弼曰：“此非他，乃云台刘法师也，余交战，故请来此，何见拒之深也？” 又开门，内公弼及法师，公弼曰：“法师此来甚饥，君可丰食遣之。”其人遂问 法师：“便能住否？”法师请以后期。其人遂取一盂水，以肘后青囊中刀圭粉糁 之以饮法师，味甚甘香，饮毕而饥渴之想除矣。公弼曰：“余昨云山中甚乐，君 盍为戏，令法师观之。”其人乃以水噀东谷中，乃有苍龙白象各一，对舞，舞 甚妙，威凤彩鸾各一对歌，歌甚清。顷之，公弼送法师回，回顾，惟见青崖丹壑， 向之歌舞，一无所见矣。及去观将近，公弼乃辞。

    Explanation

    89

    Gong Bi said, "This is not someone else; it is the Daoist Master Liu of Yun Tai. I was engaged in battle, so I asked to come here. Why are you rejecting me so deeply?" He then opened the door and let Gong Bi and the Daoist Master in. Gong Bi said, "The Daoist Master has come here very hungry; you may give him a generous meal." The person then asked the Daoist Master, "Can you stay here?" The Daoist Master requested to stay for a later time. The person then took a bowl of water and sprinkled a small amount of powder from a green bag behind his elbow to drink to the Daoist Master. The taste was very sweet and fragrant, and after drinking, the thoughts of hunger and thirst were dispelled. Gong Bi said, "I said yesterday that the mountain was very enjoyable; why don't you perform a play, so the Daoist Master can watch?" The person then sprayed water into the eastern valley, and there appeared one blue dragon and one white elephant, dancing together, with their dance being very wonderful. There were also pairs of majestic phoenixes and colorful cranes singing, with their songs being very clear. After a while, Gong Bi sent the Daoist Master back, and when he looked back, he only saw green cliffs and red ravines, and the previous dancing and singing were no longer visible. As they were about to leave, Gong Bi bid farewell.

    90

    法师至观，处置事毕，却寻公弼，则步步险阻，杳不可阶，痛恨前者不住， 号天叫地，遂成腰疾。公弼更不复至矣。
    　　
    　　昭应县尉薛公幹为僧孺叔父言也。
    　　
    　　○刁俊朝
    　　
    　　安康伶人刁俊朝，其妻巴妪，项瘿者，初微若鸡卵，渐巨如三四升瓶盎。积 五年，大如数斛之囊，重不能行。其中有琴瑟笙磬埙篪之响。细而听之，若合音 律，泠泠可乐。积数年，瘿外生小穴如针芒者，不知几亿。每天欲雨，则穴中吹 白烟，霏霏如丝缕，渐高布散，结为屯云，雨则立降。其家少长惧之，咸请远送 岩穴。俊朝恋恋不能已，因谓妻曰：“吾迫以众议，将不能庇于伉俪。送君于无 人之境，如何？”妻曰：“吾此疾诚可憎恶，送之亦死，拆之亦死。君当为我决 拆之，看有何物。”俊朝即磨淬利刃，挥挑将及妻前，瘿中轩然有声，遂四分披 裂，有一大猱，跳走腾踏而去。即以帛絮裹之。虽瘿疾顿愈，而冥然大渐矣。

    Explanation

    90

    The monk arrived at the temple, handled all the affairs, and then went back to look for Gong Bi, but every step was fraught with danger, utterly unreachable. Regretting not stopping earlier, he cried out to the heavens and the earth, and thus developed a backache. Gong Bi no longer came.

    Zhao Ying County Magistrate Xue Gonggan spoke these words on behalf of his uncle Sengru.

    Diao Junzhao, a performer from Ankang, had a wife named Ba Yu, who suffered from a goiter. Initially, it was as small as a chicken egg, but gradually grew to the size of a jar or pot holding three to four sheng. After five years, it became as large as a bag holding several dou, so heavy that she could not move. Inside the goiter were sounds resembling those of zithers, flutes, bells, and pipes. When listened to carefully, they seemed to follow the rules of music, clear and pleasant. After several years, tiny holes formed on the surface of the goiter, likened to needles, with an unknown number. Before rain, white smoke would be emitted from these holes, rising and spreading, forming clouds, and rain would fall immediately. The family, young and old, feared this and all requested to send her far away to a cave. Junzhao was deeply attached and could not bear to part. He said to his wife, "I am pressured by public opinion, and I will not be able to protect you in marriage. To send you to a place where no one lives, what do you think?" She replied, "My disease is truly disgusting, whether sent away or removed, I will die. You should remove it for me, and see what is inside." Junzhao immediately sharpened a sharp knife and was about to cut into her when the goiter split into four pieces with a loud sound, revealing a large monkey that jumped away, running and jumping. He then wrapped it in cloth and cotton. Although the goiter disease was suddenly cured, she soon became very ill.

    91

    明日，有黄冠扣门曰：“吾乃昨日瘿中走出之猱也。吾本猕猴之精，解致风 雨。无何与汉江鬼愁潭老蛟还往，常与觇船。舸将至，俾他覆之，以求舟中，饣 侯粮，以养孙息。昨者太一诛蛟，搜索党与，故借君夫人蝤蛴之领，以匿性命。 虽分不相干，然为累亦甚矣。今于凤凰山神处求得少许灵膏，请君涂之，幸当立 愈。”俊朝如其言涂之，随手疮合。俊朝因留黄冠，烹鸡设食。食讫，贳酒欲饮， 黄冠因啭喉高歌。又为丝匏琼玉之音，罔不铿锵可爱。既而辞去，莫知所诣。时 大定中也。

    Explanation

    91

    The next day, a Taoist priest knocked on the door and said, "I am the monkey that came out of the goiter yesterday. I am originally a spirit of a macaque, capable of summoning wind and rain. I frequently interacted with the old dragon in the Ghost Sorrow Pool of the Han River, often observing boats. When a ship approached, I made it capsize to seek food from it to feed my descendants. Yesterday, the Supreme Being punished the dragon and searched for accomplices, so I borrowed the neck of your wife, the Qiuqi, to hide my life. Though we are not directly related, it has also been a great burden. Now I obtained a little bit of magical ointment from the god of Phoenix Mountain. Please apply it as instructed, and it should heal immediately." Junzhao applied it as instructed, and the wound healed immediately. Junzhao then kept the Taoist priest, cooked chicken, and set a meal. After eating, he bought wine to drink, and the Taoist priest then sang a high-pitched song, also playing sounds of silk, gourds, and jade, all resonant and lovely. Afterwards, he left, and no one knew where he went. It was during the Dading period.

    92

    ○古元之
    　　
    　　后魏尚书令古弼族子元之，少养于弼，因饮酒而卒。弼怜之特甚，三日殓毕， 追思，欲与再别。因命斫棺，开已却生矣。元之云：
    　　
    　　当昏醉时，忽然如梦。有人沃冷水于体，仰视，乃见一神人衣冠绛裳霓帔， 仪貌甚伟。顾元之曰：“吾乃古说也，是汝远祖。适欲至和神国中，无人担囊侍 从，因来取汝。”即令负一大囊，可重一钧。又与一竹杖，长丈二余。令元之乘 骑随后，飞举甚速，常在半天，西南行，不知里数，山河逾远，欻然下地，已至 和神国。其国无大山，高者不过数十丈，皆积碧珉。石际生青彩簵筿，异花 珍果。软草香媚，好禽嘲哳。山顶皆平正如砥，清泉迸下者三二百道。原野无凡 树，悉生百果及相思、石榴之辈。

    Explanation

    92

    Gu Yuanzhi, a descendant of Gu Bi, the Chancellor of the Later Wei Dynasty, was raised by Gu Bi from a young age. One day, he died from drinking. Gu Bi was extremely saddened and, after three days of burial rites, began to reflect on him, wishing to say goodbye again. He then ordered the coffin to be chopped open. When it was opened, Gu Yuanzhi had come back to life. Gu Yuanzhi said:

    "At the time of being drunk, I suddenly felt as if I was in a dream. Someone poured cold water on my body. Looking up, I saw a divine figure in red robes and a colorful cloak, with an imposing appearance. The figure looked at me and said, 'I am Gu Shuo, your distant ancestor. I just wanted to go to the land of peace and spirits, but there was no one to carry the bag or accompany me, so I came to take you.' He then ordered me to carry a large bag, weighing about one catty. He also gave me a bamboo staff, about twelve feet long, and told me to ride after him. We flew up very quickly, always in mid-air, traveling southwest, not knowing the distance. The mountains and rivers became more distant, and suddenly we landed on the ground, having arrived at the land of peace and spirits. This country has no big mountains; the highest ones are no more than several dozen zhang high, all covered with green jade. Green and colorful bamboo grows at the edges of the stones, with strange flowers and precious fruits. Soft grass with a fragrant and charming scent, and beautiful birds chirping and chattering. The tops of the mountains are flat like grindstones, with clear springs gushing down in three or four hundred streams. The plains have no ordinary trees, all growing a hundred kinds of fruits and things like the xiangsi tree and pomegranates."

    93

    每果树花卉俱发，实色鲜红，映翠叶于香丛之 上，纷错满树，四时不敢，唯一岁一度暗换花实，更生新嫩，人不知觉。田畴尽 长大瓠，瓠中实以五谷，甘香珍美，非中国稻粱可比，人得足食，不假耕种。原 隰滋茂，莸秽不生，一年一度，树木枝干间悉生五色丝纩。人得随色收取，任意 纟任织。异锦纤罗，不假蚕杼。四时之气，常熙熙和淑，如中国二三月。无蚊、 虻、蟆、蚁、虱、蜂、蝎、蛇、虺、守宫、娱蚣、蛛蠓之虫，又无枭、鸱、鸦、 鹞、鸲、鹆、蝙蝠之属，及无虎、狼、豺、豹、狐狸、蓦驳之兽，又无猫、鼠、 猪、犬扰害之类。其人长短妍蚩皆等，无有嗜欲爱憎之者。

    Explanation

    93

    Every tree and flower blooms together, with the fruit vividly red, reflecting on the green leaves among fragrant clusters, creating a colorful display on the trees. All seasons are not timid; only once a year, the flowers and fruits change subtly, and new, tender ones grow, but people do not notice. All fields are filled with large gourds, which are filled with five grains, sweet, fragrant, and precious, not comparable to the rice and grains of China. People have enough food, without the need for farming. The plains and lowlands are lush and abundant, with noxious weeds not growing. Between the branches and trunks of trees, all kinds of colored silk and cotton grow, and people can collect them according to color, and weave them at will. The fabrics are exotic, fine, and delicate, without the need for silkworms or looms. The four seasons' air is always warm and pleasant, like the air in China during February and March. There are no mosquitoes, flies, frogs, ants, lice, bees, scorpions, snakes, vipers, geckos, centipedes, or spiders. There are no owls, hawks, crows, falcons, sparrows, magpies, or bats. There are no tigers, wolves, jackals, leopards, foxes, or hyenas. There are no cats, mice, pigs, or dogs causing disturbance. The people are all of equal height and beauty, with no one having desires, love, or hatred.

    94

    人生二男二女，为邻 则世世为婚姻。笄年而嫁，二十而娶，人寿一百二十。中无夭折、疾病、瘖聋、 跛躄之患。百岁已下，皆自记忆；百岁已外，不知其寿几何。寿尽则欻然失其所 在，虽亲族子孙皆忘其人，故常无忧戚。每日午时一餐，中间唯食酒浆果实耳。 餐亦不知所化，不置溷所。人无私积囷仓，余粮栖亩，要者取之。无灌园鬻蔬， 野菜皆足人食。十亩有一酒泉，味甘而香。国人日相携游览歌咏，陶陶然，暮夜 而散，未尝昏醉。人人有俾仆，皆自然谨慎，知人所要，不烦促使。随意屋室， 靡不壮丽。

    Explanation

    94

    In this society, every household has two sons and two daughters. Being neighbors leads to generations of intermarriage. Girls come of age at 15 and marry, while men marry at 20. People live to be 120 years old, free from premature death, illness, deafness, muteness, or lameness. Those under 100 years old have perfect memory, but those over 100 lose track of their age. When life ends, one disappears suddenly without trace, and even close relatives and descendants forget the deceased. They eat one meal a day at noon, consisting mainly of wine, fruit juice, and fruits. The food is not digested in the usual sense, and there is no need for a toilet. There is no private storage of grain; surplus grain is left in the fields for those who need it. There is no market for vegetables; wild plants are sufficient for food. Every ten acres has a spring of wine that is sweet and fragrant. Citizens gather daily to stroll, sing, and enjoy themselves, dispersing at dusk without ever getting drunk. Each person has a servant who is naturally cautious and anticipates their needs without being told. Houses are built according to one's will, all of which are magnificent.

    95

    其国六畜唯有马，驯极而骏，不用刍秣，自食野草，不近积聚。人要 乘则乘，乘讫而却放。亦无主守。其国千官皆足，而仕官不自知身之在仕，杂于 下人，以无职事操断也。虽有君主，而君不自知为君，杂于千官，以无职事升贬 故也。又无迅雷风雨，其风常微轻如煦，袭万物不至于摇落；其雨十日一降，降 必以夜，津润条畅，不至地有淹流。一国之人，皆自相亲，有如戚属，人各相惠 多与。无市易商贩之事，以不求利故也。古说既至其国，顾谓元之曰：“此和神 国也。虽非神仙，风俗不恶。汝回，当为世人说之。吾既至此，回既别求人负囊， 不用汝矣。”因以酒令元之饮，饮满数巡，不觉沉醉。既而复醒，身已活矣。

    Explanation

    95

    The country raises only horses among its six livestock. These horses are extremely well-trained and swift, requiring no fodder as they feed themselves on wild grass and do not approach stored grain. People ride them when they need to, and after riding, they are released. There are no owners or caretakers. All officials are sufficient, but they do not know they are officials, mixed among common people because there are no duties to manage. Even though there is a king, the king does not know he is a king, mixed among the officials because there are no duties to promote or demote. The country also lacks sudden thunderstorms or heavy rains; the wind is always gentle and warm, not shaking or damaging things. It rains once every ten days, always at night, moistening and refreshing the land without causing flooding. All the people in the country are naturally close to each other, like family members, and generously help one another. There are no market transactions or trade activities because they do not seek profit. An ancient saying has reached the country, and the speaker turned to Yuan Zhi and said, "This is a harmonious and divine country. Though it is not a land of immortals, the customs are not bad. You return, and you should tell the world about it. I have already arrived here, and Yuan Zhi will find someone else to carry the bag; I will not use you anymore." He gave Yuan Zhi wine to drink, and after several rounds, Yuan Zhi did not realize he was drunk. Afterward, he woke up, and his body was alive.

    96

    自是元之疏逸人事，都忘宦情，游行山水，自号知和子，后竟不知其所终也。
    　　
    　　○卢公焕
    　　
    　　黄门侍郎卢公焕，为明州刺史，属邑象山县，溪谷迥无人处，有盗发墓者云： 初见车辙中有花砖，因揭之，知是古冢墓。乃结十人于县投状，请路旁居止，县 尹允之。遂种麻，令外人无所见。即悉力发掘，入其隧路，渐至圹中，有三石门， 皆以铁封之。
    　　
    　　其盗先能诵咒，因斋戒禁之。翌日，两门开，每门中各有铜人铜马数百，持 执干戈，其制精巧。盗又斋戒三日，中门一扇开，有黄衣人出，传语曰：“汉征 南将军刘使来相闻，某生有征伐大勋，及死，敕令护葬及铸铜人马等，以象存日 仪卫。奉计来此，必要财货，所居之室，实无他物，且官葬不瘗货宝，何必苦以 神咒相侵，若更不见已，尝不免两损。”言讫却入，门复合如初。

    Explanation

    96

    Since then, Yuan Zhi distanced himself from worldly affairs, completely forgot about the desire for office, and wandered among mountains and waters, giving himself the name Zhihezi. Later, no one knew what happened to him.

    Lu Gonghuan, a Yellow Gate Attendant, served as the Governor of Mingzhou. In the county of Xiangshan, there was a place in the remote valleys where bandits were digging up a tomb. They reported:

    "At first, we saw flower bricks in the wheel tracks. We uncovered them and found that it was an ancient tomb. We then gathered ten people and went to the county to submit a petition, requesting to stay by the roadside. The county magistrate agreed. We then planted hemp to hide our activities. We then worked hard to excavate, entering the tunnel, gradually reaching the interior of the tomb, where there were three stone doors, all sealed with iron.

    The bandits could recite spells and fasted to purify themselves. The next day, two doors opened, and in each door, there were hundreds of bronze figures and horses holding spears and halberds, the craftsmanship being exquisite. The bandits fasted for three more days, and one of the middle doors opened. A man in yellow robes appeared and said:

    'General Liu of the Han dynasty's Southern Expedition has come to inform you. He had great military achievements in life, and upon his death, the emperor ordered his tomb to be protected and bronze figures and horses to be cast to represent his ceremonial guards. We have come here, but you must seek treasures. The room we occupy has nothing else, and official burials do not bury valuables. Why bother to use divine spells to intrude? If you do not leave, both sides will suffer.' After speaking, he returned, and the door closed as before."

    97

    盗又诵咒数日不已，门开，一青衣又出传语，盗弗允说，两扇欻辟，大水漂 荡，盗皆溺死。一盗解泅而出，自缚诣官，具说本末。黄门令覆视其墓，其中门 内有一石床，骸枕之类，水漂已半垂于下，因却为封两门，窒其隧路矣。
    　　
    　　○吴全素
    　　
    　　吴全素，苏州人，举孝廉，五上不第。元和十二年，寓居长安永兴里。十二 月十三日夜既卧，见二人白衣执简，若贡院引牌来召者，全素曰：“礼闱引试， 分甲有期，何烦夜引？”使者固邀，不得已而下床随行，不觉过子城，出开远门 二百步，正北行，有路阔二尺已来，此外尽目深泥。见丈夫妇人，捽之者，拽倒 者，枷杻者，锁身者，连裾者，僧者，道者，囊盛其头者，面缚者，散驱行者， 数百辈皆行泥中，独全素行平路。约数里。入城郭见官府，同列者千余人，军吏 佩刀者分部其人，率五十人为一引，引过，全素在第三引中。

    Explanation

    97

    The thief continued reciting spells for several days without ceasing. The door opened, and a person in green clothes came out to convey a message. The thief did not agree to the terms, and the two doors suddenly opened. A great flood surged, drowning all the thieves. One thief managed to swim out, tied himself up, and went to the authorities, detailing the whole story. The Huangmen Ling carefully examined the tomb. Inside the inner gate, there was a stone bed, with bones and pillows. The water had carried it halfway down, and therefore, the two gates were sealed, and the tunnel was blocked.

    ○ Wu Quansu

    Wu Quansu, a native of Suzhou, was recommended as a filial and honest official but failed five times in the imperial examinations. In the twelfth year of the Yuanhe era, he was staying in Yongxing Lane in Chang'an. On the thirteenth day of the twelfth month, after he had gone to bed, he saw two men in white robes holding tablets, as if they were officials from the examination hall summoning him. Wu Quansu said, "The imperial examinations are divided into categories with a set time, so why bother to summon at night?" The messengers insisted, and Wu Quansu, reluctantly, got out of bed and followed them. He did not realize that they had passed through the inner city and exited the Kaiyuan Gate after two hundred steps, traveling north on a road about two feet wide, with deep mud everywhere else. He saw men and women being dragged, pulled down, shackled, bound, with their clothes torn, monks, Taoists, heads in sacks, hands tied behind their backs, and hundreds of people being driven through the mud, while Wu Quansu alone walked on level ground. After walking about three miles, he entered a city where he saw an official building, with over a thousand people lined up, and military officers with swords dividing the people into groups of fifty. As each group passed, Wu Quansu was in the third group.

    98

    其正衙有大殿，当 中设床几，一人衣绯而坐，左右立吏数十人，衙吏点名，便判付司狱者，付硙司 狱者，付鑛狱者，付汤狱者，付火狱者，付案者。闻其付狱者，方悟身死。见 四十九人皆点付讫，独全素在，因问其人曰：“当衙者何官？”曰：“判官也。” 遂诉曰：“全素恭履儒道，年禄未终，不合死。”判官曰：“冥司案牍，一一分 明。据籍帖追，岂合妄诉！”全素曰：“审知年命末尽，今请对验命籍。”乃命 取吴郡户籍到，检得吴全素，元和十三年明经出身，其后三年衣食，亦无官禄。 判官曰：“人世三年，才同瞬息，且无荣禄，何必却回！既去即来，徒烦案牍。” 全素曰：“辞亲五载，得归即荣，何况成名尚余三载，伏乞哀察。”判官曰： “任归。”仍诫引者曰：“此人命薄，宜令速去。稍以延迟，即突明矣。”引者 受命，即与同行。出门外，羡而泣者不可胜纪。

    Explanation

    98

    In the main hall, there was a grand hall, with beds and tables set up in the center. A man wearing red robes was seated, and dozens of officials stood on both sides. The hall officials called out names, and the judge immediately judged and sent people to the prison officials, to the prison of grinding, to the prison of mining, to the prison of boiling, to the prison of fire, and to the prison of case. Hearing that he was sent to prison, he realized he was dead. Seeing that all forty-nine people had been called out and assigned, only Quansu remained. He asked the person, "What is the position of the person in charge of the hall?" The person replied, "He is a judge." Quansu then complained, "I have always followed the Confucian path with respect, and my years of service are not yet complete. I should not die." The judge said, "The records in the underworld are clearly detailed. According to the records, he is summoned. How can you falsely accuse?" Quansu said, "If it is true that his years of life are not yet finished, I request to verify the records now." The judge then ordered to bring the household register of Wu Prefecture, and found Quansu, who had passed the imperial examination in 818 as a scholar. In the following three years, he had no official salary. The judge said, "Three years in the world are like a blink of an eye, and he has no honor or salary. Why return? Once gone, he will come back, and it will only complicate the records." Quansu said, "I left my parents for five years. Returning would be honorable. Not to mention that he still has three more years to achieve fame. I humbly ask for your pity and consideration." The judge said, "Go ahead." He then warned the guide, "This person has a short life. Should be sent away quickly. If delayed, dawn will break soon." The guide accepted the order and led him away. Out of the hall, those who envied and cried could not be counted.

    99

    既出其城，不复见泥矣。复至开远门，二吏谓全素曰：“君命甚薄，突明即 归不得，见判官之命乎？我皆贫，各惠钱五十万，即无虑矣。”全素曰：“远客 又贫，如何可致？”吏曰：“从母之夫，居宣阳为户部吏者甚富，一言可致也。” 既同诣其家，二吏不肯上阶，全素入告，其家方食煎饼，全素至灯前拱曰：“阿 姨万福！”又曰：“姨夫安和！”又不应。乃以手笼灯，满堂皆暗。姨夫曰： “何不抛少物？夜食香物，鬼神便合恼人。”全素既憾其不应，又目为鬼神，意 颇忿之。青衣有执食者，其面正当，因以力掌之，应手而倒，家人竞来拔发喷水， 呼唤良久方悟。全素既言情不得，下阶问二吏，吏曰：“固然，君未还生，非鬼 而何。鬼语而人不闻，笼灯行掌，诚足以骇之。

    Explanation

    99

    After leaving the city, the mud (or metaphorical obstacles) was no longer visible. We are all poor, so each of us will give you 500,000 coins, and you will have no worries." Quansu replied, "I am a distant guest and also poor; how can I accept such a gift?" The officials said, "The husband of your mother, who lives in Xuanyang and is a wealthy official in the Ministry of Finance, can achieve this with just one word." They then went together to his home. But there was no response. Quansu then covered the lamp with his hand, and the entire room became dark. The uncle said, "Why don't you throw something small? Eating fragrant things at night will anger the spirits." Quansu, already frustrated by the lack of response, saw the situation as ghostly and became quite angry. A servant holding food was directly in front of him, so Quansu struck him with force, and the servant fell immediately. The family rushed to pull out his hair and splash water on him, calling him for a long time before he regained consciousness. Quansu, having failed to express his feelings, went down the steps to ask the two officials. The officials said, "Indeed, you have not returned to life; you must be a ghost. Ghosts speak, but no one else can hear. Covering the lamp and striking, this is certainly enough to frighten people."

    ”曰：“然则何以言事？”曰： “以吾唾涂人大门，一家睡；涂人中门，门内人睡；涂堂门，满堂人睡。可以手 承吾唾而涂之。”全素掬手，二吏交唾。逡巡掬手以涂堂门。才华，满堂欠伸， 促去食器，遂入寝。二吏曰：“君入，去床三尺立言之。慎勿近床，以手摇动， 则魇不悟矣。”全素依其言言之，其姨惊起，泣谓夫曰：“全素晚来归宿，何忽 致死。今者见梦求钱，言有所遗，如何？”其夫曰：“忧念外甥，偶为热梦，何 足遽信！”又寝，又梦，惊起而泣，求纸于柜，适有二百幅，乃令遽剪焚之，火 绝，则千缗宛在地矣。二吏曰：“钱数多，某固不能胜。而君之力，生人之力也。 可以尽举，请负以致寄之。”全素初以为难，试以两手上承，自肩挑之，巍巍然 极高，其实甚轻，乃引行寄介公庙，主人者紫衣腰金，敕吏受之。

    100

    "Asked, 'Then how can one discuss matters?'     寄毕，二吏曰：“君之还生必矣，且思便归，为亦有所见耶？今欲取一人送 之受生，能略观否？”全素曰：“固所愿也。”乃相引入西市绢行南尽人家，灯 火荧煌，呜呜而泣，数僧当门读经，香烟满户。二吏不敢近，乃从堂后檐上，让 当寝床，有抽瓦折椽，开一大穴。穴中下视，一老人气息奄然，相向而泣者周其 床。一吏出怀中绳。大如指，长二丈余，令全素安坐执之，一头垂于穴中，诫全 素曰：“吾寻取彼人，人来，当掣绳。”遂出绳下之，而以右手捽老人，左手掣 绳，全素遽掣出之，拽于堂前，以绳囚缚。二吏更荷而出，相顾曰：“何处有屠 案最大？”其一曰：“布政坊十字街南王家案最大。”乃相与往焉。既到，投老 人于案上，脱衣缠身，更上推扑。

    After completing the ritual, the two officials said, "Your return to life is certain. Consider returning easily, for is there also something to be seen? Several monks were reciting scriptures at the door, and the house was filled with incense smoke. Looking down into the hole, they saw an elderly man faintly breathing, with those weeping around his bed. One official took out a rope from his chest, as thick as a finger and over two zhang long, and instructed Quansu to sit calmly and hold it, with one end hanging into the hole. He warned Quansu, "I will seek out that person. When the person comes, pull the rope."     老人曰苦，其声感人，全素曰：“有罪当刑， 此亦非法，若无罪责，何以苦之？”二吏曰：“讶君之问何迟也。凡人有善功清 德，合生天堂者，仙乐彩云霓旌鹤驾来迎也，某何以见之？若有重罪及秽恶，合 堕地狱者，牛头奇鬼铁叉枷杻来取，某又何以见之？此老人无生天之福，又无 入地狱之罪，虽能修身，未离尘俗，但洁其身，净无瑕秽，既舍此身，只合更受 男子之身。当其上计之时，其母已孕，此命既尽，彼命合生，今若不团扑，令彼 妇人，何以能产？”又尽力揉扑，实觉渐小，须臾，其形才如拳大，百骸九窍， 莫不依然。于是依依提行，逾子城大胜业坊西南下东回第二曲北壁，入第一家， 其家复有灯火荧煌，言语切切，沙门二人，当窗读《八阳经》。因此不敢逼僧， 直上阶，见堂门斜掩，一吏执老人于堂中，才似到床，新子已啼矣。

    The old man said it was bitter, his voice moved people. Quansu said, "If there is a crime, punishment should follow, but this is also not legal. If there is no guilt, why should he suffer?" The two officials said, "Why are you asking this question so late? All people with good deeds and purity of virtue, those who should be born in heaven, are welcomed by heavenly music, colorful clouds, rainbow flags, and crane-drawn chariots. How can I see this? If there are serious crimes or filthiness, those who should fall into hell, are taken by ogres with ox heads, iron forks, shackles, and manacles. How can I see this? This old man has no merit for heaven, and no sin for hell. Although he can cultivate himself, he has not yet transcended the mundane world. But he keeps his body clean, pure and without blemish. After giving up this body, he should only be reborn as a man. When he was planning his next life, his mother was pregnant. This life has ended, that life should be born. Now if we do not roll him up, to make that woman, how can she give birth?" They rolled and rubbed him with all their might, and they felt it getting smaller. In a short time, its form is just the size of a fist, all bones and nine orifices, nothing is different. Then they carried him gently, passing by the southern part of the outer city, the Great Success Avenue, the southwest corner, turning east, the second curve, and the northern wall, entering the first house.     一吏曰：“事毕矣，送君去。”又偕入永兴里旅舍，到寝房，房内尚黑，略 无所见。二吏随自后，乃推全素大呼曰：“吴全素！”若失足而坠，既苏，头眩 苦，良久方定。而衙鼓方动，姨夫者自宣阳走马来，则已苏矣，其仆不知觉也。 乘肩舆憩于宣阳，数日复故，再由子城入胜业生男之家，历历在眼。自以明经中 第，不足为荣，思速侍亲。卜得行日，或头眩不果去，或驴来脚损，或雨雪连日， 或亲故往来，因循之问，遂逼试日，入场而过，不复以旧日之望为意。俄而成名， 笑别长安而去。乃知命当有成，弃之不可；时苟未会，躁亦何为。举此端，足可 以诫其知进而不知退者。
    　　
    　　○掠剩使
    　　
    　　杜陵韦元方外兄裴璞，任邠州新平县尉，元和五年卒于官。

    Explanation

    103

    One official said, "The matter is concluded, now I shall escort you away." They then entered the inn in Yongxing Lane together and reached the bedroom, which was still dark, and nothing could be seen. Two officials followed from behind, and they then pushed Quansu and shouted, "Wu Quansu!" As if he had lost his footing and fallen, he regained consciousness, suffering from dizziness, and it took a long time before he stabilized. The official drum had just started beating, and his father-in-law came running on horseback from Xuanyang, by which time he had already regained consciousness, though his servant was unaware. He rode in a sedan chair and rested in Xuanyang, and after several days, he returned to his old self. He again entered the house of his son-in-law in the inner city, and everything was clearly in his mind. He considered himself to have passed the imperial examination through the mingjing route, but it was not worth much honor, and he wanted to quickly serve his parents. He chose a date for his journey, but sometimes he was dizzy and did not leave, or the donkey was injured, or it rained or snowed for days, or relatives and friends came and went, through these delays, he was then close to the exam day. He entered the examination hall and passed, and he no longer cared about his previous expectations. Soon he gained fame, laughed, and left Chang'an. He then realized that his fate was to succeed, and it was not possible to abandon it; if the time was not right, what would be the point of being impatient? By way of this example, it is enough to warn those who know how to advance but not how to retreat.

    ○Plundering Leftovers

    Du Ling's brother-in-law, Wei Yuanfang, Pei Pu, served as the County Magistrate of Xinping County in Bin Prefecture and died in office in the fifth year of the Yuanhe era (810 AD).

    104

    长庆初，元方下第，将客于陇右。出开远门数十里抵偏店，将憩，逢武吏跃 马而来，骑从数十，而貌似璞。见元方若识，而急下马避之，入茶坊，垂帘于小 室中，其徒御散坐帘外。元方疑之，亦造其邸。及褰帘入见，实裴璞也，惊喜拜 之，曰：“兄去人间，复效武职，何从吏之赳赳焉？”裴曰：“吾为阴官，职辖 武士，故武饰耳。”元方曰：“何官？”陇右三川掠剩使耳。”曰：“何为典耶？” 曰：“吾职司人剩财而掠之。”韦曰：“何谓剩财？”裴曰：“人之转货求丐也， 命当即□，忽遇物之箱稀，或主人深顾所得，乃逾数外之财，即谓之剩，故掠之 焉。”曰：“安知其剩而掠之？”裴曰：“生人一饮一啄，无非前定，况财实乎？ 阴司所籍，其获有限，获而逾籍，阴吏状来，乃掠之也。”韦曰：“所谓掠者， 夺之于囊耶，窃之于怀耶？”裴曰：“非也。当数而得，一一有成，数外之财， 为吾所运。

    Explanation

    104

    In the early years of the Changqing era, Yuan Fang failed the imperial examinations and was traveling to the region west of the Long Mountains. After leaving the Kaiyuan Gate and traveling dozens of miles to a remote inn, he was about to rest when he encountered a military officer riding a horse, accompanied by several attendants. The officer appeared to resemble Pei Pu. Seeing Yuan Fang, the officer seemed to recognize him and quickly dismounted to avoid him, entering a teahouse and hanging a curtain in a small room, while his attendants sat scattered outside the curtain. Yuan Fang was puzzled by this and decided to visit his residence. Upon lifting the curtain and entering, he found it was indeed Pei Pu. Yuan Fang was surprised and greeted him, saying, "Brother, after leaving the mortal world, you have taken up a military post again. Why do you appear so stern and imposing?" Pei Pu replied, "I am an official in the underworld, responsible for overseeing warriors, hence my martial appearance." Yuan Fang asked, "What position is that?" Pei Pu answered, "I am the Seizer of Surplus from the Three Rivers of Longyou." Yuan Fang inquired, "What is your duty?" Pei Pu explained, "My role is to seize surplus wealth from people." Yuan Fang asked, "What do you mean by surplus wealth?" Pei Pu said, "When people trade goods or seek alms, their fate is predetermined, but sometimes they encounter rare items or receive more than what was expected. This excess wealth is what we call surplus, and we seize it." Yuan Fang asked, "How do you know it is surplus and seize it?" Pei Pu replied, "Every drink and bite of food a person has is predestined; how much more so wealth? The underworld keeps records of what people are entitled to. If they acquire more than what is recorded, the underworld officials report it, and we seize it." Yuan Fang asked, "What do you mean by seizing? Do you steal it from their bags or pockets?" Pei Pu said, "No. It is determined by fate, and each person receives what is due to them. Any wealth beyond what is due is taken by me."

    105

    或令虚耗，或洁横事，或买卖不及常价，殊不关身尔。始吾之生也， 常谓商勤得财，农勤得谷，士勤得禄，只叹其不勤而不得也。夫覆舟之商，旱岁 之农，屡空之士，岂不勤乎？而今乃知勤者德之基，学者善之本。德之为善，乃 理身之道耳，亦未足以邀财而求禄也。子之逢吾，亦是前定，合得白金二斤，过 此遗子，又当复掠，故不厚矣。子之是行也，岐甚厚而邠甚薄，于泾殊无所得， 诸镇平平耳。

    Explanation

    105

    Some people squander resources, others handle strange matters, and still others trade at prices below the usual; these things have nothing to do with me. When I was born, I used to think that merchants gain wealth through diligence, farmers gain grain through diligence, and scholars gain official rank through diligence, only lamenting those who do not work hard and therefore do not achieve anything. Merchants who lose their ships, farmers who face drought, and scholars who repeatedly fail—how hard do they not work? But now I understand that diligence is the foundation of virtue, and learning is the root of goodness. Virtue is the way to cultivate oneself, but it is not enough to gain wealth or seek official rank. Your meeting with me was predestined; you were supposed to receive two pounds of silver, but after giving it to you, I will lose it again, so it is not a large amount. Your journey to Qì is rich, but to Bīn it is poor, and in Jing, you gain nothing at all; the other regions are average, nothing remarkable.

    人生有命，时不参差，以道静观，无复违挠，勉之哉！璞以公事， 顷入城中，阴冥数限，不可逾越。”遂以白金二斤授之，揖而上马。元方固请曰： “阔别多年，忽此集会，款言未几，又隔晦明，何遽如此？”璞曰：“本司廨署， 置在汧陇，阻吐蕃，将来虑其侵轶，当与阴道京尹，共议会盟。虽非远图，聊亦 纾患，亦粗安之计也。戎马已驾，来期不遥，事非早谋，不可为备，且去！且去！” 上马数里，遂不复见。其所遗，乃真白金也。怅然而西，所历之获，无差其说。
