    Life is determined by fate, and time does not vary; observe calmly through the Dao, no longer to resist or disturb, strive hard! Pú entered the city on official business, and the dark and ominous limits were such that they could not be crossed. He then presented two pounds of genuine white gold to him, bowed, and mounted his horse. Yuánfāng insisted, saying, "Having been apart for many years, we suddenly met, had a brief conversation, and now we are separated by day and night. Why are you leaving so suddenly?" Pú replied, "The official residence of my bureau is located in the Qian and Long regions, blocked by the Tibetan people. We are concerned that they will invade, so we must hold a council and make an alliance with the governor of the capital. Although this is not a long-term plan, it is a way to alleviate the crisis and a rough plan for temporary security. The military is already mobilized, and the arrival is not far off. The matter was not planned early, so we cannot prepare for it. Go! Go!" After riding several miles, he was no longer seen. What he left behind was genuine white gold. Disappointed and went westward, what was experienced and gained matched what was said.

    　　○叶天师
    　　
    　　开元中，道士叶静能讲于明州奉化县兴唐观。自升座也，有老父白衣而髯者， 每先来而后去，必迟迟然，若有意欲言而未能者。讲将罢去，愈更淹留。听徒毕 去，师乃召问。泣拜而言，自称鳞位，曰：“有意求哀，不敢自陈，既蒙不问， 敢不尽其诚恳。位实非人，乃实藏之守龙也。职在观南小海中，千秋无失，乃获 稍迁，苟或失之，即受炎沙之罚。今九百余年矣，胡僧所禁且三十春，其僧虔心， 有大咒力，今忧午日午时，其术即成，来喝水乾，宝无所隐。弟子当死，不敢望 荣迁，然千载之炎海，诚不可忍。惟仙师哀之，必免斯难，不敢忘德。”师许之， 乃泣谢而去。

    Explanation

    107

    Those who are content with their fate and know their destiny understand that all events are predestined. Suddenly, the foreign tribes became restless, and the court was aware of it, fearing potential rebellion. They thought of seeking a minister's advice for a strategy, and the prime minister presided over an alliance. The prime minister, Cui Gong, did not want to go to the border, so a humiliating peace agreement was made, and it turned out as he had said.

    ○ Ye the Taoist Master

    During the Kaiyuan period, the Taoist master Ye Jingneng lectured at the Xingtang Temple in Fenghua County, Mingzhou. When he ascended the dais, there was an old man in plain clothes with a beard. He always arrived first and left last, lingering slowly, as if he had something to say but couldn't. As the lecture was about to end, he lingered even more. After all the students left, the master then called him to ask. The old man wept and bowed while speaking, calling himself a fish position, and said, "I have something to plead, but dared not speak for myself. Since I was not questioned, I dare to express my sincerity fully. My position is not human; I am actually the guardian dragon of the hidden treasure. My duty is in the small sea to the south of the temple. If I do not fail for a thousand years, I will be promoted slightly. If I fail, I will be punished by the scorching sands. Now it has been over nine hundred years, and I have been forbidden by a foreign monk for nearly thirty years. The monk is devout and has great magical power. Now I fear that on the day of the fifth month and the fifth hour, the monk's spell will be completed. The monk will come to drink up the water, and the treasure will be revealed. I will die, but I dare not hope for promotion. However, a thousand years in the scorching sea is truly unbearable. Only you, the immortal master, can pity me and save me from this difficulty; I will never forget your kindness." The master agreed, and the old man wept and thanked him before departing.

    108

    师恐遗忘，乃大书其柱曰：“午日午时救龙。”其日赴食于邑人，既回方憩， 门人忽读其柱曰：“午日午时救龙。今方欲午，吾师正憩，岂忘之乎？”将入， 师已闻，遽问曰：“今何时？”对曰：“顷刻未午耳。”仙师遂使青衣门人执墨 符，奔往海。一里余，见黑云惨空，毒风四起，有婆罗门仗剑，乘黑云，持咒于 海上连喝，海水寻减半矣。青衣使亦随声堕焉。又使黄衣门人执朱符奔马以往， 去海一百余步，又喝，寻堕，海水十涸七八矣。有白龙跳跃浅波中，喘喘焉。

    Explanation

    108

    The teacher, fearing he might forget, wrote in large letters on the pillar: "Rescue the dragon at noon on the noon day." On that day, he went to dine with the townspeople and, upon returning, was just resting when his disciple suddenly read from the pillar: "Rescue the dragon at noon on the noon day. It is now just before noon, and my teacher is resting; how could he have forgotten it?" As the disciple was about to enter, the teacher had already heard and quickly asked, "What time is it now?" The disciple replied, "It has not yet reached noon." The immortal teacher then sent a green-clad disciple to hold a black talisman and rush to the sea. After a mile or so, they saw black clouds darkening the sky and toxic winds arising from all sides. There was a Brahmin wielding a sword, riding on black clouds, and shouting spells repeatedly over the sea, causing the seawater to soon reduce by half. The green-clad disciple also fell along with the sound. The teacher then sent a yellow-clad disciple to hold a red talisman and rush on horseback. After a hundred or more steps from the sea, they shouted again, and soon fell, causing the seawater to almost completely dry up. There was a white dragon jumping in the shallow waves, breathing heavily.

    109

    又 使朱衣使执黄符以往，僧又喝之，连喝不堕。及岸，则海水才一二尺，白龙者奋 鬣张口于沙中。朱衣使投符于海，随手水复。婆罗门抚剑而叹曰：“三十年精勤， 一旦术尽，何道士之多能哉！”拗怒而去。既空海恬然，波停风息，前堕二使， 亦渐能起，相与偕归，具白于师。未毕，老父者已到，泣拜曰：“向者几死于胡 术，非仙师之力，不能免矣。位也，惧不克报，然终天依附，愿出门人，可指使 也。若承师命，虽秦越地阻，江山路殊，一念召之，即立左右矣。”自是朝夕定 省，若门人焉。

    Explanation

    109

    Again, he sent a messenger dressed in red robes with a yellow talisman to go. The monk shouted at him again, and he did not fall despite the shouting. When they reached the shore, the sea water was only one or two feet deep. The white dragon raised its mane and opened its mouth on the sand. The messenger in red robes threw the talisman into the sea, and the water immediately returned to its original state. The Brahmin touched his sword and sighed, saying, "Thirty years of diligent practice, all lost in an instant. How many skills does this Taoist have!" He left in anger. Afterwards, the sea became calm, and the waves and wind ceased. The two messengers who had fallen before gradually got up and returned together, reporting everything to the master. Before the report was finished, the old man arrived, wept, and said, "Earlier, I almost died from the foreign magic, but without the power of the immortal master, I could not have escaped. I, Wei, fear I cannot repay you, but I will always be attached to you. I wish to be your disciple, and you can command me. If I receive your command, even if there are great distances between Qin and Yue, or mountains and rivers, with just a thought, I will be at your side." From then on, he came to visit every morning and evening, like a disciple.

    110

    师以其观在原上，不可穿井，童稚汲水，必于十里之外，阖观患之。他日， 师谓髯父曰：“吾居此多日，怜其汲远，思绕观有泉以济之，子可致乎？”曰： “泉水之流，天界所有，非力可致。然师能见活，又脱千年之苦，岂可辞乎！夫 非可致而致之，界神将拒，俟战胜然后可。令诸人皆他徙。其日晦明三复，然后 归，庶几有从命□□之功。”合观从之。过期而还，则石甃绕观，清流潺潺，既 周而南，入于海，黄冠赖焉。乃题渠曰：“仙师渠”。师所以妙术广大天下，盖 龙之所助焉。
    　　
    　　○许元长
    　　
    　　许元长者，江陵术士焉，客淮南。御史陆俊之从事广陵也，有贤妻，待之情 分倍愈于常。俄而妻亡，俊之伤悼，情又过之。每至春风动处，秋月明时，众乐 声悲，征鸿韵咽，或展转忘寐，思苦畏叹，或伫立无憀，心伤永日。如此者逾年 矣，全失壮容，骤或雪鬓。

    Explanation

    110

    The master, seeing that his residence was on high ground, realized that it was impossible to dig a well. As a result, children had to fetch water from ten miles away, causing the entire community great trouble. One day, the master said to the bearded father, "I have lived here for a long time and feel pity for the children who have to fetch water so far. I am thinking of having a spring around the residence to help them. Can you bring it?" The bearded father replied, "The flow of water is something in the heavens, not something that can be brought by force. However, since you have seen the living, you have also escaped the suffering of a thousand years. How can I refuse? Although the spring cannot be brought by force, it can be brought after a battle. Order everyone to move elsewhere. On that day, after three cycles of darkness and light, they returned, perhaps there would be some success in following the command." The entire community followed the instructions. After the designated period, they returned to find stones laid around the residence, with clear water flowing gently. After circling around, the water flowed south into the sea, and the Daoist priests relied on it. They then named the channel "Fairy Master's Channel." The master's marvelous skills spread widely throughout the world, which was due to the help of the dragon.

    Translation of the Second Part

    Xu Yuanchang, a sorcerer from Jiangling, was a guest in Huainan. When the censor Lu Jun served in Guangling, he had a virtuous wife whom he treated with exceptional care and affection. Soon after, his wife passed away, and Lu Jun was deeply grieved, his sorrow even surpassing that of ordinary people. Whenever the spring wind blew or the autumn moon shone bright, the sounds of music would evoke sadness, and the cries of geese in flight would choke his throat. Sometimes he would toss and turn, unable to sleep, tormented by grief and fear; at other times, he would stand motionless, feeling utterly desolate, his heart heavy with sorrow. This state of mind lasted for over a year, and he completely lost his youthful appearance, his hair turning white overnight.

    111

    他日元长来，陆生知有奇术，试以汉武帝李夫人之事诱之，元长曰：“此甚 易耳。”曰：“然则能为我致亡妻之神乎？”曰：“彼所致者，但致其魂，瞥见 而已。元长又异焉。”陆曰：“然则子能致者何？”曰：“可致其身若生人，有 以从容尽平生之意。”陆喜极拜曰：“先生诚致之，顾某骨肉，手足无所措矣。” 曰：“亡夫人周身之衣，亦仿佛能记乎？”曰：“然。”于是择癸丑日，艮宫直 音，空其室，陈设焚香之外，悉无外物。乃备美食，夜分，使陆生公服以俟焉。 老青衣一人侍立。元长曰：“夫人之来，非元长在此不可。元长若去，夫人隐矣。 侍御夫人久丧，枕席单然，魂（以下缺）。”

    Explanation

    111

    One day, Yuan Chang arrived, and Lu Sheng, knowing of his extraordinary skills, tried to tempt him with the story of Emperor Wu of Han and his favorite concubine, Lady Li. Yuan Chang replied, "This is very easy." Lu Sheng asked, "Then can you bring the spirit of my deceased wife for me?" Yuan Chang said, "What I can bring is only her spirit, and you will only get a brief glimpse of her." Yuan Chang found this strange. Lu Sheng asked, "Then what can you bring?" Yuan Chang replied, "I can bring her body as if she were alive, and we can interact at ease, fulfilling all the intentions of life." Lu Sheng, extremely happy, bowed and said, "Master, if you truly bring her, my family and I will be overjoyed." Yuan Chang asked, "Can you remember the entire outfit of your deceased wife?" Lu Sheng replied, "Yes." So they chose the day of Gui Chou, with the direction of Gen Gong and the direct sound. They emptied the room, setting up only incense and nothing else. They then prepared a feast at midnight, having Lu Sheng dress formally and wait. An old servant stood by. Yuan Chang said, "Lady Li's arrival depends on me being here. If I leave, she will disappear. Your wife has been deceased for a long time, and your bed is now empty and lonely, her spirit (the rest is missing)."

    ○马仆射总
    　　
    　　检校右仆射总，元和末节制东平。长庆二年六月十日午时，寝熟，梦二军吏 乘马入中门，及阶而下，一人握刀拱手而前，曰：“都统屈公。”公惊曰：“都 统谁耶？”曰：“见则知矣。”公欲不去，使者曰：“都统之命，仆射不合辞。” 不觉衣服上马。一吏引，一吏从，遂出郓州北郭门数百里，入城又数十里，见城 门题曰：“六押大都统府”。门吏武饰，威容甚严。
    　　
    　　入一二百步，有大衙门，正北百余步，有殿九间，垂帘下有大声曰：“屈上 阶。”阴知其声，乃杜司徒佑也，遂趋而升，二阉竖出卷帘。既而见之，果杜司 徒也。公素承知友，交契甚深，相见极喜，慰劳如平生。遂揖坐，都统曰：“莫 怪奉邀否？佑任此官，年劳将转，上司许自择替。中朝之堪付重权者，今揣量无 逾于阁下者，将欲奉托耳。此官名‘六押大都统’，□□不是过也，且以大庇亲 族知友耳。人之生世，白驹过隙，谁能不死。

    Explanation

    112

    Inspector of the Right Privy Councilor Ma Zong, in the late Yuanhe era, was in charge of Dongping. On the sixth day of the sixth month of the second year of Changqing (822 AD), at noon, he was asleep and had a dream in which two military officials rode horses into the main gate, dismounted at the steps, and one of them held a knife and bowed, saying, "The Grand Commander summons you." Ma was startled and asked, "Who is the Grand Commander?" The official replied, "You will know when you see." Ma wanted not to go, but the messenger said, "The Grand Commander's command, the Privy Councilor should not refuse." Without realizing, he dressed and mounted his horse. One official led him, and another followed, and they rode out of the northern gate of Yuncheng (modern-day Shandong) hundreds of miles, then entered the city again for dozens of miles, where they saw a gate inscribed with "The Sixth Battalion Grand Commander's Office." The gate guards were militarily adorned and had a very stern demeanor.

    After entering for a hundred or two hundred steps, they came to a grand hall. A hundred or more steps to the north, there was a nine-roomed hall, and below the curtain, a loud voice said, "Ascend the steps." Secretly knowing the voice, it was Duke Du You. He hurried to ascend, and two eunuchs unrolled the curtain. Upon seeing him, it was indeed Duke Du You. Ma had always been acquainted with him, having a deep bond, and met with great joy, comforting and consoling as usual. They bowed and sat down, and the Grand Commander said, "Do not blame me for inviting you. I am about to be rewarded for my years of service, and superiors allow self-selection for replacement. Those in the capital who can be entrusted with heavy responsibilities, today, no one surpasses you in capability, and I wish to entrust this position to you. This position is called 'Sixth Battalion Grand Commander,' it is not too much, and it will greatly protect relatives and friends. Life in this world is like a white horse passing through a crevice, who can avoid death?"

    而又福不再遇，良时易失，苟非深 分，岂荐自代。权位既到，幸勿因循。”公曰：“生为节制，死岂为民？阳禄方 崇，阴位谁顾。直使为王且不愿，况都统哉？”杜曰：“上请授公，天命难拒。 文符即下，何能违天！”公曰：“天听甚卑，亦从人欲，奈何自取求替，诬其天 命乎？”杜曰：“终与公，公岂能免。”公曰：“终不受，都统安能与？必若以 鬼相逼，岂无天乎？”杜乃顾谓群吏曰：“公既拒，事不谐矣！”公曰：“渴， 请两盂茶。”杜仍促煎茶。从吏曰：“仆射既不住，不合饮此茶。况时热，不可 久住，宜速命驾。”

    However, good fortune does not come twice, and good times are easily lost. Unless there is a deep understanding, how could one recommend oneself in place of another? Once power and position have been attained, do not be complacent or negligent. The chancellor replied, "If one lives as a general, how can one die as a commoner? Official rank and salary are just rising; who cares about the afterlife? Even if made king, one would not want it, how much more so as a general?" Du said, "The emperor requests to grant this to you, and heavenly mandate is hard to resist. Once the official document is issued, how can one defy heaven!" The chancellor replied, "Heaven listens closely, and also follows human desires. How can one seek to replace oneself, thus falsely claiming heavenly mandate?" Du said, "I will ultimately grant it to you, how can you avoid it?" The chancellor replied, "I will ultimately refuse, how can the general grant it? If it's forced by ghosts, isn't there still heaven?" Du then turned to the officials and said, "Since the chancellor has refused, the matter will not be successful!" The chancellor said, "I am thirsty, please bring two cups of tea." Du still urged the preparation of tea. The attendant said, "Since the chancellor does not stay, it is not appropriate to drink this tea. Especially in the heat, one cannot stay long, it is best to leave quickly."

    　　○华山客

    ○ The Guest of Mount Hua

    Dang Chaoyuan was a native of He County, Tongzhou. In the second year of the Yuanhe era, he retired to live south of Luo Fu Water in Mount Hua. On the sixteenth day of the twelfth month of the following year, near the second watch of the night, the sky was clear and the moon was bright, the scenery was very beautiful. Suddenly, he heard the sound of knocking on the door. He ordered the servant to wait for her, and she said, "A young woman, about seventeen or eighteen years old, with an extraordinary appearance, and a strange fragrance filled the road." Dang Chaoyuan invited her in and sat with her. Her words were clear and eloquent, her grace was very high, and she was certainly not of this world. After a long time, she said, "Do you know who I am?" Dang Chaoyuan replied, "If you are not a goddess, then you must not be an ordinary person." The woman said, "No." She then asked, "Do you know why I have come here?" Dang Chaoyuan said, "I am not ashamed of my lowly status, but I seek only the pleasure of your bed." The woman smiled and said, "Certainly not."

    115

    妾非神仙，乃南冢之妖狐也。 学道多年，遂成仙业。今者业满愿足，须从凡例，祈君活之耳。枕席之娱，笑言 之会，不置心中有年矣，乞不以此怀疑，若徇微情，愿以命托。”超元唯唯。又 曰：“妾命后日当死于五坊箭下。来晚猎徒有过者，宜备酒食以待之。彼必问其 所须，即曰：‘亲爱有疾，要一猎狐，能遂私诚，必有殊赠。’以此恳请，其人 必从。赠礼所须，今便留献。”因出束素与党，曰：“得妾之尸，请夜送旧穴。 道成之后，奉报不轻。”乃拜泣而去。

    Explanation

    115

    I am a woman, not a divine being, but a fox spirit from the Southern Graveyard. After studying the Dao for many years, I attained the state of being a spirit. Now that my spiritual goals are fulfilled, I must follow the rules of the ordinary world, and I beg you to save my life. The pleasures of our intimate moments and the laughter and conversation we shared have not been in my thoughts for years. I ask you not to doubt me because of this. If you agree to this small request, I will entrust my life to you. My fate is to die tomorrow at the hands of the archers in the imperial stables. Any hunter who passes by late in the evening should be prepared with food and drink for him. He will ask what you need, so you should say: "My beloved is ill and needs a hunting fox to fulfill a private wish, and there will be a special reward." If you make this request, he will surely agree. The gifts he will bring, I leave for you now. I am giving you this silk as a token of my gratitude. If you find my body, please send it back to my old den at night. After achieving enlightenment, I will repay you generously. She bowed and wept before departing.

    116

    至明，乃鬻束素以市酒肉，为待宾之具。其夕，果有五坊猎骑十人来求宿， 遂厚遇之。十人相谓曰：“我猎徒也，宜为衣冠所恶。今党郎倾盖如此，何以报 之？”因问所须，超元曰：“亲戚有疾，医藉猎狐，其疾见困，非此不愈。”乃 祈于诸人：“幸得而见惠，愿奉五素为酒楼费。”十人许诺而去。南行百余步， 有狐突走绕大冢者，作围围之，一箭而毙。其徒喜曰：“昨夜党人固求，今日果 获。”乃持来与超元，奉之五素。既去，超元洗其血，卧于寝床，覆以衣衾。至 夜分人寂，潜送穴中，以土封之。

    Explanation

    116

    By dawn, he had sold a roll of white silk to buy wine and meat, preparing for the guest. That night, indeed, ten hunters from the Five Fences came to request lodging, and he treated them generously. The ten men said to each other, "We are hunters and should be disliked by the literati. Now that Lord Tang has treated us so generously, how can we repay him?" They then asked what was needed, and Chao Yuan said, "My relative is ill, and the doctor needs a hunting fox. His illness is worsening, and it will not improve without this." He then asked the others, "If you could kindly give it to me, I would be willing to offer five rolls of white silk as payment for the wine." The ten men agreed and left, walking south for more than a hundred steps. Suddenly, a fox ran around a large tomb, and they surrounded it, shooting it with an arrow and killing it instantly. His companions were delighted and said, "Last night, Lord Tang earnestly requested it, and today we have indeed obtained it." They then brought it to Chao Yuan and gave him five rolls of white silk. After they left, Chao Yuan washed its blood, laid it on the bed, and covered it with a quilt. By midnight when everyone was quiet, he secretly sent it to a den and sealed it with earth.

    117

    后七日夜半，复有扣门者，超元出视，乃前女子也，又延入。泣谢曰：“道 业虽成，准例当死，为人所食，无计复生。今蒙深恩，特全毙质，修理得活，以 证此身。磨顶至踵，无以奉报。人尘已去，云驾有期，仙路遥遥，难期会面。请 从此辞。药金五十斤，收充赠谢。此金每两值四十缗，非胡客勿示。”乃出其金， 再拜而去，且曰：“金乌未分，有青云出于冢上者，妾去之候也。火宅之中，愁 焰方炽，能思静理，少息俗心，亦可一念之间，暂臻凉地。勉之！勉之！”言讫 而去。明晨专视，果有青云出于冢上，良久方散。
    　　
    　　人验其金，真奇宝也。即日携入市，市人只酬常价。后数年，忽有胡客来诣， 曰：“知君有异金，愿一观之。”超元出示，胡笑曰：“此乃九天掖金，君何以 致之？”于是每两酬四十缗，收之而去。后不知其所在耳。

    Explanation

    117

    Seven days after midnight, there was again someone knocking at the door. Chao Yuan went out to see, and it was the same woman who had come before. He invited her in again. She wept and thanked him, saying, "Even though my spiritual path has been completed, by rule, one should die. Being consumed by others, there is no way to be reborn. Now I have received your deep grace, and you have specially preserved my mortal body. I have been repaired and thus live again, to prove this body. From head to toe, there is nothing to repay. The dust of the human world has departed, and the chariot of the clouds has a set time. The path to immortality is long and distant, and it is difficult to meet again. Please allow me to take my leave. I have fifty pounds of medicinal gold, which I will use as a gift and thanks. This gold is worth forty strings of cash per pound, and do not show it to anyone except a foreigner." Then she took out the gold, bowed twice, and left, saying, "Before the golden bird (sun) has risen, if blue clouds emerge from the grave, that is the time when I am leaving. In the house of fire, the flames of sorrow are just beginning to blaze. If one can think of calm principles and slightly rest from worldly desires, one can temporarily reach a cool place. Encourage yourself! Encourage yourself!" After speaking, she left. The next morning, he observed, and indeed, blue clouds emerged from the grave, lingering for a long time before dissipating.

    The people tested the gold, and it was truly a rare treasure. That day, he carried it to the market, but the market people only paid the regular price. Several years later, suddenly, a foreigner came to visit, saying, "Knowing that you have unusual gold, I wish to see it once." Chao Yuan showed it to him, and the foreigner laughed, saying, "This is the gold from the celestial treasury. How did you obtain it?" Then he paid forty strings of cash per pound, took it, and left. Later, no one knew where he was.

    ○尹纵之
    　　
    　　尹纵之，元和四年八月肄业中条山西峰。月朗风清，必吟啸鼓琴以怡中。一 夕，闻檐外履步之声，若女子行者。纵之遥谓曰：“行者何人？”曰：“妾山下 王氏女，所居不远，每闻郎君吟咏鼓琴之声，未尝不倾耳向风，凝思于蓬户。以 父母训严，不敢来听。今夕之亲有适人者，父母俱往，妾乃独止。复闻久慕之声， 故来潜听。不期郎之闻也。”纵之曰：“居止接近，相见是常。既来听琴，何不 入坐？”纵之出迎，女子乃拜。纵之略复之，引以入户，设榻命坐。仪貌风态， 绰约异常，但耳稍黑。纵之以为真村女之尤者也。山居闲寂，颇积愁思，得此甚 惬心也。命仆夫具果煮茗，弹琴以怡之。山深景静，琴思清远，女意欢极。因留 宿，女辞曰：“父母如何？”纵之曰：“喜会是赴，固不夜归。五更潜复闭户为 独宿者，父母曙到，亦何觉之。”女笑而止。相得之欢，誓将白首。绸缪之意， 无不备尽。

    118

    尹纵之，元和四年八月在中条山西峰读书。月光明亮，风清气爽，他常常吟诗啸歌，弹琴自娱。一天晚上，他听到屋檐外有脚步声，像是女子走动。尹纵之远远问道：“你是谁？”女子回答说：“我是山下的王氏女子，住处不远，每次听到郎君吟诗弹琴的声音，总是倾耳聆听，凝神于茅屋之中。因父母管教严厉，不敢前来听。今晚父母有亲事，一同前往，我独自留下。又听到久慕之声，所以前来偷听。没想到被郎君听见了。”尹纵之说：“我们住得近，相见是常事。既然来听琴，为什么不进来坐坐？”尹纵之出门迎接，女子便行礼。尹纵之略施礼，将她请进屋，设下坐榻请她坐下。女子仪态风姿，绰约异常，只是耳朵稍黑。尹纵之认为她是村中女子中最美的。山居生活闲适寂静，他心中积了不少愁思，有了她的陪伴，心情十分舒畅。他吩咐仆人准备水果和茶水，弹琴以娱她。山深景静，琴声清远，女子听后非常高兴。于是尹纵之留她过夜，女子推辞说：“父母怎么办？”尹纵之说：“既然高兴相会，就不必连夜回家。五更时分，悄悄关门独宿，父母天亮来，也不会察觉。”女子笑着同意了。两人相处十分愉快，发誓要白头偕老。彼此的深情厚意，无不尽情表达。

    Zong allowed the creature to rest from the exhaustion of the entire night. Suddenly, he fell into a deep sleep and awoke only when the sun reached the window. Zong informed Wang Chao, who took up his bow and arrow and pursued it, killing it with a single arrow. That year, Zong went to the foot of the mountain to seek an offering, though his reputation and prestige were great, he ultimately achieved nothing. Was it the fault of the pig?

    ○ Wang Huang

    Wang Huang of Taiyuan, on the 5th day of the 5th lunar month in the 3rd year of the Yuanhe era (808 CE), at the hour of shen (around 3–5 PM), departed from Luoyang for Gou Shi Village. He traveled twenty-five li from Jianchun Gate, and on the left side of the road, he saw a newly dug grave. Before it stood a young woman in white mourning attire, offering a sacrifice and weeping bitterly. Huang secretly observed her and saw that she was about eighteen or nineteen years old, of extraordinary beauty. Two maids stood by her side, and there was no husband present. One of the attendants said, "This young lady is from the state of Qin. After her coming-of-age ceremony, she married Pei Zhi of Hedong. Less than two years later, Pei went to Luoyang and never returned. The young lady was surprised by this and, together with these two of us, came to Luoyang, only to find that Pei had already died. Her husband is buried here, hence she has come to mourn and offer a sacrifice." Huang asked, "If that is the case, where will she go?" The attendant replied, "The young lady was orphaned at a young age and has no family. Where could she go? Recently, her family arranged her marriage, but her uncle has since passed away. For now, she will stay in Luoyang and must certainly seek a husband." Huang was pleased and said, "I hold an official post and have been unmarried since youth."

    Huang summoned his attendant soldiers and traveled with him for more than ten miles, staying together at Pengbo Inn. He arranged a separate bed according to etiquette.     Several months later, Huang returned to Luoyang for a reason. In Luoyang, there was a Taoist named Ren Xuanyan, a master of magical arts, who had always been friendly with Huang. Seeing Huang's appearance, Xuanyan was greatly surprised and asked, "What has happened to you, dear friend? Why do you look so worn out?" Huang smiled and replied, "I've taken a wife." Xuanyan said, "The one you've taken is not a human wife, but a powerful spirit. If you can quickly break off this relationship, you can still be saved. But in another ten or so days, your path to life will be cut off, and even I will be unable to save you." Huang was not pleased, as the planned matter had not been successful, and he had not left anyone behind to request a return. His intention was even more urgent. His deep, lingering thoughts could not be described.

    Another ten or so days passed, and Huang returned to Luoyang again. He met Xuanyan at the South Market, took his hand, and said, "Your appearance is that of someone who is about to die. Not believing my words, you have come to this. Tomorrow at noon, that person will come, and when they do, you will die. Alas! Alas!" He then wept and bid farewell to Huang, who became even more confused. Xuanyan said, "You don't believe me? Please keep this talisman in your chest. Tomorrow at noon, when your beloved enters the door, please throw the talisman at her, and you will see her true form." Huang took the talisman and kept it in his chest. After Xuanyan left, he told his servant, "Tomorrow at noon, the spirit from the Field of Cinnabar will come. Your master must throw the talisman at her. You can observe her shape; she will either be a blue-faced, heavy spirit or a red-faced one. When she enters and sits down, your master will die. When he dies, look at him—did he die sitting down?" The servant secretly remembered these words.

"It is customary for it to be replaced every three thousand years. When the ghost's term is up, it should naturally choose a replacement, so it transforms into a human and takes it." "Huang died sitting down," he continued, "and after three thousand years, he should also seek a replacement. Now that he has died lying down, he will never get a replacement again." Before his eyes, Huang's body was lying with his spine broken. Xuan Yan wept and left. This is the servant who told the story.

    ○岑曦
    　　
    　　进士郑知古，睿宗朝客于相国岑公门下，有日矣。一夕，寝于内厅。夜分， 远闻众闹祈哀之声。倾耳听之，声声渐近。既而分明闻其所救人曰：“岑氏寒微， 未达于天下，幸而生之。曦谬掌朝政，其心畏惧，未尝敢危人。设使妇人而持权 者，其心亦猛于曦也。即曦□□御物，生无怨人，死无怨鬼，何所触犯，而当此 戮？唯使者恕之。某等当使曦以阴钱百万奉谢。”泣告之声盈路。俄见大鬼丈余， 蓬头朱衣，执长剑逾墙而入，有丈夫、妇女、老者、少者亦随之入，或自投于墙 下遮拜，其辞恳切。大鬼不顾，又逾中门，众已纷纭而入。食顷，闻阖门大哭之 声，惊起听之，大鬼者执曦头仍出，门内哭声极哀，若有大祸。衙鼓将动，稍稍 似息。知古徨不知所为，行于廊下，以及鸣鼓。

    A Scholar's Encounter with the Supernatural: The Tale of Cen Xi

    During the reign of Emperor Ruizong, the scholar Zheng Zhiguo, a guest in the household of the high-ranking official Cen Xi, stayed there for some time. One night, he slept in the inner hall. At midnight, he heard from afar the clamor and cries for mercy. He leaned forward to listen, and the sounds became increasingly closer. Soon, he clearly heard the person being saved say, "Cen's family is humble and lowly, not widely known or respected. I am lucky to be alive. Cen Xi mistakenly holds the reins of government. His heart is filled with fear, and he never dared to harm anyone. If a woman were to hold power, her heart would be even more fierce than Cen Xi's. Even if Cen Xi were to rule over things, no one will resent me when I am alive, and no ghost will resent me when I die. What have I done to deserve such punishment? Only the messenger can forgive me. We will make Cen Xi offer a million hidden coins as a token of gratitude." The cries of pleading filled the road. Soon, he saw a large ghost, more than a zhang tall, with disheveled hair and red clothing, holding a long sword and leaping over the wall. Men, women, old people, and young people also followed him in, some throwing themselves at the wall and prostrating themselves, their words earnest. The large ghost paid no heed and then leapt over the middle gate. The crowd entered in a disordered manner. After a meal's time, he heard loud weeping from the entire house. He woke up and listened, and the large ghost took Cen Xi's head and left. The crying inside the door was extremely sad, as if a great calamity had befallen. The drum of the government office was about to sound, and gradually, it seemed to subside. Zheng Zhiguo was in a state of confusion and did not know what to do. He walked along the corridor, and the drum sounded.

    ○Li Shen

    Li Shen of Longxi was the son of a man who once received favors from Zhu Ci. After the rebels were pacified and punished according to the law, Li Shen escaped and was spared. Later, when amnesty was granted, he gave all his family property and servants to the Huilin Temple in Luobei and lived there temporarily. He read books and played the qin, just to pass the time. Today, Cui Qun, the chancellor of Jingnan and a high-ranking official from Qinghe, along with his brother, a jinshi (advanced scholar), both observed the etiquette of disciples toward Li Shen, and his reputation was well-known. He often had a close friendship with the reclusive scholar Li Zuo, as sworn brothers.

    In the autumn of the thirteenth year of the Yuanhe era, Li Zuo told Li Shen, "I have an old comrade who is heading to Song. I won't know when I'll return, so can you accompany me on a boat trip?" Upon hearing that Li Zuo was leaving, Li Shen felt a deep sense of separation, so he boarded the boat. They initially agreed to travel one stage, and when the journey was over, Li Zuo said, "Your affection hasn't reached its limit yet, has it?" As they continued, Li Zuo seemed to be moved by something, and they couldn't say goodbye, continuing straight to Suoyang. That evening, Li Zuo thanked the boatman and left, and he and Li Shen descended from the Bian River embankment. Under the moonlight, Li Zuo slowly said, "Your affection has been sincere for a long time. Do you know who I am, Li Shen?" Li Shen replied, "A learned and eloquent person." Li Zuo said, "That's not it. I am an official in the underworld, recently serving as the governor of Luozhou, which is why I stayed in Luoyang for a long time. My official duties are concealed, so I cannot be seen during the day, which is why I could travel with you at night. Now, I am transitioning from the underworld to the earthly realm and have been entrusted to carry a child for five years. That's why I stayed with you step by step, having something to entrust to you." Li Shen asked, "What is it?" Li Zuo said, "My body is difficult to match in skill. I only fear that if I let go of this body, I might be completely absorbed in my past karma. I ask you to wake me up."

    128

    然擢孕五载，寓亲腹中，其家以为不祥，祈神祝佛之法，竭货而为。擢尚未 往，神固何为。兄可往其家，朱书“产”字令吞之，擢即生矣。必奉兄绢素。兄 得且去，候擢三岁，宜复来视之，且曰：“主人孙久不产者，某以朱字吞之，生 儿奇惠，今三载矣，思宿以告之，故复来也。”可取儿抱卧，夜久，伺掌人闭户， 即抱于静处呼曰：“李擢记我否？”儿当啼，啼即掌之。再三问之，擢必微悟。 兄宜与擢言洛中居处及游宴之地，擢当大悟，悟后此生之业无孑遗矣。此事必醒 素以归，擢乃后荣盛，兄不可复得从容矣。兄声名籍甚，不久当有大谏之拜，慎 勿赴也，赴当非寿。此郡北三十里有胡村，村前有车门，即擢新身之居也。言讫， 泣拜而去。

    Explanation

    128

    Yet Ruo was pregnant for five years, in her mother's womb, and her family considered it an omen. They prayed to gods and worshipped Buddha, spending all their resources. Ruo had not yet been born, what could the gods do? Brother can go to their home, write the character "产" in red ink and make them swallow it, Ruo will be born immediately. They will certainly present the brother with fine silk and white cloth. The brother should leave, wait until Ruo is three years old, and then come to see him again, and say, "The master's grandson who has not been born for a long time, I made them swallow the red character, and the boy is very clever, now he is three years old, I think it is appropriate to tell him, so I came back." Can take the child and hold him, at night, when the caretakers have closed the door, then take him to a quiet place and call out, "Li Ruo, do you remember me?" If he cries, then pat him. Ask him repeatedly, Ruo will surely have a slight understanding. The brother should talk to Ruo about the places he lives and plays in Luoyang, Ruo will have a great understanding, after understanding, his life's work will be without any remnants. This matter must be clearly explained and returned, Ruo will later become prosperous and honored, the brother cannot afford to be leisurely anymore. The brother has a great reputation, soon he will be appointed to a high office, be cautious not to accept it, accepting it will not be good for longevity. North of this prefecture, thirty miles away, there is a village called Hu, in front of the village there is a carriage gate, which is where Ruo will live in the future. After finishing speaking, he wept and bowed, then left.

    129

    迟明，沈策杖访之，果有胡村。叩门求憩，掌人翁年八下余，倚杖延入。既 命坐，似有忧色，沈问之，翁曰：“新妇孕五载矣，计穷术尽，略无少征。”沈 因曰：“沈道门留心，颇善咒术，不产之由，见之即辨。”遽令左右召新妇来， 沈诊其臂曰：“男也，甚明惠，有非常之才，故不拘常月耳。”于是令速具产所 帷帐床榻毕，沈执笔若祝者，朱书“产”字令吞之。入口，而男生焉。翁极喜， 奉绢三十疋，沈乃受焉，曰：“此儿不常也，三岁当复来为君相之。”言讫而去。

    Explanation

    129

    Just before dawn, Shen, walking with a staff, visited and indeed found the village of Hu. He knocked on the door to seek rest, and the elderly man of the household, over eighty years old, leaned on a cane and invited him in. After seating him, the elderly man seemed worried, and Shen asked him about it. The elderly man replied, "The new wife has been pregnant for five years, all methods have been exhausted, and there are no signs at all." Shen said, "I have studied the Daoist arts and am skilled in spells. The reason for the lack of birth, I can discern immediately." He immediately ordered the attendants to bring the new wife, and after examining her arm, said, "It is a boy, very bright and intelligent, with extraordinary talent, hence not bound by the usual lunar cycles." Then he ordered the preparations for the birthing room to be made quickly, including curtains, beds, and other furnishings. Shen took a brush as if performing a ritual, wrote the character '生' (birth) in red ink, and had her swallow it. After she swallowed it, a boy was born. The elderly man was extremely happy and presented thirty bolts of silk. Shen accepted it and said, "This child is not ordinary; I will return in three years to advise you further." After saying this, he left.

    130

    及期再往，乃曰：“前所生子，今三岁矣，愿得之一宿占相之。”掌人喜而 许之。沈夜伺人静，抱之远处，呼曰：“李擢，今识我否？”儿惊啼，沈掌之， 曰：“李擢何见我不记耶？”又掌之，儿愈啼。而问之者三四，儿忽曰：“十六 兄果能来此耶？”沈因与言洛中事，遂大笑言若平生，曰：“擢一一悟矣。”乃 抱之归宿。及明朝，告其掌人曰：“此儿有重禄，乃成家之贵人也，宜保持之。” 胡氏喜，又赠绢五十疋，因取别。乃忆醒素之言，盖以三才五星隐其成数耳。
    　　
    　　以沈食禄而诛，不食而免，其命乎？足以警贪禄位而不知其命者也。
    　　
    　　
    　　
    　　辑佚
    　　
    　　◇杜巫
    　　
    　　杜巫尚书年少未达时，曾于长白山遇道士贻丹一丸，即令服讫，不欲食，容 色悦怿，轻健无疾。后任商州刺史，自以既登太守，班位已崇而不食，恐惊于众， 于是欲去其丹，遇客无不问其法。

    Explanation

    130

    On the agreed-upon date, Shen returned, and said, "The child you had before is now three years old. I wish to take him for one night to observe and divine." The caretaker was pleased and agreed. At night, when people were quiet, Shen took the child to a distant place and called out, "Li Zuo, do you recognize me now?" The child cried in fright, and Shen held him, saying, "Li Zuo, why don’t you remember me?" He held him again, and the child cried even more. Shen asked him three or four times, and the child suddenly said, "Is it really true that Brother Li has come here?" Shen then spoke to him about matters in Luoyang, and the child laughed as if they were old friends, saying, "I have now understood everything." Shen then took him back and kept him overnight. In the morning, he told the caretaker, "This child will have a great official rank and will be a prosperous person in his family. It is advisable to keep him well." Hu was pleased and gave him fifty bolts of silk as a gift. Shen then left. He remembered the words of the Taoist priest, who had used the three celestial bodies and five stars to hint at the child's fortune.

    Because Shen was killed due to his official rank, but avoided disaster by not eating, it was indeed his fate. This story is sufficient to warn those who covet official rank and wealth without understanding their fate.

    Compilation of Lost Texts

    Du Wu

    When Du Wu was young and not yet successful, he once met a Taoist priest on Changbai Mountain who gave him a pill of elixir. He took it, and from then on, he did not want to eat. His face appeared joyful and healthy, and he was light and agile without illness. Later, he became the prefect of Shangzhou and thought that he had already reached a high position. He feared to startle the crowd, so he decided to remove the elixir from his body. Whenever he met guests, he would always ask about the method.

    131

    岁余，有道士至，甚年少。巫询之，道士教以食猪肉仍吃血。巫从之食吃， 道士命挲罗。须臾，巫吐痰涎至多，有一块物如栗。道士取之。甚坚固。道士剖 之，若新胶之未乾者，丹在中。道士取以洗之，置于手中，其色绿莹。巫曰： “将来，吾自收之，暮年服也。”道士不与，曰：“长白吾师曰：‘杜巫悔服吾 丹，今愿出之。汝可教之，收药归也。’今我奉师之命，欲去其神物。今既去矣， 而又拟留至耄年。纵收得，亦不能用也。自宜息心。”遂吞之而去。巫后五十余 年，罄产烧药，竟不成。
    　　
    　　○崔尚
    　　
    　　开元时，有崔尚者，著《无鬼论》，词甚有理。既成，将进之，忽有道士诣 门，求见其论。读竟，谓尚曰：“词理甚工。然天地之间，若云无鬼，此谬矣。” 尚谓“何以言之？”道士曰：“我则鬼也，岂可谓无？君若进本，当为诸鬼神所 杀，不若焚之。”因尔不见，竟失其本。

    Explanation

    131

    After more than a year, a Taoist arrived, and he was extremely young. The witch asked him, and the Taoist taught her to eat pork and drink blood. The witch followed his instructions and ate, and the Taoist ordered her to spit. Shortly after, the witch spat out a large amount of phlegm, and there was a lump in it like a chestnut. The Taoist took it. It was very hard. The Taoist cut it open, and it was like newly made glue that was not yet dry, with a pill inside. The Taoist took it and washed it, putting it in his hand, and its color was green and lustrous. The witch said, "Give it to me, I will keep it for my old age." The Taoist did not give it, saying, "My master told me, 'Witch Du regrets taking my pill, now wants to give it back. You can teach her to take the medicine back.' Now I am following my master's command, wanting to remove the magical object. Now it is gone, and she wants to keep it until old age. Even if you keep it, you will not be able to use it. You should calm your mind." And he swallowed it and left. After more than fifty years, the witch spent all his wealth on burning medicine, but it never succeeded.

    ○Cui Shang

    During the Kaiyuan era, there was a man named Cui Shang, who wrote the Wu Gui Lun (Treatise on the Nonexistence of Ghosts), which was very well-reasoned. After it was completed, he was about to submit it, when suddenly a Taoist came to his door, asking to see the treatise. After reading it, the Taoist said to Cui Shang, "The reasoning in your treatise is very skillful. However, in the world, if one says there are no ghosts, this is a mistake." Cui Shang asked, "Why do you say so?" The Taoist replied, "I am a ghost, how can one say there are none? If you submit this treatise, you will be killed by the spirits. It would be better to burn it." And so, the Taoist disappeared, and Cui Shang eventually lost the manuscript.

    132

    ○郑望
    　　
    　　乾元中，有郑望者自都入京。夜投野狐泉店宿，未至五六里而昏黑。忽于道 侧见人家。试问门者，云是王将军，与其亡父有旧。望甚喜，乃通名参承。将军 出，与望相见，叙悲泣，人事备之。因尔留宿，为设馔饮。中夜酒酣，令呼蘧蒢 三娘唱歌送酒，少间三娘至，容色甚丽，尤工唱《阿鹊盐》。及晓别去，将军夫 人传语，令买锦裤及头髻花红朱粉等。
    　　
    　　后数月，东归过，送所求物，将军相见欢洽，留宿如初。望问何以不见蘧蒢 三娘。将军云：“已随其夫还京。”以明日辞去。出门不复见宅，但余丘陇。望 怃然，却回。至野狐泉，问居人，曰是王将军冢。冢边，伶人至店，其妻暴疾亡， 以苇席裹尸，葬将军坟侧，故呼曰蘧蒢三娘云。旬日前，伶官亦移其尸归葬长安 讫。

    Explanation

    132

    In the middle of the Qianyuan era, there was a man named Zheng Wang who traveled from the capital to the imperial city. At night, he checked into a guesthouse called Wild Fox Spring for lodging, but he was not yet five or six li away when it became dark. Suddenly, he saw a house on the side of the road. He asked the gatekeeper, who told him it was the residence of General Wang, and that his father had been friends with the general. Zheng Wang was very pleased and introduced himself, paying his respects. The general came out and greeted him, exchanging sad tears and discussing various matters. They decided to stay overnight and had a meal together.

    In the middle of the night, after drinking to their heart's content, the general asked for a musician to sing and entertain them. Soon, a young woman named Qu Chu San娘 appeared, her appearance very beautiful, and she was especially skilled at singing "The Salt of the Magpie." Until dawn, they parted ways. The general's wife conveyed a message, instructing Zheng Wang to buy silk trousers, a headband, red flowers, and rouge.

    A few months later, on his way back east, Zheng Wang stopped by to deliver the requested items. The general greeted him warmly and invited him to stay overnight, as before. Zheng Wang asked why he didn't see Qu Chu San娘 anymore. The general replied, "She has already returned to the capital with her husband." The next day, Zheng Wang bid farewell and left. As he stepped out, he saw no more signs of the house, only hills and mounds remained. Zheng Wang felt disheartened and turned back. When he reached Wild Fox Spring, he asked the locals, who told him it was the tomb of General Wang. Near the tomb, a musician came to the inn. The musician's wife had suddenly fallen ill and died. She was wrapped in a reed mat and buried beside the general's grave, hence she was called Qu Chu San娘. A few days ago, the musician had also moved her body to be buried in Chang'an.

    133

    ○元载
    　　
    　　大历九年春，中书侍郎平章事元载，早入朝。有献文章者，命左右收之。此 人若欲载读，载云：“候至中书，当为看。”人言：“若不能读，请自诵一首。” 诵毕不见，方知非人耳。诗曰：
    　　
    　　城东城西旧居处，城里飞花乱如絮。
    　　
    　　海燕衔泥欲下来，屋里无人却飞去。
    　　
    　　载后竟破家，妻子被杀云。
    　　
    　　○魏朋
    　　
    　　建州刺史魏朋，辞满后，客居南昌。素无诗思，后遇病，迷惑失心，如有人 相引接。忽索笔抄诗言：
    　　
    　　孤坟临清江，每睹白日晚。
    　　
    　　松影摇长风，蟾光落岩甸。
    　　
    　　故乡千里余，亲戚罕相见。
    　　
    　　望望空云山，哀哀泪如霰。
    　　
    　　恨为泉台客，复此异乡县。

    Explanation

    133

    Yuan Zai

    In the spring of the ninth year of the Dali era, Yuan Zai, the Chancellor of the Secretariat, arrived at court early in the morning. Someone presented an article, and he ordered the attendants to collect it. If this person wanted Yuan Zai to read it, Yuan Zai said, "Wait until I am in the cabinet, then I will read it." The person said, "If you cannot read it, please recite one yourself." After reciting, the person disappeared, and it was only then that Yuan Zai realized it was not a human being. The poem said:

    In the old residence to the east and west of the city, the flying flowers in the city are as chaotic as fluff.
    The swallow carries mud and wants to descend, but the house is empty, yet it flies away.

    Later, Yuan Zai's family was broken, and his wife and children were killed.

    Wei Peng

    Wei Peng, the governor of Jianzhou, after his term ended, became a guest in Nanchang. He had never had a thought for poetry, but later, after falling ill, he became confused and lost his mind, as if someone was leading him. Suddenly, he picked up a pen and wrote a poem:

    A lonely grave by the clear river, every day I see the late white sun.
    The shadow of pines sways in the long wind, the moonlight falls on the rocky fields.
    My hometown is thousands of miles away, relatives seldom meet.
    Looking at the empty clouds and mountains, tears fall like snowflakes.
    Regret being a guest of the underworld, again in this foreign county.

    134

    愿言敦畴昔，勿以弃疵贱。
    　　
    　　诗意如其亡妻以赠朋也。后十余日，朋卒。
    　　
    　　○岑顺
    　　
    　　汝南岑顺字孝伯，少好学有文，老大尤精武略。旅于陕州，贫无第宅。其外 族吕氏有山宅，将废之，顺请居焉。人有劝者，顺曰：“天命有常，何所惧耳！” 卒居之。
    　　
    　　后岁余，顺常独坐书阁下，虽家人莫得入。夜中闻鼓鼙之声，不知所来。及 出户，则无闻，而独喜，自负之，以为石勒之祥也。祝之曰：“此必阴兵助我， 若然，当示我以富贵期。”数夕后，梦一人被甲胄前报曰：“金象将军使我语岑 君，军城夜警，有喧诤者，蒙君见嘉，敢不敬命。君甚有厚禄，幸自爱也。既负 壮志，能猥顾小国乎？今敌国犯垒，侧席委贤，钦味芳声，愿执旌钺。”顺谢曰： “将军天质英明，师真以律，猥烦德音，屈顾疵贱。然犬马之志，惟欲用之。” 使者复命。顺忽然而寤，恍若自失，坐而思梦之征。

    Explanation

    134

    I wish to cherish the past, do not abandon me because of my flaws or lowly status.

    The poem is like the late wife's gift to a friend. After more than ten days, the friend died.

    ○ Cen Shun

    Cen Shun from Runan, courtesy name Xiao Bo, was fond of learning and had literary talent when young, and especially skilled in military strategy when older. He lived in Shan Prefecture, poor and without a home. His cousin, the Lü family, had a mountain house that was about to be abandoned, and Cen Shun requested to live there. When someone advised him against it, Cen Shun said, "Fate is constant, so what is there to fear!" and eventually moved in.

    After more than a year, Cen Shun often sat alone in the study, and even family members could not enter. At night, he heard the sound of drums, not knowing where it came from. When he went out the door, he heard nothing, but he was alone in his joy, believing it to be an omen of Shi Le. He prayed, saying, "This must be the aid of hidden soldiers. If so, please show me the promise of wealth and status." A few nights later, he dreamed of a man in armor and armor reporting to him, saying, "The Golden Elephant General sent me to tell Cen Shun, the city is on alert at night, there are noisy disturbances, I am honored by your favor, how dare I not follow your command. You will have a generous salary, please take care of yourself. Having great ambitions, can you condescend to visit a small country? Now the enemy country is attacking, we are eager to entrust the wise, we admire your good reputation, and wish to hold the banner." Cen Shun replied, saying, "General, your natural qualities are brilliant, you are a true teacher, I am honored by your words, and you have condescended to visit me. However, my loyalty is to serve you." The messenger returned with his message. Cen Shun suddenly woke up, feeling as if he had lost himself, sitting and thinking about the meaning of the dream.

    135

    俄然鼓角四起，声愈振厉。顺整巾下床，再拜祝之。须臾，户牖风生，帷帘 飞扬，灯下忽有数百铁骑，飞驰左右，悉高数寸，而被坚执锐，星散遍地。倏闪 之间，云阵四合。顺惊骇，定神气以观之。须臾，有卒赍书云：“将军传檄。” 顺受之，云：
    　　
    　　地连獯虏，戎马不息，向数十年。将老兵穷，姿霜卧甲，天设劲敌，势不可 止。明公养素畜德，进业及时，屡承嘉音，愿托神契。然明公阳官，固当享大禄 于圣世，今小国安敢望之。缘天那国北山贼合从，克日会战，事图子夜，否灭未 期，良用惶骇。
    　　
    　　顺谢之，室中益烛，坐观其变。夜半后，鼓角四发。先是东面壁下有鼠穴， 化为城门，垒敌崔嵬，三奏金革，四门出兵，连旗万计，风驰云走，两皆列阵。 其东壁下是天那军，西壁下金象军。部后各定，军师进曰：

    Explanation

    135

    Suddenly, drums and horns sounded from all sides, and the sound grew more resounding and fierce. Shun tidied his headgear, got out of bed, and bowed twice to make a wish. In a moment, the wind blew through the doors and windows, and the curtains flew up. Under the lamp, hundreds of iron-clad cavalry suddenly appeared, flying around, all about an inch tall, wearing armor and holding sharp weapons, scattered like stars across the ground. In the blink of an eye, the cloud formations gathered from all sides. Shun was startled but then calmed down to observe the scene. In a moment, a soldier arrived with a message saying, "The general sends a summons." Shun received it, and it read:

    The land is connected to the Xiongnu, with continuous warfare for several decades. Old generals and soldiers are exhausted, lying in their armor like frost, facing a powerful enemy that cannot be stopped. Your Excellency has nurtured virtue and pursued your career at the right time, often receiving good news, and I wish to entrust our fate to a divine pact. However, Your Excellency holds a high office and should enjoy great fortune in this sacred era, so how dare I, a small state, hope for such things. Because the bandits from the northern mountains of Tianya State have united, they plan to attack at midnight, and the outcome is uncertain, causing great fear.

    Shun thanked him, lit more candles in the room, and sat to observe the changes. After midnight, drums and horns sounded from all sides. Earlier, there was a mouse hole on the eastern wall, which transformed into a city gate, with enemy fortifications towering up, three times the sound of metal and leather, four gates sending out troops, thousands of banners, rushing like wind and clouds, both sides arrayed in formation. On the eastern wall is the Tianya Army, and on the western wall is the Jinxiang Army. After the formations were set, the military advisor said:

    136

    天马斜飞度三止，上将横行系四方。
    　　
    　　辎车直入无回翔，六甲次第不乖行。
    　　
    　　王曰：“善。”于是鼓之，两军俱有一马，斜去三尺，止。又鼓之，各有一 步卒，横行一尺。又鼓之，车进。如是鼓渐急而各出，物包矢石乱交。须臾之间， 天那军大败奔溃，杀伤涂地。王单马南驰，数百人投西南隅，仅而免焉。先是西 南有药臼，王栖臼中，化为城堡。金象军大振，收其甲卒，舆尸横地。顺俯伏观 之，于时一骑至禁，颁曰：“阴阳有厝，得之者昌。亭亭天威，风驱连激，一阵 而胜，明公以为何如？”顺曰：“将军英贯白日，乘天用时，窃窥神化灵文，不 胜庆快。”如是数日会战，胜败不常。王神貌伟然，雄姿罕俦。宴馔珍筵，与顺 致宝贝明珠珠玑无限。顺遂荣于其中，所欲皆备焉。后遂与亲朋稍绝，闲间不出。

    Explanation

    136

    A Swift Horse and a Mighty General

    A swift horse, slanting its flight across three stops, and a mighty general, advancing broadly to bind all directions.

    A carriage, directly entering without circling, and the six divisions of the army, proceeding in order without deviating from the path.

    The king said, "Good." Then, the drum was beaten, and both armies had one horse, which slanted away three feet and stopped. Again, the drum was beaten, and each had one foot soldier, who moved horizontally one foot. Again, the drum was beaten, and the carriage advanced. Thus, as the drumming became more urgent, each emerged, and objects, arrows, and stones were mixed together in chaos. In a moment, the heavenly army was defeated and scattered, with killed and wounded scattered everywhere. The king rode alone to the south, and hundreds of people fled to the southwest corner, barely escaping. Before that, in the southwest, there was a medicine mortar, and the king stayed in the mortar, which turned into a castle. The golden elephant army was greatly invigorated, gathered their armored soldiers, and carried bodies across the ground. Shun bowed down to observe, and at that time, a rider arrived at the palace, declaring, "The yin and yang have their place; those who obtain it will flourish. The majestic power of heaven, wind-driven and continuous, won in one battle. What do you think, distinguished sir?" Shun replied, "The general's brilliance shines through the day, riding the heavens and using the time, secretly observing the divine and spiritual writings, cannot help but feel joy and relief." Like this, battles continued for several days, with victories and defeats not constant. The king's divine appearance was magnificent, and his heroic appearance was rare. A feast of fine dishes, together with Shun, presented innumerable treasures, pearls, and gemstones. Shun was honored among them, and all his desires were fulfilled. Later, he gradually distanced himself from relatives and friends, did not go out.

    137

    家人异之，莫究其由。而顺颜色憔悴，为鬼气所中。亲戚共意有异，诘之不 言。因饮以醇醪，醉而究，泄之。其亲入潜备锹锸，因顺如厕而隔之。荷锸乱作， 以掘室内八、九尺，忽坎陷，是古墓也。墓有砖堂，其盟器悉多，甲胄数百，前 有金床戏局，列马满枰，皆金铜成形，其干戈之事备矣。乃悟军师之词，乃象戏 行马之势也。既而焚之，遂平其地。多得宝贝，皆墓内所畜者。顺阅之，恍然而 醒，乃大吐。自此充悦，宅亦不复凶矣。时宝应元年也。

    Explanation

    137

    The family found Shun strange, but none could fathom the reason. Shun's complexion became gaunt, as if he had been afflicted by a ghostly presence. Relatives all felt something was amiss and interrogated him, but he remained silent. They gave him strong liquor to drink, and when he was drunk, they questioned him, and he revealed the truth. His relatives secretly prepared shovels and, while Shun was in the bathroom, they separated him. They carried shovels and began digging frantically, digging eight or nine feet into the room. Suddenly, a hole collapsed, revealing an ancient tomb. The tomb had a brick chamber, and it was filled with many ritual objects. There were hundreds of armor and weapons, with a gold bed in front of a chessboard, lined with horses on the board, all made of gold and bronze, and all the implements of warfare were present. They then realized that the general's words referred to the formation of the chess pieces. Afterward, they burned it and leveled the ground. They found many treasures, all of which had been stored in the tomb. Shun examined them, and suddenly he woke up, vomiting profusely. From then on, he felt refreshed, and the house no longer seemed ominous. This was during the first year of the Baoying era.

    138

    ○韦协律兄
    　　
    　　太常协律韦生，有兄甚凶，自云平生无惧惮耳。闻有凶宅，必往独宿之。其 弟话于同官，同官有试之者，且闻延康东北角有马镇西宅，常多怪物，因领送其 宅，具与酒肉，夜则皆去，独留之于大池之西孤亭中宿。韦生以饮酒且热，袒衣 而寝。
    　　
    　　夜半方寤，乃见一小儿，长可尺余，身短脚长，其色颇黑，自池中而出，冉 冉前来，循阶而上，以至生前。生不为之动，乃言曰：“卧者恶物，直又顾我耶？” 乃绕床而行。须臾，生回枕仰卧，乃觉其物上床，生亦不动。逡巡，觉有两个小 脚缘于生脚上，冷如水铁，上彻于心，行步甚迟。生不动，候其渐行，上及于肚， 生乃遽以手摸之，则一古铁鼎子，已欠一脚矣。遂以衣带系之于床脚。明旦，众 看之，具白其事。乃以杵碎其鼎，染染有血色。自是人皆信韦生之凶而能绝宅之 妖也。

    Explanation

    138

    The Brother of Wei Sheng, the Imperial Music Official

    Wei Sheng, an official of the Imperial Household known as the Imperial Music Official, had a brother who was exceedingly fearsome. He claimed that he had never been afraid of anything. Whenever he heard of a haunted house, he would go there alone to spend the night. His brother told this to their colleagues, and one of them decided to test him. They learned that there was a house belonging to Ma Zhenxi in the northeast corner of Yan Kang, which was often plagued by strange creatures. So, they led Wei Sheng’s brother to this house, providing him with wine and food, and then left him alone in a solitary pavilion west of a large pond to spend the night. Wei Sheng’s brother drank until he was slightly warm and then undressed and lay down to sleep.

    In the middle of the night, he suddenly woke up and saw a small child, about a foot tall, with a short body and long legs, and a rather dark complexion. The child emerged from the pond, slowly moving forward, climbing the steps, and approaching Wei Sheng’s brother. Wei Sheng’s brother did not move, and the child said, "You’re a vile creature, do you think you’re so important that you can look down on me?" Then the child began to walk around the bed. After a while, Wei Sheng’s brother turned over and lay on his back, and he felt the creature climb onto the bed. He remained still. After a moment, he felt two small feet climbing up his own feet, cold as water and iron, reaching up to his heart, and moving very slowly. Wei Sheng’s brother did not move, waiting for the creature to continue moving until it reached his belly. He then quickly reached out and touched it, discovering it was an ancient iron pot missing one leg. He tied it to the bedpost with his belt. The next morning, the others came to see what had happened, and he fully explained the incident. They smashed the pot with a pestle, and it turned a bloody color. From then on, people believed that Wei Sheng’s brother was so fearsome that he could banish the evil spirits from the haunted house.

    139

    ○苏履霜
    　　
    　　太原节度马侍中燧小将苏履霜者，顷事前节度使鲍防，从行营日，并将伐回 纥。时防临阵，指一旗刘明远，以不进锋，命履霜斩之。履霜受命，然数日明远 遽进，得脱丧元之祸。后十余年卒。履霜亦游于冥间，见明远，乃谓履霜曰： “曩日蒙君以生成之故，无因酬德，今日当展素愿。”遂指一路，路多榛棘，云： “但趋此途，必遇舍利王。王平生会为侍中之部将也，见而诉之，必获免。”告 之命去，履霜遂行一二十里间，果逢舍利王弋猎。舍利索识履霜，惊问曰：“何 因至此？”答曰：“为冥司所召。”乃曰：“公不合来，宜速反！”遂命判官王 凤翔，令早放回，兼附信耳。谓履霜曰：“为余告侍中，自此二年，当罢节，一 年之内，先须去入赴朝廷。郎君早弃人世，慎勿泄之。”凤翔检籍放归。至一关 门，逢平生饮酒之友数人，谓履霜曰：“公独行归，余曹企慕所不及也。”

    Explanation

    139

    Su Lushuang, a subordinate under Ma Sui, the military governor of Taiyuan, once served under Bo Fang, a previous military governor. During a campaign against the Uyghurs, Bo Fang, on the battlefield, pointed to a flag of Liu Mingyuan and ordered Su Lushuang to execute him for not advancing in battle. Su Lushuang accepted the order, but a few days later, Liu Mingyuan suddenly advanced and managed to escape the death penalty. Many years later, Su Lushuang died. He also wandered in the underworld, where he met Liu Mingyuan. Liu Mingyuan said to Su Lushuang, "In the past, I was saved by you, and I had no way to repay your kindness. Today, I will fulfill my long-held wish." He then pointed out a path, which was filled with thorny bushes, and said, "Just follow this path, and you will meet Sheli Wang. Sheli Wang was a subordinate of the Chancellor in life. If you see him and plead with him, you will surely be spared." He told Su Lushuang to leave quickly, and Su Lushuang walked about twenty miles, eventually meeting Sheli Wang, who was hunting. Sheli Wang recognized Su Lushuang and asked, "Why are you here?" Su Lushuang replied, "I was summoned by the underworld authorities." Sheli Wang said, "You should not have come here; you should return quickly!" He then ordered the judge Wang Fengxiang to release Su Lushuang early and to deliver a message. He told Su Lushuang, "Tell the Chancellor that two years from now, he will be dismissed from his position. Within a year, he must first go to court. Your son died young; be careful not to reveal this." Wang Fengxiang released Su Lushuang. When Su Lushuang reached a gate, he met several friends he had drunk with before, who said to him, "You have returned alone; we could not even hope to accompany you."

    140

    生五六日，遂造凤翔。凤翔逆已知之，问云：“舍利何词？”曰：“有之， 不令告他人也。”凤翔曰：“余亦知之，汝且归，余侯隙当白侍中。”旬日，遂 与履霜白之。侍中召履霜讯之，履霜亦具所见。凤翔陈告，后所验一如履霜所言， 盖凤翔生自司冥局，隐而莫有知之者，因履霜还生而泄也。
    　　
    　　○景生
    　　
    　　景生者，河中猗氏人也，素精于经籍，授胄子数十人。岁暮将归，途中偶逢 故相吕潭，以旧相识，遂以后乘载之而去。群胄子乃散，报景生之家。而景生到 家，身已卒讫，数日乃苏，云：“冥中见黄门侍郎严武、朔方节度张或然。”

    Explanation

    140

    A person was born and lived for five or six days, then arrived at Fengxiang. Fengxiang had already anticipated and knew about something, and asked, "What words were spoken about Sarira?" The person replied, "There were words, but I was not allowed to tell others." Fengxiang said, "I also know about it. You may return for now; I will report to the Attendant General when the opportunity arises." After ten days, the person reported it with Lushuang. The Attendant General summoned Lushuang to interrogate him, and Lushuang also detailed what he had seen. Fengxiang then reported, and what was later verified matched exactly what Lushuang had said. It is said that Fengxiang was born from the Department of the Underworld, and the fact was hidden and unknown to others, but it was revealed because Lushuang returned to life.

    Jing Sheng, a man from Yishi in Hedong, was always highly skilled in the classics and taught dozens of students. At the end of the year, he was about to return home. On the way, he happened to meet the former chancellor Lü Tan, an old acquaintance, and was taken away by him. The students then scattered and reported to Jing Sheng's family. However, when Jing Sheng arrived home, he had already died. After several days, he woke up and said, "In the underworld, I saw the Yellow Gate Attendant General Yan Wu and the Military Governor of the Northern Frontier Zhang Huo."

    景生善《周易》，早岁兼与吕相讲授，未终秩，遇吕相薨，乃命景生，请终 余秩。时严、张俱为左右台郎，顾吕而怒曰：“景生未合来，固非冥间之所勾留， 奈何私欲而有所害？”共请放回。吕遂然之。张尚书乃引景生，嘱：“两男，一 名曾子，一名夫子，闰正月三日当起比屋，妨曾子新妇，为报止之。令速罢，当 脱大祸。”及景苏数日，而后报其家，屋已立，其妻已亡矣。又说：“曾子当终 刺史，夫子亦为刺史，而不正拜。”后果如其言。
    　　
    　　○卢顼表姨
    　　
    　　洺州刺史卢顼表姨常畜一猧子，名花子，每加念焉。一旦而失，为人所毙。 后数月，卢氏忽亡。冥间见判官姓李，乃谓曰：“夫人天命将尽，有人切论，当 得重生一十二年。”拜谢而出。

    Explanation

    141

    Jing Sheng was proficient in The Book of Changes. In his early years, he also taught alongside Lord Lv, but before he could complete his term, Lord Lv passed away. Lord Lv then appointed Jing Sheng to complete the remaining term. At that time, Yan and Zhang were both officials in the imperial court. They looked at Lord Lv and angrily said, "Jing Sheng should not be here; it is certainly not something that can be detained in the afterlife. Why should private desires harm him?" They jointly requested to let Jing Sheng return. Lord Lv agreed. Minister Zhang then called Jing Sheng and instructed him: "Two sons, one named Zengzi, the other named Fuzi, on the third day of the leap month of the first month, they will start building next to each other's houses, which will harm Zengzi's new wife. Please report and stop it. Let them stop quickly, and he will escape a great disaster." After Jing Sheng regained consciousness for several days, he reported this to his family. By then, the houses had already been built, and his wife had already passed away. Minister Zhang also said, "Zengzi will eventually become a prefect, and Fuzi will also become a prefect, but not through proper appointment." Indeed, as predicted, the events unfolded as he had said.

    Lu Xū's aunt, who was the aunt of the Prefect of Mingzhou, often kept a small dog named Huāzi, and she would always think of it fondly. One day, the dog went missing and was killed by someone. Several months later, Lu Xū's aunt suddenly died. In the afterlife, she saw a judge surnamed Li, who told her, "Your fate is nearly over, but someone strongly argued, and you will be given another twelve years of life." She bowed in thanks and left.

    142

    行长衢中，逢大宅。有丽人，侍婢十余人，将游门屏，使人呼夫人入，谓曰： “夫人相识耶？”曰：“不省也。”丽人曰：“某即花子也。平生蒙不以兽畜之 贱，常加育养。某今为李判官别室。昨所嘱夫人者，即某也。冥司不广其请，只 加一纪。某潜以改十二年为二十，以报存育之恩。有顷李至，伏愿白之本名，无 为夫人之号，恳将力祈。”李逡巡而至，至别坐语笑。丽人首以图乙改年白李。 李将让之，对曰：“妾平生受恩，以此申报，万不获一，料必无难之。”李欣然 谓曰：“事则匪易。”感言请之切，遂许之。临将别，谓夫人曰：“请收余骸， 为瘗埋之。骸在履信坊街之北墙委粪之中。”夫人既苏，验而果在。遂以子礼葬 之。后申谢于梦寐之间。后二十年，夫人乃亡也。

    Explanation

    142

    Walking along the main street, he encountered a grand mansion. Inside, there was a beautiful woman accompanied by more than ten attendants, who were about to pass through the gate. Someone was sent to call the lady inside, and she was asked, "Do you recognize this lady?" The lady replied, "I do not recall her." The beautiful woman said, "I am Flower Girl. Throughout my life, I was not treated as a lowly animal, but was always nurtured. I am now the concubine of Judge Li. The request I made to you yesterday was indeed me. The underworld did not expand the petition, only granting a twelve-year extension. I secretly changed the twelve years to twenty to repay the kindness of being raised. Soon after, Judge Li arrived, and I humbly ask that you present my true name, not the title of 'Lady,' and I earnestly pray for your help." Judge Li hesitated and arrived. The beautiful woman first presented the petition to change the year to Judge Li. Judge Li was about to refuse, but she replied, "I have received much kindness in my life, and I am using this opportunity to report it. It is rare to succeed, but I believe it will not be difficult." Judge Li happily said, "The matter is not easy." Moved by the earnest request, he agreed. As they were about to part, the beautiful woman said to the lady, "Please collect my remains for burial. They are in the northern wall of the street in the Lu Xin Ward, among the refuse." The lady then revived, verified the location, and indeed found the remains. She buried him with the rites of a son. Later, she expressed gratitude in her dreams. Twenty years later, the lady passed away.

    ○狐诵通天经
    　　
    　　裴仲元家鄠北，因逐兔入大冢，有狐凭棺读书。元仲搏之不中，取书以归， 字不可认识。忽有胡秀才请见，曰行周，仍凭棺读书者。裴曰：“何书也？”曰： “《通天经》，非人间所习。足下诚无所用，愿奉百金赎之。”裴不应。又曰： “千镒。”又不应。客怒，拂衣而起。裴内兄韦端士，已死，忽逢之，曰：“闻 逐兔得书，吾识其字。”乃出示之。韦云：“为胡秀才取尔。”遂失不见。裴亦 寻卒。

    143

    A Fox Reciting the Tongtian Jing

    Péi Zhongyuan lived in the northern part of Huxian, and one day, while chasing a rabbit into a large tomb, he saw a fox sitting on a coffin and reading. Zhongyuan tried to catch the fox but failed, and instead, he took the book home. The characters on the book were unreadable. Suddenly, a scholar of the Hu ethnicity appeared and asked to be seen. He introduced himself as Xingzhou, the same fox who had been reading the book on the coffin. Péi asked, "What book is this?" The scholar replied, "It is the Tongtian Jing, a text not studied by ordinary people. You truly have no use for it, but I wish to offer a hundred gold pieces to redeem it." Péi refused. The scholar then offered a thousand yì (an ancient unit of weight for gold or silver), but Péi still refused. Angered, the scholar waved his robe and rose to leave. Péi’s brother-in-law, Wei Danshi, who had passed away, suddenly appeared and said, "I heard you caught a rabbit and found a book. I can recognize its characters." He then showed the book to Péi. Wei said, "It belongs to the scholar Xingzhou." He then vanished and was no longer seen. Péi also died shortly after.
